<h2 id='tocuniq2'>Prologue</h2>

The Commentaries on the Gospel of Matthew by Saint Jerome of Stridon, a Presbyter. Four Books addressed to Eusebius.

There were indeed many who attempted to arrange the narrative of the things that have been fulfilled among us, just as those who were eyewitnesses from the beginning and ministers of the word handed them down to us. And up to the present time, the persistence of these accounts demonstrates that diverse authors have produced the beginnings of various heresies, such as that of the Egyptians, Thomas, Matthew, Bartholomew, and the twelve apostles, as well as Basilides, Appelles, and others, whom it would be too lengthy to enumerate. However, it is necessary to say at present that there have been some who, without the spirit and grace of God, have attempted to arrange the narrative more than to weave the truth of history. To whom can that prophecy be applied? Woe to those who prophesy from their own heart, who follow their own spirit and have said, 'This is what the Lord says,' when the Lord has not sent them (Ezekiel 13:3). The Savior also spoke about them in the Gospel of John: All who came before me were thieves and robbers (John 10:8). They came on their own, not sent by God. For he himself says, 'They were coming to me, but I did not send them' (Jeremiah 14:14; and 23:21). To those who come, presumption is rashness; to those who are sent, obedience is servitude. But the Church, which is founded upon the rock of the Lord's voice, which the king introduced into his chamber (Song of Songs, 1 and 2), and to which he reached out his hand through the hidden opening (Song of Songs, 5), is like a damsel and a little deer (Song of Songs, 2:9), pouring forth four rivers like the paradise (Genesis 2), and having four corners and rings, through which, like the Ark of the Covenant and the guardian of the Law of the Lord, it is carried on immovable wood (Exodus 25:10ff).


Matthew, a tax collector by the name of Levi, is the first of all, who published the Gospel in Judea in the Hebrew language, for the sake of those who had believed in Jesus from the Jews, and did not keep the shadow of the Law once the truth of the Gospel succeeded. Mark is the second, the interpreter of the Apostle Peter, and the first bishop of the Church in Alexandria. He himself did not see the Lord and Savior, but narrated the things he heard the teacher preach, not in chronological order but according to the faith of the deeds. Tertius Lucas, a physician from Antioch, Syria (whose praise is in the Gospel), who himself was a disciple of the Apostle Paul, wrote a volume in the regions of Achaia and Boeotia (2 Corinthians VIII), delving deeper into some matters and, as he confesses in the preface, describing things he heard more than things he saw. The last Apostle and Evangelist, John, whom Jesus loved greatly, who reclined on the Lord's chest (John XIII and XXI), drank from the pure streams of teachings and was the only one who deserved to hear from the cross: Behold your mother (John XIX, 27)." } When he was in Asia, and now when the seeds of heretics were sprouting, Cerinthus, Ebion, and the others who deny that Christ came in the flesh (whom he himself calls antichrists in his letter (1 John 2:18), and the apostle Paul frequently rebukes (Romans 3; 2 Corinthians 5)), he was compelled by almost all the bishops of Asia at that time, and by delegations from many Churches, to write more deeply about the divinity of the Savior and to burst forth, not so much audaciously as luckily, to the very Word of God Himself, as it were. And the Ecclesiastica history recounts that when he was asked by the brothers to write, he responded that he would do so if they all prayed to God in common after a fast was declared. And when this was done and he was filled with divine revelation, he burst forth upon coming to that introduction with these words: 'In the beginning was the Word, and the Word was with God, and the Word was God' (John 1). These four Gospels, therefore, are proven by the book of Ezekiel, in which the first vision is described as follows: 'In the midst of the likeness of the four living creatures, their faces were like those of men, and the face of a lion, and the face of a calf, and the face of an eagle' (Ezekiel 1:5 and 10). The first appearance of man signifies Matthew, who began to write as it were about a man: The book of the generation of Jesus Christ, the son of David, the son of Abraham (Matthew 1). The second signifies Mark, in which the voice of a roaring lion is heard: The voice of one crying in the wilderness, Prepare the way of the Lord, make his paths straight (Mark 1:3). The third signifies the calf, which foreshadows the beginning that the evangelist Luke took from the priest Zacharias. In the fourth (Gospel), John the evangelist, who had eagle's wings and was hastening to higher things, discusses the Word of God. The other things which follow in the same sense advance. Their legs were straight, and they had feathered feet, and wherever the spirit went, they went, and did not turn back. And their backs were full of eyes, and sparks and lamps were running in their midst, and wheel within wheel, and in each of the four faces. Hence the Revelation of John, after the exposition of the twenty-four elders who were holding harps and bowls, worshiped (or adore) the Lamb of God. It introduces flashes of lightning and thunder, and seven spirits running, and a glassy sea, and four living creatures full of eyes (Rev. IV and V), saying: The first creature was like a lion, and the second creature was like a calf, and the third creature had a face like a man, and the fourth creature was like a flying eagle. And after a little while: Their eyes were full and had no rest day and night, saying: Holy, Holy, Holy, Lord God Almighty, who was, and is, and is to come (Apoc. IV, 7, 8). It is clearly shown to all that only the four Gospels should be accepted, and all the nonsense of the apocrypha should be sung to the dead heretics rather than the living Church. And I am amazed, dearest Eusebius, why, suddenly sailing to Rome, you wanted me to give you this book as a gift, so that I could briefly explain Matthew, summarize it in words, and expand on its meaning. If you remember my response, you would never ask for a matter of years in a few days. Firstly, it is difficult to read all those who have written on the Gospels 7-8. Secondly, it is much more difficult, with critical judgment, to accept what is best. I admit that I read many years ago the twenty-five volumes of Origen on Matthew, as well as his Homilies, and the comical genre of interpretation; and the Commentaries of Theophilus, Bishop of the city of Antioch; also those of Hippolytus, Theodore of Heraclea, Apollinaris of Laodicea, and Didymus of Alexandria; and of the Latins, the writings of Hilary, Victorinus, and Fortunatianus, among which even if I were to carp at something small, something worthy would be written in memory. But you, in these two weeks, with Easter approaching and the winds blowing, force me to dictate, so that when the notaries take note, when the documents are written, when they are corrected, how they are arranged to be clean, especially since you know that I have been ill for three months, so that I can barely start walking now; and I cannot compensate for the extent of the work with the brevity of time. Therefore, disregarding the authority of the Ancients, whom I have neither the opportunity to read nor to follow, I have briefly arranged the historical interpretation that you especially demanded: and at times I have mixed in flowers of spiritual insight, reserving the complete work for the future. But if my life is prolonged, or if you fulfill your promises upon your return, then I will strive to complete what remains, nay, I will lay the foundations and partly construct the walls, and place a most beautiful finishing touch, so that you may know the difference between sudden boldness in speaking and studious diligence in writing. Surely you know, and I would be ashamed to call you a witness to my falsehood, that I have dictated this little work with such speed that you might think I write more readily what others have written than what I have composed myself. And do not think that this is said out of arrogance and confidence in my own intelligence, but rather because I desire to show you how highly I regard you. I would rather risk being criticized by the learned than deny anything to you, who diligently ask for something. Therefore, I beg you to attribute any clumsiness in my speech or any deviation from the usual style to haste rather than lack of skill, and provide copies when you come to Rome, to the Virgin Princess of Christ, who asked me to write a Commentary on the Song of Songs. Due to a long illness, I have postponed this work for the future. And under this condition, I bind you, so that if you keep the letters I wrote to you, she should also keep the letters that she will write to her own little chest afterwards.


<h2 id='tocuniq3'>First Book</h2>

First Book

<h2 id='tocuniq4'>9 (Caput I.—Vers. 1.)</h2>

9 (Chapter 1, Verse 1) The book of the generation of Jesus Christ. In Isaiah we read: Who shall declare his generation? (Isaiah 53:8). Therefore, we should not think that the Evangelist contradicts the prophet, so that what he said was impossible, he begins to narrate here, because there it was said about the generation of divinity, here it is said about the incarnation. But he begins with the carnal, so that we may begin to say that God is also man.

The sons of David, the sons of Abraham. Abraham begot Isaac. Isaac, however, begot Jacob. Jacob, however, begot Judah and his brothers. The order is reversed, but necessarily altered. For if Abraham had been placed first, and then David, Abraham would have needed to be repeated in order to complete the series of generations. Therefore, leaving aside the others, he called them his sons because the promise of Christ was made only to them, to Abraham: 'In your seed, all nations will be blessed' (Gen. XXII, 18), which is Christ. To David: Of the fruit of your womb I will set upon your throne. (Ps. 131:11)

<h2 id='tocuniq5'>(Vers. 3.)</h2>

(Verse 3.) But Judas begot Phares and Zaram from Thamar. Phares begot Esron. Esron begot Aram. Aram begot Aminadab. Aminadab begot Naasson. It should be noted in the genealogy of the Savior that no holy women are included, but rather those whom Scripture reproves, for he came for sinners, being born of sinners, to erase the sins of all. Therefore, in the following genealogy, Ruth the Moabite and Bathsheba, the wife of Uriah, are mentioned.


<h2 id='tocuniq6'>(Vers. 4 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 4 and following) Naasson begot Salmon. Salmon begot Boaz from Rahab. Boaz begot Obed from Ruth. Obed begot Jesse. Jesse begot King David. David begot Solomon from the woman who had been Uriah's wife. Solomon begot Rehoboam. Rehoboam begot Abijah. Abijah begot Asa. Asa begot Jehoshaphat. Jehoshaphat begot Joram. This is Naasson, the chief of the tribe of Judah, as we read in the Book of Numbers (Num. 1 and 2).


But Joram begot Oziam. Ozias begot Joathan. Joathan begot Achaz. Achaz begot Ezechiam. Ezechias begot Manassen. Manasses begot Amon. Amon begot Josiam. Josias begot Jechoniam and his brothers in the Babylonian exile. In the fourth book of Kings (Chapters III, VIII and following) we read that Joram was begotten by Ochoziam, and when he died, Josabeth, daughter of King Joram and sister of Ochozia, took Joas, the son of her brother, and rescued him from the death inflicted by Athaliah. His son Amaziah succeeded him as king, followed by his son Azariah, also known as Uzziah (or Ahaziah). His son Jotham succeeded him. You see, according to historical records, there were three kings in between, whom the Evangelist omitted: Jehoram did not father Uzziah, but Ahaziah, and the others we listed. However, because the purpose of the Evangelist was to present the three fourteens in different periods of time, and Jehoram had mixed in with the wicked Jezebel, his memory is erased up to the third generation, so it would not be included in the order of the Holy Nativity.


<h2 id='tocuniq7'>(Vers. 12 seqq.)</h2>

(v. 12 ff.) And after the exile to Babylon, Jechoniah fathered Salathiel. Salathiel fathered Zerubbabel. Zerubbabel fathered Abiud. Abiud fathered Eliakim. Eliakim fathered Azor. Azor fathered Sadoc. Sadoc fathered Achim. Achim fathered Eliud. Eliud fathered Eleazar. Eleazar fathered Matthan. Matthan fathered Jacob. If we include Jechoniah at the end of the first fourteen generations, in the next there will not be fourteen, but thirteen. Therefore, let us know that Jechoniah is the same as Joacim: the former is written with 'c' and 'm', while the latter is written with 'ch' and 'n', which has been confused by the error of scribes and the passage of time among the Greeks and the Latins.

<h2 id='tocuniq8'>(Vers. 16.)</h2>

(Verse 16) But Jacob fathered Joseph. Julianus Augustus objects to us at this point the discordance of the Evangelists, why the evangelist Matthew said that Joseph is the son of Jacob, and Luke called him the son of Heli, not understanding the custom of the Scriptures, that one according to nature, the other according to the Law is his father. For we know this through Moses, by God's command, as a precept, that if a brother or relative without children dies, another should take his wife to raise up offspring for his brother or relative (Deuteronomy 25). Both Africanus, a historian of his time, and Eusebius of Caesarea extensively discussed the discrepancies in the Gospels in their books.

<h2 id='tocuniq9'>(Vers 17.)</h2>

(Verse 17.) The husband of Mary, from whom was born Jesus, who is called Christ. When you hear the word 'husband,' do not suspect anything about marriage, but remember the custom of the Scriptures, that husbands are called spouses, and wives are called wives.

<h2 id='tocuniq10'>(Vers. 18.)</h2>

(Ver. 18.) And from the deportation to Babylon to Christ, there are fourteen generations. Count from Jechoniah to Joseph, and you will find thirteen generations. Therefore, the fourteenth generation will be considered as Christ himself.

But the generation of Christ was like this. Let the diligent reader ask and say: Since Joseph is not the father of the Lord and Savior, what does the order of the generation have to do with Joseph? To this we will respond first, that it is not the custom of the Scriptures to trace the order of women in generations. Then, Joseph and Mary were from the same tribe: hence, according to the Law, she had to be regarded as a close relative, and that they were both registered in Bethlehem, being generated from the same lineage.


When his mother Mary was betrothed to Joseph, why was she conceived not by a simple Virgin, but by a betrothed one? First, so that through the genealogy, Joseph's origin would be shown as Mary's. Second, so that she would not be stoned by the Jews as an adulteress. Third, so that, fleeing into Egypt, she would have the comfort of a husband. The martyr Ignatius also added a fourth reason why she was conceived by a betrothed one: so that the birth, he says, could be hidden from the devil, who thought that He was born not of a Virgin, but of a wife.


Before they came together, she was found to be pregnant through the Holy Spirit. She was found to be pregnant by Joseph, who knew everything about his future wife through nearly marital consent. However, what is said, Before they came together, does not imply that they later came together; but Scripture shows that it did not happen.

<h2 id='tocuniq11'>(Vers. 19.)</h2>

(Verse 19) But Joseph, her husband, being a just man and unwilling to put her to shame, resolved to divorce her quietly. As he considered this, behold, an angel of the Lord appeared to him in a dream, saying, “Joseph, son of David, do not fear to take Mary as your wife, for that which is conceived in her is from the Holy Spirit. She will bear a son, and you shall call his name Jesus, for he will save his people from their sins.” All this took place to fulfill what the Lord had spoken by the prophet: “Behold, the virgin shall conceive and bear a son, and they shall call his name Immanuel” (which means, God with us). When Joseph woke from sleep, he did as the angel of the Lord commanded him: he took his wife, but knew her not until she had given birth to a son. And he called his name Jesus.


<h2 id='tocuniq12'>(Vers. 20.)</h2>

(Verse 20) Joseph, son of David, do not be afraid to take Mary as your wife. For what is conceived in her is from the Holy Spirit. She will give birth to a son. And as we have said before, the word 'spouse' is used for wives, which is more fully taught against Helvidius. And with a gentle affection, an Angel speaks to him in a dream to confirm the righteousness of silence. At the same time, it should be noted that Joseph is said to be the son of David, so that Mary would also be shown to be from the line of David.


<h2 id='tocuniq13'>(Vers. 21.)</h2>

(Verse 21) And you shall call his name Jesus. For he will save his people from their sins. Jesus, in the Hebrew language, means Savior. Therefore, the evangelist indicated the etymology of his name, saying: You shall call his name Jesus, for he will save his people.

<h2 id='tocuniq14'>(Vers. 22 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 22 and following) But all this was done, that it might be fulfilled which was spoken by the Lord through the prophet, saying: Behold, a virgin shall be with child, and shall bring forth a son, and they shall call his name Emmanuel, which being interpreted is, God with us. Then Joseph, being raised from sleep, did as the angel of the Lord had bidden him. And Matthew the evangelist says, she shall be with child, which was written by the prophet, she shall conceive. But the prophet, because he predicts the future, signifies what will happen, and he writes, he will receive: but the evangelist, because he narrates a past history, not a future event, changed 'will receive' to 'has received', and put 'will have'. For he who has, will by no means receive. We read something similar in the Psalms: "Ascending on high, he led captivity captive: he received gifts among men" (Ps. 68:18). When the apostle cited this testimony, he did not say 'received', but 'gave', because there it signified a future event that he would receive; here it narrates the history of the one who had already given what he had received.


<h2 id='tocuniq15'>(Vers. 25.)</h2>

(Verse 25.) And he took his wife, and he did not know her until she gave birth to her firstborn son; and he called his name Jesus. From this passage, some wickedly suspect and claim that Mary had other children, saying that firstborn is not said unless one has brothers: whereas this is the custom of the divine Scriptures, that they do not call the firstborn him whom 14 brothers follow, but him who is born first. Read the aforementioned book against Helvidius.


<h2 id='tocuniq16'>(Chap. II.—Vers. 2 seqq.)</h2>

(Chapter 2 — Verses 2 and following) For we have seen his star in the East, and have come to worship him. When King Herod heard this, he was troubled, and all Jerusalem with him. And he gathered together all the chief priests and scribes of the people, and inquired of them where Christ would be born. To confuse the Jews, so that they might learn of the birth of Christ from the Gentiles, a star rises in the East, which the successors of Balaam, who were familiar with his prophecy, had known would happen. Read the Book of Numbers (Chapter XXIV). Now the wise men were led by the stars to Judea, so that when the priests were asked by the wise men where Christ would be born, they would be without excuse concerning His coming.

<h2 id='tocuniq17'>(Vers. 5.)</h2>

(Verse 5.) But they said to him: in Bethlehem of Judea. For thus it is written by the prophet: And you, Bethlehem, land of Judah, are by no means least among the leaders of Judah. For from you shall come forth a ruler who will shepherd my people Israel. This is an error of the scribes. For we think it was first written by the evangelist, as we read in the Hebrew itself, Judah, not Judea. For what is the Bethlehem of other nations, that here it should be distinguished as Bethlehem of Judea? But it is written 'Judae' because there is another Bethlehem in Galilee. Read the book of Joshua, the son of Nun (Joshua 19). Finally, even in the very testimony, which is taken from the prophecy of Micah, it is thus stated: And you, Bethlehem, land of Judah (Micah 5:2).

<h2 id='tocuniq18'>(Vers. 11.)</h2>

(Verse 11.) And opening their treasures, they offered him gifts, gold, frankincense, and myrrh. The sacrament of the most beautiful gifts is captured by Juvencus the priest in one verse:

Thus, they bring gifts of gold, myrrh, and frankincense to the king, the people, and to God.

And having received a response in a dream, they did not return to Herod, but went back to their own country by another route, etc. Those who had offered gifts to the Lord subsequently receive a response. However, the response (which in Greek is called χρηματισθέντες) is not made through an angel, but through the Lord himself, in order to demonstrate the merit of Joseph. They return by another route, because they were not inclined to join in the unfaithfulness of the Jews.


<h2 id='tocuniq19'>(Vers. 13, 14.)</h2>

(Verses 13, 14) Behold, an angel of the Lord appeared to Joseph in a dream, saying: Get up and take the child and his mother, and flee to Egypt, and stay there until I tell you. For it will happen that Herod will seek the child to destroy him. So Joseph got up, took the child and his mother at night, and went to Egypt; and he stayed there until the death of Herod. When he takes the child and his mother to go to Egypt, he does so at night and in darkness; but when he returns to Judea, neither night nor darkness is mentioned in the Gospel.


<h2 id='tocuniq20'>(Vers. 15, 16.)</h2>

(Vers. 15, 16.) So that what was spoken by the Lord through the prophet might be fulfilled, saying: Out of Egypt I called my son. Then Herod, seeing that he had been fooled by the wise men, became very angry; and sending, he killed all the boys who were in Bethlehem, and in all its territories, from two years old and under, according to the time that he had diligently inquired from the wise men. Let those who deny the truth of the Hebrew scriptures answer where this is read in the Septuagint translators. But when they do not find it, we will tell them that it is written in the prophet Hosea (Chap. 11), as they can also prove from the copies we have recently published. However, we can reconcile ((or console)) this passage differently for the contentious, whose behavior the Apostle Paul denies having. We also bring forward the testimony from Numbers, with Balaam saying: God has called him out of Egypt; his glory is like that of a wild ox (Num. XXIII, 22).


<h2 id='tocuniq21'>(Vers. 17 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 17 and following) Then was fulfilled what was spoken by the prophet Jeremiah, saying: A voice was heard in Ramah, lamentation, weeping, and great mourning, Rachel weeping for her children, and would not be comforted, because they are not (Jeremiah 31:15). But when Herod was dead, behold, an angel of the Lord appeared in a dream to Joseph in Egypt, saying: Arise, and take the young child and his mother, and go into the land of Israel. Out of Rachel was born Benjamin, in whose tribe Bethlehem is not (Genesis 35). So the question is, how does Rachel weep for the sons of Judah, that is, Bethlehem, as if they were her own? We will answer briefly, because she is buried near Bethlehem in Ephrath, and she received her name from her mother's lodging place. Either because Judah and Benjamin were two joined tribes, and Herod had ordered not only the killing of the children in Bethlehem, but also in all its borders. By the killing of Bethlehem, we mean that many of Benjamin were also killed. But he weeps for his sons, and does not receive consolation, according to a twofold understanding. Either because he considered them to be dead forever, or because he did not want to be comforted concerning those whom he knew would survive. And what is said in Rama, let us not think that the name of the place is, near Gabaa, but Rama is interpreted as elevated, so that the sense may be: A voice was heard on high, that is, widely and far and wide.

<h2 id='tocuniq22'>(Vers. 20.)</h2>

(Verse 20.) For those who sought the life of the child are dead. From this passage we understand that not only Herod, but also the priests and scribes at the same time had planned the death of the Lord.

<h2 id='tocuniq23'>(Vers. 21.)</h2>

(Verse 21) He arose and took the child and his mother, and came into the land of Israel. He did not say, 'I took my son and my wife,' but the child and his mother, as if a caregiver, not a husband.

<h2 id='tocuniq24'>(Vers. 22.)</h2>

(Verse 22.) But hearing that Archelaus reigned in Judea, in place of his father Herod, he was afraid to go there. And having been warned in a dream, he withdrew to the region of Galilee. Many fall into error due to ignorance of history, thinking that he is the same Herod who is mocked by the Lord in his passion and who is now reported to be dead. Therefore, this Herod, who later made friends with Pilate, is the son of that Herod and the brother of Archelaus. And Tiberius Caesar himself exiled both him and his brother Herod, who became the successor of the kingdom, to Lugdunum, which is a city of the Gauls. Read the story of Joseph.

<h2 id='tocuniq25'>(Vers. 23.)</h2>

(Verse 23.) And he came and lived in a city called Nazareth, that what was spoken by the prophets might be fulfilled: 'He shall be called a Nazarene.' If he had set an example from the Scriptures, he would never have said, 'what was spoken by the prophets,' but simply, 'what was spoken by the prophet.' But now, from using the plural 'prophets,' he shows that he did not take his words from the Scriptures, but the meaning. Nazarene, saint, is interpreted. However, all of Scripture testifies that the Lord will become holy. We can also say in another way, that in the same words, according to the Hebrew truth, it is written in Isaiah: A twig will come out from the root of Jesse, and a Nazarene will ascend from his root (Isaiah 11:1).

<h2 id='tocuniq26'>(Chap. III.—Vers. 1.)</h2>

(Chapter III—Verse 1) Repent: for the kingdom of heaven is at hand. John the Baptist proclaims the kingdom of heaven first, so that he may be honored as the precursor of the Lord with this privilege.

<h2 id='tocuniq27'>(Vers. 3.)</h2>

(Verse 3.) For this is he who is spoken of through the prophet Isaiah, saying: 'The voice of one crying out in the desert, prepare the way of the Lord, make straight his paths.' He prepared the souls of the believers in which the Lord would walk, so that he would walk in the purest ways, saying: 'I will dwell in them and walk among them; I will be their God, and they shall be my people' (Leviticus 26:12). Porphyry compares this passage to the beginning of the Gospel of Mark, where it is written: 'The beginning of the Gospel of Jesus Christ, the Son of God, as it is written in the prophet Isaiah: Behold, I am sending my messenger ahead of you, who will prepare your way.'" } The voice of one crying in the wilderness: Prepare the way of the Lord, make straight his paths. (Isaiah 40:3). For even though the testimony is from Malachi (Chapter 3) and the context is from Isaiah, they ask how we can consider it as an example taken from one Isaiah. To this, the learned men of the Church have answered fully. However, we think that the name of Isaiah was added due to an error of the scribes, which we can also prove in other places, or certainly that one body has been made from various testimonies of the Scriptures. Read the thirteenth Psalm, and you will find the same.

<h2 id='tocuniq28'>(Vers. 4.)</h2>

(Verse 4.) Now John himself had a garment made of camel's hair and a leather belt around his waist. He said he had clothing made of hair, not wool. The type of clothing he wore indicated austerity, not luxury. The leather belt that he was girded with, like Elijah, is a symbol of mortification (IV Kings 1). Furthermore, what follows is...

But his food was locusts and wild honey. It is fitting for a dweller of solitude to fill not the delights of food, but the necessity of human flesh.

<h2 id='tocuniq29'>(Vers. 9.)</h2>

(Verse 9) God is able to raise up children of Abraham from these stones. He calls them heathen stones because of their hardness of heart. Read Ezekiel: 'I will remove your heart of stone and give you a heart of flesh' (Ezekiel 36:26). In the stone, hardness is shown; in the flesh, softness is shown. It either simply indicates God's power, that he who created all things out of nothing can also bring forth a people from the hardest stones.


<h2 id='tocuniq30'>(Vers. 10, 11.)</h2>

(Verses 10, 11.) For now the axe is laid to the root of the trees. Every tree therefore that does not bear good fruit will be cut down and thrown into the fire. I indeed baptize you with water for repentance; but he who is coming after me is mightier than I. The preaching of the Gospel, which is sharp on both sides, is called an axe, according to the prophet Jeremiah, who compares the word of the Lord to a cutting axe splitting the rock (Jeremiah 46).


Whose sandals I am not worthy to carry. In another Gospel: Whose, he says, I am not worthy to untie the strap of his sandal: here humility is demonstrated, there mystery is shown, that Christ is the bridegroom, and John does not deserve to untie the strap of the bridegroom, lest his house be called according to the law of Moses, and the example of Ruth, the house of the barefoot (Deut. XXV, and Ruth. IV).

<h2 id='tocuniq31'>(Vers. 12.)</h2>

(Verse 12.) He will baptize you with the Holy Spirit and fire. His winnowing fork is in his hand, and he will thoroughly cleanse his threshing floor. He will gather the wheat into his barn, but he will burn the chaff with unquenchable fire. This is because the Holy Spirit is like a fire, as the Acts of the Apostles teach, when it descended and appeared like tongues of fire over each of the believers (Acts 2). And the word of the Lord was fulfilled when he said, 'I have come to bring fire to the earth, and how I wish it were already kindled!' (Luke 12:49)." } Whether because in the present we are baptized in the Spirit, and in the future, by fire. The Apostle also agrees with this idea, saying: The work of each one will be revealed by fire, what sort it is. (1 Corinthians 3:13).

<h2 id='tocuniq32'>(Vers. 13, 14.)</h2>

(Verse 13, 14.) Then Jesus came from Galilee to the Jordan to John, to be baptized by him. But John tried to prevent him, saying: I should be baptized by you, and yet you come to me? But Jesus answered and said to him. The Savior received baptism from John for three reasons. First, because he was born as a man, to fulfill all the righteousness and humility of the Law. Second, to confirm John's baptism with his own baptism. Thirdly, as Jordan sanctifies the waters by the descent of the dove, may the Holy Spirit in the baptismal font reveal His coming to the believers.

<h2 id='tocuniq33'>(Vers. 15.)</h2>

(Verse 15) Without hesitation. He spoke beautifully, without hesitation, to demonstrate Christ in the water, John to be baptized by Christ in the Spirit. Or in another way, without hesitation: so that as one who took on the form of a servant, I may also fulfill his humility. Otherwise, know that you must be baptized by me on the day of judgment. Without hesitation, says the Lord Jesus, I have another baptism by which I must be baptized. You baptize me in water, so that I may baptize you on behalf of me in your blood.


<h2 id='tocuniq34'>(Vers. 16.)</h2>

(Verse 16.) For it is fitting for us to fulfill all righteousness. Then he let him go. And when Jesus was baptized, he immediately came up from the water. He did not add the righteousness of the Law or of nature, so that we may understand both: that if God received baptism from a man, no one should disdain to receive it from a servant.

<h2 id='tocuniq35'>(Vers. 17.)</h2>

(Verse 17) And behold, the heavens were opened to him, and he saw the Spirit of God descending like a dove and coming upon him. And behold, a voice from heaven said, 'This is my beloved Son, with whom I am well pleased.' The mystery of the Trinity is demonstrated in baptism: the Lord is baptized, the Spirit descends in the form of a dove, and the voice of the Father, bearing witness to the Son, is heard. The heavens are opened not by the unlocking of physical elements, but by spiritual eyes; as Ezekiel also states at the beginning of his book. And a dove also sat upon the head of Jesus, so that no one would think that the voice of the Father was directed to John and not to the Lord.

<h2 id='tocuniq36'>(Chap. IV.—Vers. 1.)</h2>

(Chapter IV - Verse 1) Then Jesus was led into the desert by the spirit. There is no doubt that it was by the Holy Spirit. For it follows:

In order to be tempted by the devil. However, he is led not unwillingly or captured, but by the will to fight.

<h2 id='tocuniq37'>20 (Vers. 2.)</h2>

20 (V. 2.) And when he had fasted forty days and forty nights, afterward he was hungry. And the tempter came and said to him, If you are the Son of God. In this number of the forty days, the sacrament is shown to us, in which both Moses fasted on Mount Sinai (Exod. 24), and Elijah beside Mount Horeb (1 Kings 19). However, it is allowed for the body to hunger, so that there may be an opportunity for the devil to tempt.

<h2 id='tocuniq38'>(Vers. 3.)</h2>

(Verse 3.) Say that these stones be made bread. It is fittingly said to the hungry: say that these stones be made bread: you tempt him with two opposing things, O devil. If these stones can be made bread at his command, then you are trying in vain the one who has such great power. But if he cannot do it, then you wrongly suspect the Son of God. If you are the Son of God, say that these stones be made bread.

<h2 id='tocuniq39'>(Vers. 4.)</h2>

(Verse 4.) And he answered, saying: It is written: Man does not live by bread alone, but by every word that proceeds from the mouth of God. The testimony is taken from Deuteronomy (Deut. VIII, 3). The Lord responded in this way because his purpose was to overcome the devil through humility, not power. It should also be noted that unless the Lord had begun to fast, there would not have been an opportunity for the devil to tempt him, according to the saying: Son, when you come to serve God, stand in righteousness and fear, and prepare your soul for temptation (Ecclus. II, 1)." } But the response of the Savior itself indicates that he was a man who was tempted. Man does not live by bread alone, but by every word that proceeds from the mouth of God. Therefore, if anyone does not feed on the word of God, they do not live.

<h2 id='tocuniq40'>(Vers. 5.)</h2>

(Verse 5) Then the devil took him to the holy city. This assumption, which is spoken of, did not come from the weakness of the Lord, but from the pride of the enemy, who considers the will of the Savior as a necessity. It is understood from this place what that which is written in another place means: They went into the holy city and appeared to many (Matthew 27:53).

<h2 id='tocuniq41'>(Vers. 6.)</h2>

(Verse 6) And he set him upon the pinnacle of the temple, and said to him, 'If you are the Son of God, throw yourself down, for it is written, 'He will command his angels concerning you,' and 'On their hands they will bear you up, so that you will not strike your foot against a stone.'

If you are the Son of God. In all temptations the devil does this, to understand if you are the Son of God; but the Lord tempers the answer in such a way as to leave him ambiguous.

Send yourself downward. For it is written. The voice of the devil, who always desires all to fall downward, says, Send yourself downward, he can persuade, he cannot compel to fall.

He has commanded his angels concerning you, that they shall lift you up in their hands, lest you strike your foot against a stone. We read this in the ninety-first psalm; but there it is not about Christ, but about a holy man. Therefore, the devil misinterprets the Scriptures. Certainly, if he truly knew that it was written about the Savior, he should have also said what follows against himself in the same psalm: You will tread on the viper and the basilisk, and you will trample the lion and the dragon. He speaks of the help of angels as if to an infirm person: he is silent about his own trampling as if a deserter.

<h2 id='tocuniq42'>(Vers. 7.)</h2>

(Verse 7) Jesus said to him again: It is written: You shall not tempt the Lord your God. He breaks the false arrows of the devil with the true shields of the Scriptures. And it should be noted that he brought forth necessary testimonies only from Deuteronomy, in order to demonstrate the sacraments of the second law.

<h2 id='tocuniq43'>(Vers. 8.)</h2>

(Verse 8) Again, the devil took him to a very high mountain and showed him all the kingdoms of the world and their glory, and he said to him, 'All these I will give you, if you will fall down and worship me.' The glory of the world, which is passing away with the world, is shown on the mountain and on the pinnacle. But the Lord descends to lowly and humble places to overcome the devil with humility. Furthermore, the devil hastens to lead him to mountains, so that through the mountains by which he himself fell, others may also fall, according to the saying of the Apostle: 'lest he become conceited and fall into the condemnation of the devil' (1 Timothy 3:6)." }


<h2 id='tocuniq44'>(Vers. 9.)</h2>

(Verse 9) I will give you all this, if you fall down and worship me. This arrogant and proud one also speaks of this boastfully: not that the devil has power over the whole world or can give all kingdoms, since we know that many holy men have been made kings by God. If you fall down and worship me, he says. Therefore, the one who is going to worship the devil falls down beforehand.

<h2 id='tocuniq45'>(Vers. 10.)</h2>

(Verse 10) Then Jesus said to him, 'Go away, Satan! For it is written: Not as many suppose, Satan and the apostle Peter are condemned with the same opinion. For it is said to Peter: Get behind me, Satan (Mat. XVI, 23), that is, follow me, who are contrary to my will. But here he hears, go away, Satan, and it is not said to him, behind me, so that it may be understood, go into the eternal fire, which is prepared for you and your angels.'


You shall worship the Lord your God and serve only Him. The devil said to the Savior: if you fall down and worship me, on the contrary, it is heard that he himself should worship the Lord his God more.

<h2 id='tocuniq46'>(Vers. 11.)</h2>

(Verse 11) Then the devil left him: and behold, angels came and ministered to him. Temptation precedes victory for it to be followed. Angels minister to confirm the dignity of the victor.

<h2 id='tocuniq47'>(Vers. 15, 16.)</h2>

(Verse 15, 16.) The land of Zebulun and the land of Naphtali, by the way of the sea, beyond the Jordan, Galilee of the Gentiles: The people who walked in darkness have seen a great light; those who dwelt in the land of the shadow of death, upon them a light has shined. These are the first ones who heard the Lord preaching, that where the Israelites were first taken captive by the Assyrians, there the proclamation of the Redeemer would be born.

<h2 id='tocuniq48'>(Vers. 17, 18.)</h2>

(Vers. 17, 18.) Then Jesus began to preach and say: Repent, for the kingdom of heaven is at hand. And walking by the sea of Galilee, Jesus saw two brothers, Simon called Peter, and Andrew his brother, casting a net into the sea: for they were fishermen. And he said to them. With John delivered, he rightly begins to preach: with the Law ending, the Gospel consequently arises. But if the Savior preaches the same things that John the Baptist had previously foretold, he shows himself to be the Son of the same God, of whom that prophet is.


<h2 id='tocuniq49'>(Vers. 19, 20.)</h2>

(Verse 19, 20.) Come after me, and I will make you fishers of men. And immediately they left their nets and followed him. These were the first called, to follow the Lord: fishermen and illiterate were sent to preach, so that the faith of believers would not be thought to come about by the power of God, but by eloquence and teaching.

<h2 id='tocuniq50'>(Vers. 24.)</h2>

(Verse 24.) And he cured the lunatics and the paralyzed. And many crowds followed him from Galilee and the Decapolis, and from Jerusalem, and from Judea, and from beyond the Jordan. Not truly lunatics, but those who were thought to be lunatics due to the deception of demons, who, by observing the movements of the moon, wished to defame the creation so that they might overflow with blasphemies against the Creator.

<h2 id='tocuniq51'>(Chap. V.—Vers. 1, 2.)</h2>

(Chapter 5, Verses 1-2.) But seeing the crowds, Jesus went up on the mountain, and when he sat down, his disciples came to him. And opening his mouth, he taught them, saying: The Lord goes up to the mountains, so that the crowds may be drawn to higher things with him. But the crowds are not able to ascend. And the disciples follow, to whom he speaks not standing, but sitting and gathered. For they were not able to understand him shining in his majesty. According to the literal meaning, some of the simpler brothers think that he taught the Beatitudes and the rest of what follows on the Mount of Olives, which is by no means the case: for from what precedes and follows, the place is shown to be in Galilee, which we believe to be either Mount Tabor or any other lofty mountain. Finally, after he finished his discourse, immediately it follows: And when he had entered Capernaum.

<h2 id='tocuniq52'>(Vers. 3.)</h2>

(Verse 3.) Blessed are the poor in spirit, for theirs is the kingdom of heaven. This is what we read elsewhere: And the humble in spirit he will save (Ps. 33:16): But lest anyone should think that poverty, which is sometimes borne out of necessity, is being preached by the Lord, he added in spirit, so that you would understand that it is humility, not destitution. Blessed are the poor in spirit, who are poor by their own will for the sake of the Holy Spirit. Hence, concerning such poor, the Savior speaks through Isaiah: The Lord has anointed me; therefore he has sent me to preach good news to the poor (Isa. 61:1)." }


<h2 id='tocuniq53'>(Vers. 4.)</h2>

(Verse 4) Blessed are the meek, for they themselves shall inherit the earth. Not the land of Judah, nor the land of this world; not the accursed land that brings forth thorns and thistles, which the most cruel and warlike possess more; but the land that the Psalmist desires, saying: I believe to see the good things of the Lord in the land of the living. Such a possessor, and after victory, a triumphator, is also described in the forty-fourth psalm: Attend, proceed and reign prosperously: because of truth, meekness, and justice. No one possesses this land by gentleness, but by arrogance.

<h2 id='tocuniq54'>(Vers. 5.)</h2>

(Verse 5) Blessed are those who mourn, for they shall be comforted. This mourning is not for the dead, according to the common law of nature, but for the sins and vices of the dead. Thus, Samuel wept for Saul because he regretted that God had anointed him king over Israel (1 Samuel 15). So too, the apostle Paul says that he weeps and mourns for those who have not repented after committing fornication and impurity (2 Corinthians 12).

<h2 id='tocuniq55'>24 (Vers. 6.)</h2>

24 (Verse 6.) Blessed are those who hunger and thirst for righteousness, for they shall be satisfied. It is not enough for us to desire justice, unless we also endure the hunger for justice: so that, under this example, we may never consider ourselves fully just, but always understand the hunger for the works of justice.

<h2 id='tocuniq56'>(Vers. 7.)</h2>

(Verse 7) Blessed are the merciful, for they will receive mercy. Mercy is not only understood in acts of charity, but also in bearing the burdens of one another's sins (Galatians 6).

<h2 id='tocuniq57'>(Vers. 8.)</h2>

(Verse 8.) Blessed are the pure in heart, for they shall see God. Those who are not accused by any conscience of sin. The pure in heart are seen by the pure: the temple of God cannot be defiled.

<h2 id='tocuniq58'>(Vers. 9.)</h2>

(Verse 9.) Blessed are the peacemakers, for they shall be called children of God. They first make peace in their own hearts, and then among their discordant brethren. For what good is it to pacify others through you, when there are wars of vices in your own soul?

<h2 id='tocuniq59'>(Vers. 10.)</h2>

(Verse 10.) Blessed are those who are persecuted for righteousness' sake, for theirs is the kingdom of heaven. He specifically added (or says), for righteousness' sake. For many indeed suffer persecution for their own sins and are not righteous. Also, consider that the blessedness of true circumcision is concluded with martyrdom.

<h2 id='tocuniq60'>(Vers 11.)</h2>

(Verse 11.) Blessed are you when men revile you and persecute you and utter all kinds of evil against you falsely on my account. That curse should be despised which creates blessedness, which is falsely uttered by the mouth of one who curses. Hence, he specially defined what should be the blessed curse: every curse uttered against you falsely on my account. Where Christ is therefore the cause, there also is the desirable curse.


<h2 id='tocuniq61'>(Vers. 12.)</h2>

(Verse 12.) Rejoice and be glad, for your reward is great in heaven. For so they persecuted the prophets who were before you. I do not know who among us can fulfill this, that our reputation be torn apart by insults, and yet we rejoice in the Lord. Those who pursue empty glory cannot fulfill this. Therefore, we must rejoice and be glad, so that a reward may be prepared for us in heavenly things. We elegantly read in a certain volume: 'Do not seek glory, and you will not grieve when you are without glory.'" } »

<h2 id='tocuniq62'>(Vers. 13.)</h2>

(Verse 13.) You are the salt of the earth. The apostles are called salt, because through them the entire human race is preserved.

25 Quod si sal evannerit, in quo salietur? Si doctor erraverit, a quo alio doctore emendabitur?

It is worth nothing more, except to be thrown out and trampled by men. An example is taken from agriculture. For salt, indeed, is necessary as a seasoning for food and for preserving meat: it has no other use. Certainly we read in the Scriptures that certain cities, sown with the salt of the conquered, so that no seed would sprout in them (Judith. IX). Therefore let the doctors and bishops beware and see: the powerful can withstand torment powerfully (Sap. VI, 7); and that there is no remedy: but to lead the ruins of the ancestors to Tartarus.


<h2 id='tocuniq63'>(Vers. 14 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 14 onwards) You are the light of the world. A city set on a hill cannot be hidden; nor does anyone light a lamp and put it under a basket, but on the lampstand, and it gives light to all who are in the house. Let your light shine before men in such a way that they may see your good works, and glorify your Father who is in heaven. It teaches confidence in preaching, so that the apostles do not hide out of fear and be like a lamp under a basket, but rather freely reveal themselves, so that what they heard in private, they may preach on the housetops (Matthew 10:27)."  }


<h2 id='tocuniq64'>(Vers. 17.)</h2>

(Verse 17.) Do not think that I came to abolish the Law or the Prophets. I did not come to abolish, but to fulfill. Whether it is that He fulfilled the prophecies about Himself through others, or that He fulfilled those things which were rudimentary and imperfect before due to the weakness of the listeners, by His preaching, removing wrath, excluding the principle of retaliation, and the hidden desire in the mind.

<h2 id='tocuniq65'>(Vers. 18.)</h2>

(Verse 18.) Until heaven and earth pass away. The new heavens and the new earth are promised to us, which the Lord God will make. Therefore, if new things are to be created, the old ones will pass away as a result. But what follows:

Iota unum, aut unus apex non praeteribit a Lege, donec omnia fiant. Ex figura litterae ostenditur, quod etiam quae minima putantur in Lege, sacramentis spiritualibus plena sint, et omnia recapitulentur in Evangelio. Cujus ergo eruditionis est, cujusque doctrinae, etiam diversa sacrificia, et quae superstitiosa videntur, in victimis quotidie demonstrare compleri?

<h2 id='tocuniq66'>(Vers. 19 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 19 onwards) Therefore, whoever breaks one of the least of these commandments, and teaches others to do the same, will be called least in the kingdom of heaven; but whoever does and teaches them, he will be called great in the kingdom of heaven. For I tell you, unless your righteousness exceeds that of the scribes and Pharisees, you will never enter the kingdom of heaven. You have heard that it was said to the ancients: 'You shall not murder,' and whoever murders will be liable to judgment. But I say to you. This chapter agrees with the previous testimony, in which he said: One iota or one dot will not pass from the Law, until all things are accomplished. Therefore, it condemns the Pharisees who, disregarding the commandments of God, established their own traditions, which do not benefit the people if they destroy even the smallest thing that is commanded in the Law. However, we can also understand it differently, that the teaching of the masters, even if liable to a small sin, takes them down from the highest position and does not benefit them in teaching righteousness, which the slightest fault destroys. And let perfect happiness consist in fulfilling in action what you have taught in words.

<h2 id='tocuniq67'>(Vers. 22.)</h2>

(Verse 22.) Because everyone who is angry with his brother will be liable to judgment. In some codices, it is added 'without cause,' but in true definitive sentence it is stated, and anger is completely abolished, the Scripture saying: 'Whoever is angry with his brother.' For if we are commanded to offer the other cheek to one who strikes us and to love our enemies and pray for those persecuting us (Luke VI), every occasion of anger is removed. Therefore, 'without cause' must be removed, because the anger of man does not accomplish the justice of God (James I).


But whoever says to his brother 'Raca,' shall be guilty before the council. And this word is properly of the Hebrews: Raca () for κενὸς, that is, empty or void: which we can express in common insult, without brains, we can say. If we are going to render an account for idle talk, how much more for insult! But it is also emphatically added: Whoever says to his brother, 'Raca.' For our brother is no one else, but the one who has the same Father as us. So, when he believes in God in the same way, and knows the wisdom of God in Christ (I Cor. I): by what reasoning can it be indicated by the praise of folly?

But whoever says, 'You fool!' will be liable to the hell of fire. From a common perspective, it is understood that whoever says to his brother, 'You fool!' will be liable to the hell of fire. For anyone who insults a believer by calling them a fool is impious in religion.

<h2 id='tocuniq68'>(Vers. 23, 24.)</h2>

(Verse 23, 24.) Therefore, if you bring your gift to the altar, and there you remember that your brother has something against you, leave your gift there in front of the altar, and go first to reconcile with your brother; and then come and offer your gift. He did not say, if you have something against your brother, but if your brother has something against you, so that a more difficult necessity of reconciliation may be imposed on you. As long as we cannot appease him, I do not know if we should consequently offer our gifts to God.


<h2 id='tocuniq69'>(Vers. 25 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 25 and following) Be agreeable with your adversary quickly, while you are on the way with him, lest your adversary deliver you to the judge, and the judge deliver you to the officer, and you be thrown into prison. Amen I tell you, you shall by no means get out of there, until you have paid the last penny. You have heard that it was said to the ancients, 'You shall not commit adultery.' But I tell you, that everyone. But from the preceding and following, it is clear that our Lord and Savior, while we run on the way of this world, encourages us to peace and concord, according to the Apostle, saying: If it is possible, as much as it depends on you, have peace with all men (Rom. XII, 18). For in the preceding chapter he also said: If you offer your gift at the altar, and there you remember that your brother has something against you: and when that is finished, he immediately adds: Be agreeable or benevolent to your adversary, and so on. And in the following, he commands: Love your enemies, do good to those who hate you, and pray for those who persecute and slander you. When this is evident, and the consequent understanding, many think it to be about the flesh and the soul, or the soul and the spirit: which is not entirely true. For how can the flesh be thrown into prison if the soul does not consent? Since both the soul and the flesh must be confined together, and the flesh can do nothing except what the mind commands, or the Holy Spirit dwelling in us hands over the flesh or the soul opposing judgment, for he himself is the judge. Others, according to the Epistle of Peter, saying: Your adversary the devil, as a roaring lion, goeth about (I Pet. V, 8), and the rest, interpret the adversary as the devil, and they desire to be commanded by the Savior that, while it is in our power, we may be kind towards the devil, who is an enemy and avenger, and not make him suffer punishment on our behalf. For when he himself supplies the incentives of vices, and we also willingly sin, if we consent to him suggesting vices, he must be tortured on our behalf as well. And they say it is pleasing for each saint to resist their adversary if they do not make them suffer torment for themselves. Some argue more forcefully, saying that in Baptism each person enters into a pact with the devil and says: I renounce you, devil, and your pomp, and your vices, and your world, which is placed in wickedness (1 John 5:19). Therefore, if we keep the pact, we are kind and agreeable to our adversary and should not be imprisoned. But if we should transgress anything of what we promised to the devil, we shall be handed over to the judge and the officer, and we shall be thrown into prison, and we shall not be released from it until we pay the last quadrant. A quadrant is a kind of coin that has two minutes. Hence, in another Gospel, that poor and widowed woman is said to have sent a quadrant into the treasury  (Mark 12), and in another, two minutes  (Luke 21). Not that the Gospels are inconsistent, but because one quadrant has two minute coins. This is therefore what he says: You will not leave the prison until you have also paid for the smallest sins.

<h2 id='tocuniq70'>(Vers. 28.)</h2>

(Verse 28) Whoever looks at a woman with the intention of lusting after her, he has already committed adultery with her in his heart. Between πάθος and προπάθεια, that is, between passion and pre-passion, there is this difference, that passion is considered a vice: pre-passion, although it has the fault of beginning, is not held accountable for the crime. Therefore, whoever looks at a woman and his soul is tickled, he is struck by pre-passion. But if he consents and allows himself to be affected by the thought, as it is written in David: "They passed over to the affectation of the heart" (Ps. 73:7), from pre-passion he passes to passion, and it is not a lack of will to sin, but an opportunity. Therefore, whoever sees a woman with the intention of lusting after her, that is, if he looks in order to desire or plan to act, he is rightly said to commit adultery in his heart.

<h2 id='tocuniq71'>(Vers. 29, 30.)</h2>

(Verse 29, 30) But if your right eye causes you to sin, tear it out and throw it away. For it is better for you to lose one of your members than for your whole body to be thrown into Hell. And if your right hand causes you to sin, cut it off and throw it away. For it is better for you to lose one of your members than for your whole body to go into Hell. He had previously spoken about the desire for a woman, and now he aptly called the wandering thought and sense "the eye. But by the right hand and the other parts of the body, the beginnings of will and emotions are shown: so that what we conceive in our mind, we may accomplish by action. Therefore, we must be careful that what is best in us does not quickly fall into vice. For if the right eye and right hand offend, how much more those things that are on the left side of us! For if the soul falls, how much more the body, which is more inclined to sin! Otherwise. In the right eye and in the right hand, the affection of brothers, wives, and children, as well as of relatives and friends, is shown. If we see that these hinder us from contemplating the true light, we must cut off such attachments, so that while we desire to benefit others, we ourselves do not perish forever. And it is said about the high priest, whose soul is dedicated to the worship of God: He shall not defile himself for the dead among his people, except for his relatives. (Lev. 21:11), that is, he shall not have any emotional attachment except to those to whom he is dedicated.

<h2 id='tocuniq72'>(Vers. 31 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 31 onwards) It was said, however: Whoever divorces his wife, let him give her a certificate of divorce. But I say to you: that whoever divorces his wife, except for the cause of fornication, allows her to commit adultery; and whoever marries a divorced woman commits adultery. Again, you have heard that it was said to the ancients: You shall not swear falsely, but you shall fulfill your oaths to the Lord. In the later part, the Savior further explains this passage, that Moses commanded the giving of a certificate of divorce because of the hardness of the hearts of the husbands, not permitting divorce but removing homicide (Deut. XXIV). For it is much better, even if mournful discord arises, than for blood to be shed through hatred.

<h2 id='tocuniq73'>(Vers. 34 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 34 onwards) But I say to you, do not swear at all: neither by heaven, for it is the throne of God; nor by the earth, for it is his footstool; nor by Jerusalem, for it is the city of the great King. Nor shall you swear by your head, for you cannot make a single hair white or black. Let your 'yes' be 'yes,' and your 'no' be 'no.' Anything more than this comes from the evil one. The Jews have always had this worst custom of swearing by the elements, as the prophet frequently condemns them (Isaiah 65). Whoever swears, either reveres or loves the one by whom he swears." } In the law it is commanded that we do not swear, except by the Lord our God (Deut. VI and VII). The Jews, by swearing through angels, the city of Jerusalem, the temple, and the elements, honored and worshipped creatures and carnal things, but God should be honored and obeyed. Finally, consider that here the Savior did not forbid swearing by God, but by heaven, earth, Jerusalem, and by your own head. And this was allowed as if to little children by the law, so that just as they sacrificed victims to God and not to idols, they would be permitted to swear by God; not that they were doing this rightly, but because it was better to show this to God than to demons. However, the truth of the Gospel does not require an oath, since every faithful word is considered as an oath.

<h2 id='tocuniq74'>(Vers. 38.)</h2>

(Verse 38.) You have heard that it was said: An eye for an eye, and a tooth for a tooth. But I say to you, do not resist evil. The one who says an eye for an eye does not want to take away the other, but to preserve both. Our Lord, abolishing vengeance, cuts off the beginnings of sins. And in the Law there is retribution, but in the Gospel there is grace. There, guilt is corrected; here, the beginnings of sins are removed.

<h2 id='tocuniq75'>(Vers. 39.)</h2>

(Verse 39.) 31 But if anyone strikes you on the right cheek, offer him the other also. And if anyone wants to sue you and take your tunic, let him have your cloak as well. And whoever forces you to go one mile, go with him two. The man of Ecclesiastes is described as an imitator of him who says, 'Learn from me, for I am gentle and humble in heart' (Below II, 29). And he proves his promise by being slapped in the face: 'If I have spoken wrongly,' he says, 'testify to the wrong; but if I have spoken rightly, why do you strike me?' (John 18:23)." } Such is what David spoke in the Psalm: 'If I have repaid those who have done evil to me' (Ps. 7:5). And Jeremiah in the Lamentations: 'It is good for a man when he bears' ('sits under', etc.) 'the yoke from his youth. Let him offer his cheek to the one who strikes him; he will be filled with reproach' (Lam. 3:27, 30). This is directed against those who think there is one God of the Law and another of the Gospel; both there and here, gentleness is taught. According to a mystical understanding: our right hand, when struck, we are not commanded to offer our left, but rather our other right hand. For the just man does not have his left hand. If he should strike us in a dispute as a heretic and want to wound the right doctrine, let another testimony from the Scriptures be presented to him, and let us offer our right hands to him while he continues striking until the anger of the enemy subsides.

<h2 id='tocuniq76'>(Vers. 42, 43.)</h2>

(Verse 42, 43.) Whoever asks of you, give to him, and whoever wishes to borrow from you, do not turn away. You have heard that it was said: Love your neighbor and hate your enemy. If we understand this as only referring to almsgiving, it cannot apply to most of the poor. But even if the rich always give, they cannot always give. Therefore, after the good of almsgiving, the apostles, that is, the teachers, are given precepts, so that those who have received freely may give freely (Matthew 10). Money of this kind never runs out; but the more it is given, the more it is multiplied. And when it irrigates the fields subject to it, the water of the fountain never dries up.

<h2 id='tocuniq77'>(Vers. 44.)</h2>

(Verse 44.) But I say to you, love your enemies, do good to those who hate you, and pray for those who persecute and calumniate you. Many consider the precepts of God impossible due to their own weakness, not appreciating the power of the saints, and they say that virtues are sufficient, not to hate one's enemies. However, it is commanded to love more than human nature can endure. Therefore, it must be understood that Christ does not command the impossible, but the perfect: what David did to Saul and Absalom (1 Samuel 24 and 26, and 2 Samuel 18). Stephanus also prayed for his enemies who were stoning him (Acts 7). And Paul desires to be accursed for his persecutors (Romans 9). Jesus both taught and did these things, saying: 'Father, forgive them, for they know not what they do' (Luke 23:34).

<h2 id='tocuniq78'>(Vers. 45.)</h2>

(Verse 45.) That you may be children of your Father who is in heaven; who makes his sun rise on the good and the evil, and sends rain on the just and the unjust. For if you love those who love you, what reward do you have? Do not even the tax collectors do the same? And if you greet only your brothers, what more are you doing? Do not even the Gentiles do the same? Therefore you must be perfect, as your heavenly Father is perfect. If one keeps the commandments of God, they become a child of God. Therefore, they are not a child by nature, but by their own choice.

<h2 id='tocuniq79'>(Chap. VI.—Vers. 1.)</h2>

(Chapter 6, Verse 1) Take heed that you do not your righteousness before men, to be seen of them: otherwise you have no reward of your Father who is in heaven. Therefore when thou doest thine alms, do not sound a trumpet before thee, as the hypocrites do in the synagogues and in the streets, that they may have glory of men. Verily I say unto you, They have their reward. But when thou doest alms, let not thy left hand know what thy right hand doeth: That thine alms may be in secret: and thy Father who seeth in secret himself shall reward thee openly. And when thou prayest, thou shalt not be as the hypocrites are: for they love to pray standing in the synagogues and in the corners of the streets, that they may be seen of men. Verily I say unto you, They have their reward. From all of these things it is gathered that they are hypocrites, who do everything in order to be glorified (or honored) by men. It seems to me that even the one who says to his brother, 'Let me remove the speck from your eye' (Matthew VII, 4), does this for the sake of appearing righteous. Hence the Lord says to him: Hypocrite, first remove the beam from your own eye. Therefore, it is not virtue but the motive behind virtue that receives reward from God. If you have strayed a little from the right path, it doesn't matter whether you go to the right or to the left, since you have lost the true path.

<h2 id='tocuniq80'>(Vers. 3, 4.)</h2>

(Verses. 3, 4.) But when you give alms, do not let your left hand know what your right hand is doing, so that your alms may be in secret; and your Father who sees in secret will reward you. And when you pray, you must not be like the hypocrites; for they love to stand and pray in the synagogues and at the street corners, so that they may be seen by others. Truly I tell you, they have received their reward. But when you give alms, do not let your left hand know what your right hand is doing, so that your alms may be in secret; and your Father who sees in secret will reward you.


Truly I tell you, they have received their reward. Not God's reward, but their own. For they were praised by men, for whom they performed their virtuous acts.

<h2 id='tocuniq81'>(Vers. 6.)</h2>

(Verse 6) But you, when you pray, go into your room, and when you have shut your door, pray to your Father who is in secret; and your Father who sees in secret will reward you. This is simply understood, it instructs the listener to avoid vain glory in prayer. But it seems to me that this is more of a command to pray with inward thoughts, and with lips shut, as we read that Anna did in the Book of Kings; Her lips moved only (1 Kings 1:13).


<h2 id='tocuniq82'>(Vers. 7.)</h2>

(Verse 7.) But when praying, do not use many words as the pagans do. For they think that by their many words they will be heard. Therefore, do not be like them. If a pagan speaks many words in prayer, then a Christian ought to speak few. For God is not the listener of words, but of the heart. (Wisdom 1:6).

<h2 id='tocuniq83'>(Vers. 8.)</h2>

(Verse 8) For your Father knows what you need before you ask him. So you should pray like this. There arises in this place a certain heresy, and also a perverse teaching of the philosophers, who say: If God knows what we pray for, and what we need before we ask, then we speak in vain to the one who knows. To this, we must respond briefly that we are not narrators, but askers. For it is one thing to narrate to someone who is ignorant, and another to ask of someone who knows. In that there is evidence, here there is obedience. There we faithfully indicate, here we plead miserably.

<h2 id='tocuniq84'>(Vers. 9.)</h2>

(Verse 9.) Our Father, who art in heaven. By saying 'Father,' they confess themselves as sons.

Hallowed be thy name. Not in you, but in us. For if the name of God is blasphemed among the Gentiles because of sinners (Rom. 8), on the contrary, it is hallowed because of the righteous.

<h2 id='tocuniq85'>(Vers. 10.)</h2>

(Verse 10.) Your kingdom come. Either generally for the kingdom of the whole world, that the devil may cease to reign in the world, or that God may reign in each one, and sin may not reign in the mortal body of man (Rom. VI). And at the same time, this must also be noted, that it is a great boldness and pure conscience to demand the kingdom of God and not to fear judgment.

Your will be done, as in heaven and on earth. Just as the Angels serve you blamelessly in heaven, so may humans serve you on earth. Let those be ashamed who daily lie about the falling of ruins from heaven. For what benefit is there to us in the likeness of heaven, if there is sin even in heaven?

<h2 id='tocuniq86'>(Vers. 11-13.)</h2>

(Verses 11-13.) Give us this day our daily bread. And forgive us our debts, as we also have forgiven our debtors. And lead us not into temptation. But deliver us from evil. The word 'supersubstantialem' that we have translated is rendered as 'epiousios' in Greek, a word that the Septuagint translators often render as 'periousios'. Therefore, we have considered the Hebrew, and wherever they have rendered 'periousios', we have found 'Sgolla', which Symmachus has translated as 'exaireton', meaning special or excellent, although he has provided a different translation in one particular place. Therefore, when we ask for special or excellent bread from God, we ask for Him who says: I am the living bread which came down from heaven (John 6:51). In the Gospel called according to the Hebrews, instead of supersubstantial bread, I found the word Mahar, which means tomorrow; so the sense is: Give us our bread for tomorrow, that is, for the future, today. We can also understand supersubstantial bread in another way, as that which is above all substances and surpasses all creatures. Others simply think, according to the words of the Apostle saying (1 Tim. 6:8): Having food and clothing, with these we are content, that we should only be concerned with providing holy food for the present. Hence, in what follows, it is commanded: Do not worry about tomorrow.

Amen. The sign of the Lord's Prayer is: which the Eagle interprets faithfully: we, truly, can say.

<h2 id='tocuniq87'>(Vers. 14.)</h2>

(Verse 14.) For if you forgive men their offenses, your heavenly Father will also forgive you your offenses. This is what is written: I said, You are gods, and all of you are sons of the Most High; but you shall die like men, and fall as one of the princes. (Psalm 82:6-7) This is said to those who, because of their sins, deserved to be considered gods. Therefore, it is right that even those to whom sins are forgiven are called men.


<h2 id='tocuniq88'>(Vers. 16.)</h2>

(Verse 16.) For they disfigure their faces, so that they may be seen by men to be fasting. Amen I say to you, they have received their reward. The word exterminant, which is often misunderstood in the Scriptures, means something far different than it is commonly understood. For exterminant refers to those who are expelled and sent outside the boundaries. Therefore, we must always take care with this expression: which in Greek is ἀφανίζουσιν. However, the hypocrite demolishes his face to simulate sadness; and with a strong mind rejoicing, he carries grief on his countenance.

<h2 id='tocuniq89'>(Vers. 17 seq.)</h2>

(Ver. 17 seq.) But when you fast, anoint your head and wash your face, so that you do not appear to be fasting to men, but to your Father who is in secret; and your Father who sees in secret will repay you. Do not store up for yourselves treasures on earth, where rust and moth consume, and where thieves break in and steal. He speaks according to the custom of the province of Palestine, where they are accustomed to anoint their heads on feast days. Therefore, he commanded that when we fast, we should show ourselves to be cheerful and festive. Those who read the Psalmist say: The oil of sinners shall not anoint my head (Ps. CXL, 5), on the contrary, they want the good oil, of which it is said elsewhere: God, your God, has anointed you with the oil of gladness above your fellows (Ps. XLIV, 8). And He commands that we, who exercise virtues, should anoint the principal (ἡγεμονικὸν) of our heart with spiritual oil.

<h2 id='tocuniq90'>(Vers. 21.)</h2>

(Verse 21) For where your treasure is, there will your heart be also. This applies not only to money, but also to all possessions. The greedy god is the stomach: there, therefore, he has his heart, where his treasure is. (Verse 36) The treasure of the gluttonous is feasts. For the lustful, it is games. For the lover, it is desire. Each person serves whom they are conquered by. (2 Peter 2:19).

<h2 id='tocuniq91'>(Vers. 22, 23.)</h2>

(Verse 22, 23.) If your eye is clear, your whole body will be bright. But if your eye is bad, your whole body will be dark. Therefore, if the light in you is darkness, how great is the darkness! Those with blurred vision ((Or: with blemished eyes)) tend to see many lights: a clear and pure eye sees clear and pure things. This can be applied to the sense as a whole. Just as the body is in darkness if the eye is not clear, so the soul, if it loses its principal brightness, will dwell in darkness with all its senses. If therefore the light which is within is darkness, how great is that darkness! If the sense which is light is clouded by the vice of the soul, how much darkness do you think will envelop it!

<h2 id='tocuniq92'>(Vers. 24.)</h2>

(Verse 24) You cannot serve God and mammon. Mammon is called wealth in the Syriac language. You cannot serve God and mammon. Let the greedy hear this, let those who are considered Christians by name know that they cannot serve both wealth and Christ at the same time. And yet, it is not said, 'he who has wealth,' but 'he who serves wealth.' For whoever is a servant of wealth, guards it like a servant; but whoever shakes off the yoke of servitude, distributes it like a master.


<h2 id='tocuniq93'>(Vers. 25.)</h2>

(Verse 25) Therefore I tell you: do not be anxious about your life, what you will eat or what you will drink, nor about your body, what you will put on. In some manuscripts it is added: nor what you will drink. Therefore, what nature gives to all, and is common to both animals and humans, we are completely free from the care of this. But we are commanded not to be anxious about what we will eat, because with the sweat of our brow we prepare bread for ourselves. Labor must be exercised, anxiety must be removed. This which is said: Do not be anxious about what you will eat, nor about what you will wear (Gen. III), let us understand it concerning carnal food and clothing. However, we should always be concerned about spiritual food and clothing.

<h2 id='tocuniq94'>(Vers. 26.)</h2>

(Verse 26.) Is not the soul more than food, and the body more than clothing? What he is saying is this: He who has provided greater things will certainly provide lesser things as well.

Look at the birds of the sky, that they do not sow, nor reap, nor gather into barns, and yet your heavenly Father feeds them. Are you not worth much more than they? The Apostle teaches (Rom. XI) that we should not be wiser than we ought to be. This testimony should be kept in mind in the present chapter. For there are some who, while they desire to surpass the limits of the fathers and soar to the heights, are plunged into the depths, saying that the birds of the sky are angels and that the other powers in the service of God, which are nourished without concern by the providence of their God. If this is true, as they want it to be understood, how does the statement follow to men: Are you not more valuable than them? Thus it must be understood simply: if the birds are nourished by God's providence without care and toil, which exist today and will not exist tomorrow, how much more are men, to whom eternity is promised, governed by God's will!

<h2 id='tocuniq95'>(Vers. 27.)</h2>

(Verse 27.) But which of you, being anxious, can add one cubit to his stature? And why are you anxious about clothing? Consider the birds of the air, that they don't sow, neither do they reap, nor gather into barns. Your heavenly Father feeds them. Aren't you of much more value than they?

<h2 id='tocuniq96'>(Vers. 28-30.)</h2>

(Vers. 28-30.) Consider the lilies of the field, how they grow: they neither toil nor spin. And yet I tell you that even Solomon in all his glory was not arrayed like one of these. Now if God so clothes the grass of the field, which today is alive and tomorrow is thrown into the oven, will he not much more clothe you, O you of little faith? And why are you anxious about clothing? Consider the lilies of the field, how they grow: they neither toil nor spin. Why does the lily shine so brightly? The violet, indeed, surpasses even purple, not with any purple dye, but with the judgment of the eyes rather than of words.

<h2 id='tocuniq97'>(Vers. 31 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 31 and following) Do not be anxious, saying: What shall we eat, or what shall we drink, or what shall we wear? For all these things the Gentiles seek. For your heavenly Father knows that you need all these things. But seek first the kingdom of God and His righteousness, and all these things will be added to you. Therefore, do not be anxious about tomorrow, for tomorrow will be anxious for itself. Sufficient for the day is its own trouble. Therefore, he conceded that those who prohibit thinking about the future should be anxious about present matters. And the Apostle says: 'Night and day, we worked with our own hands, so as not to be a burden to any of you' (1 Thess. 2:9). In the Scriptures, 'tomorrow' is understood to mean a future time, as Jacob said: 'He will listen to me tomorrow, because of my righteousness' (Gen. 30:33). And in the vision of Samuel, the witch of Endor speaks to Saul: 'Tomorrow you will be with me' (1 Sam. 28:19).

<h2 id='tocuniq98'>(Vers. 34.)</h2>

(Verse 34.) Each day has enough trouble of its own. Here, he placed malice, not contrary to virtue, but rather labor and affliction, and the hardships of the world: just as Sarah afflicted her maidservant Hagar (Gen. XVI), which is significantly said in Greek ἐκάκωσεν αὐτὴν. Therefore, let us be content with the thoughts of the present time; let us leave the care of the future, which is uncertain.

<h2 id='tocuniq99'>(Chap. VII.—Vers. 1, 2.)</h2>

(Chapter VII - Verses 1, 2) Do not judge, so that you may not be judged. For with the judgment you pronounce you will be judged, and with the measure you use it will be measured to you. If judging is prohibited, what is the consequence of Paul judging the fornicator in Corinth (1 Corinthians 5) and Peter rebuking Ananias and Sapphira for their lie (Acts 5)? But he shows what he prohibits from the consequences, saying: for with the judgment you pronounce, you will be judged. Therefore, he did not prevent judgment, but he taught.

<h2 id='tocuniq100'>(Vers. 3-5.)</h2>

(Verses 3-5.) But why do you see the speck in your brother's eye and not notice the beam in your own eye? Or how can you say to your brother, 'Brother, let me take out the speck from your eye,' when you yourself do not see the beam in your own eye? Hypocrite, first take the beam out of your own eye, and then you will see clearly to take out the speck from your brother's eye. He is speaking about those who, while themselves guilty of mortal sin, do not forgive minor sins in their brothers: straining out a gnat and swallowing a camel (Matthew 23)." } Therefore, those who, as we have said above, are falsely called hypocrites, are rightly condemned.
