They look at the splinter in their brother's eye through the beam in their own.

<h2 id='tocuniq101'>(Vers. 6.)</h2>

(Verse 6.) Do not give what is holy to dogs. Holy, bread is for the children. Therefore, we should not take the bread of the children and give it to the dogs.

Do not cast your pearls before swine, lest they trample them under their feet, and turn and tear you to pieces. A swine does not appreciate ornaments when it wallows in the mire. And according to the Proverbs of Solomon: If he has a golden ring, he is found more repugnant (Prov. XI, 22). Some understand them as dogs who return to the vomit of their sins after having believed in Christ: but pigs are those who have not yet believed in the Gospel and are immersed in the mud of unbelief and vices. Therefore, it is not fitting for people of this kind to quickly believe the Gospel pearl, lest they trample it and, having been converted, begin to scatter.

<h2 id='tocuniq102'>(Vers. 7 seq.)</h2>

(Verse 7 onwards) Ask, and it will be given to you; seek, and you will find; knock, and it will be opened to you. For everyone who asks receives, and he who seeks finds, and to him who knocks it will be opened. Or what man is there among you, who, if his son asks for bread, will give him a stone? Or if he asks for a fish, will he give him a serpent? He demonstrates what we should seek, having forbidden to ask for carnal things. If it is given to the one who asks, and the one who seeks finds, and to the one who knocks it is opened, therefore it is clear that he who does not receive, and does not find, and to whom it is not opened, has not asked, sought, and knocked well. Let us therefore knock at the door of Christ, of which it is said: This is the gate of the Lord, the righteous shall enter through it (Ps. CXVII, 20); so that when we have entered, hidden and dark treasures may be revealed to us in Christ Jesus, in whom all knowledge is (Coloss. II).

<h2 id='tocuniq103'>(Vers. 11, 12.)</h2>

(Verses 11, 12.) So if you, being evil, know how to give good gifts to your children, how much more will your Father who is in heaven give good things to those who ask Him! Therefore, whatever you want men to do to you, do also to them, for this is the Law and the Prophets. It should be noted that he called the apostles evil, unless perhaps under the guise of the apostles the entire race of men is condemned, whose hearts from infancy are inclined towards evil in comparison to divine mercy. Read Genesis (Gen. VIII). It is not surprising if people of this age are called evil, since the Apostle Paul also reminds us: Redeeming the time, because the days are evil (Ephes. V, 16).

<h2 id='tocuniq104'>(Vers. 13, 14.)</h2>

(Ver. 13, 14.) Enter through the narrow gate, because wide is the gate and spacious is the way that leads to destruction, and many are those who enter through it. How narrow is the gate, and tight the way that leads to life! And few are those who find it. The wide way is the pleasure of the world, which men desire. Narrow is the path, which is opened through labors and fasts, which even the Apostle entered (2 Corinthians 6, 11): and he encourages Timothy to enter through it (1 Timothy 5). At the same time, consider how clearly he speaks about both paths. Many walk on the broad path, but few find the narrow one. We do not seek the broad path, nor is there a need for discovery: it presents itself spontaneously, and it is the path of those who wander. However, not everyone finds the narrow path, nor do those who find it immediately enter it. Indeed, many, having discovered the path of truth, are captivated by the pleasures of the world and turn back from the middle of the journey.

<h2 id='tocuniq105'>(Vers. 15 seq.)</h2>

(Verse 15 and following) Beware of false prophets, who come to you in sheep's clothing but inwardly are ravenous wolves. You will recognize them by their fruits. Are grapes gathered from thornbushes, or figs from thistles? So, every healthy tree bears good fruit, but the diseased tree bears bad fruit. And by their fruits, you will know them. It can be understood in general that those who promise one thing in appearance and speech, but show another thing in action, are deceptive. But specifically, this should be understood about heretics, who seem to wrap themselves in the garment of piety, such as continence, chastity, and fasting, but inwardly have a poisoned mind, deceiving the hearts of the simple-minded brothers. Therefore, from the fruits of the soul, which lead innocence to ruin, they are compared to rapacious wolves.

<h2 id='tocuniq106'>(Vers. 18 seq.)</h2>

(Verse 18 and following) A good tree cannot bear bad fruit, nor can a bad tree bear good fruit. Every tree that does not bear good fruit will be cut down and thrown into the fire. So, by their fruits you will know them. Let us ask the heretics who claim that there are two contrary natures in themselves, if, according to their understanding, a good tree can never bear bad fruit, how did Moses, a good tree, sin by striking the rock with his staff (Deut. XXXII), and how did David, after killing Uriah, commit adultery with Bathsheba (II Sam. XI)? Also, how did Peter, during the Passion of the Lord, deny Him, saying, 'I do not know the man' (Matt. XXVI, 72)? What is the connection between Jethro, Moses' father-in-law, who certainly did not believe in the God of Israel, giving good advice to Moses (Exod. XVIII), and Achior speaking something useful to Holofernes (Judith. V)? And as the comedian said (which the Apostle approved): 'Evil conversations corrupt good manners' (I Cor. V). And when they do not find what to reply, we will bring up the example of Judas (John 13), who was once a good tree but produced bad fruits after betraying (or delivering) the Savior; and of Saul (Philippians 3), who was a bad tree when he persecuted (or hunted down) the Church of Christ, but produced good fruits afterwards when he was converted into a vessel of election (Acts 9). Therefore, a good tree does not bear bad fruits as long as it perseveres in the pursuit of goodness, and a bad tree continues to bear the fruits of sin as long as it does not turn to repentance. For no one remains in that which was, but begins to be that which has not yet begun.

<h2 id='tocuniq107'>(Vers. 21.)</h2>

(Verse 21) Not everyone who says to me, 'Lord, Lord,' will enter the kingdom of heaven, but only the one who does the will of my Father who is in heaven. As he said before, those who have the garment of a good life should not be received because of the wickedness of their teaching; now, on the contrary, he asserts that even faith should not be accommodated to those who, though they possess the integrity of faith, live in a shameful manner and destroy the integrity of doctrine with evil works. For both the work by word and the word by works are necessary for the servants of God to be proven. This statement can be seen as contrary to that saying: No one can say, 'Jesus is Lord,' except in the Holy Spirit (I Cor. XII, 3). However, it is customary for the sayings of the Scriptures to be understood as actions, as immediately in the following it is confirmed, refuting those who boast of having knowledge of the Lord without works, and they hear from the Savior: Depart from me, you workers of iniquity, I do not know you (Luke XIII). And the Apostle speaks in this sense: They confess to know God, but by their deeds they deny Him (Titus 1:16).

<h2 id='tocuniq108'>(Vers. 22.)</h2>

(Vers. 22.) Many will say to me on that day: Lord, Lord, did we not prophesy in your name, and in your name cast out demons, and in your name perform many miracles? Sometimes, it is not the merit of the one who works to prophesy, perform miracles, or cast out demons, but either the invocation of the name of Christ that accomplishes it, or for the condemnation of those who invoke it, and for the benefit of those who see and hear, it is granted: so that even though people may despise those who perform signs, they may still honor God, for whose invocation such great miracles are done. For both Saul (1 Samuel 10) and Balaam (Numbers 23) and Caiaphas (John 11) prophesied without knowing what they were saying. And Pharaoh (Genesis 41) and Nebuchadnezzar (Daniel 2) understood future events through dreams. And in the Acts of the Apostles, the sons of Sceva were seen casting out demons (Acts 19). But it is also told that Judas the apostle, with the intention of a traitor, performed many miracles among the other apostles.

<h2 id='tocuniq109'>42 (Vers. 23.)</h2>

42 (Verse 23.) And then I will confess to them, because I never knew you. He specifically said, I will confess, because he had previously pretended not to know them: I never knew you. The Lord does not know those who perish. However, observe why he added, I never knew you, if, according to some, they have always been among rational creatures.

<h2 id='tocuniq110'>(Vers. 24.)</h2>

(Verse 24) Depart from me, you workers of iniquity. Therefore, everyone who hears these words of mine and does them will be like a wise man who built his house on the rock. He did not say, 'You who have worked in iniquity,' so as not to seem to take away the opportunity for repentance, but rather 'you who work' - that is, those who, up to the present moment, when the time of judgment arrives, though you may not have the ability to sin, still have the inclination.


<h2 id='tocuniq111'>(Vers. 25.)</h2>

(Verse 25.) And the rain descended, and the rivers came, and the winds blew, and they beat upon that house, and it fell not: for it was founded upon a rock. This rain which tries to subvert the house is the devil. The rivers represent all the Antichrists who oppose Christ. The winds of spiritual wickedness are in the heavenly places (Ephesians 6).

<h2 id='tocuniq112'>(Vers. 26.)</h2>

(Verse 26) For it was founded upon a rock. And everyone who hears these words of mine and does not do them will be like a foolish man. Upon this rock the Lord built the Church (Matthew 15): from this rock the apostle Peter received his name. Upon such a rock the tracks of a serpent are not found (Proverbs 30). The prophet confidently speaks about this: He set my feet upon a rock (Psalm 40:3). And in another place: The rock is a refuge for rabbits, or hedgehogs (Psalm 104:8). For a timid animal seeks refuge in the caves of the rock: and with rough skin and fully armed with spears, it protects itself with such a defense. Hence it is said to Moses, at that time when he had fled from Egypt, and he was the little hare of the Lord: Stand in the hole of the rock, and you shall see my back (Exod. XXXIII, 21).

<h2 id='tocuniq113'>(Vers. 27, 28.)</h2>

(Vers. 27, 28.) He who built his house upon sand: and the rain came down, and the rivers came, and the winds blew, and they rushed against that house, and it fell: and its ruin was great. And it came to pass, when Jesus had finished these words, that the crowds were amazed at his teaching. The foundation which the Apostle, the architect, laid (I Cor. III), is one (or, one is) our Lord Jesus Christ. Upon this stable and firm foundation, and by itself a solid mass founded, the Church of Christ is built. Truly, every heretic speech is built towards the purpose of collapsing, just as [it is] unable to be joined together and unable to be reduced into one unity, indeed, which is loose.

<h2 id='tocuniq114'>(Vers. 29.)</h2>

(Verse 29.) For he was teaching them as one having authority, and not as the scribes and Pharisees. For they taught the people the things that were written in Moses and the Prophets. But Jesus, as though God and Lord Himself, added to the law for the sake of the freedom of His will, or changing it, preached to the people, as we also read above: It was said to the ancients: But I say to you.

<h2 id='tocuniq115'>(Chap. VIII.—Vers. 1.)</h2>

(Chapter 8, Verse 1) When Jesus descended from the mountain, many crowds followed him, and behold, a leper came and worshiped him, saying, 'When the Lord descended from the mountain, the crowds met him because they were unable to ascend to higher places. And the leper was the first to meet him. For he had not yet been able to hear the Savior's speech with such a multitude of leprosy on the mountain. And it should be noted that he was the first to be specifically cured: secondly, the Centurion's servant; thirdly, Peter's mother-in-law, who had a fever; fourthly, those who were presented to him, vexed by a demon, whose spirits he cast out with a word, when he cured all who were sick.' And behold, a leper came and worshiped Him, saying, 'Lord, if You are willing, You can make me clean.' After the preaching and teaching, there is an opportunity for a sign to be offered: that the word spoken may be confirmed in the hearing by the power of a miracle.

<h2 id='tocuniq116'>(Vers. 2.)</h2>

(Verse. 2.) Lord, if you will, you can cleanse me. He who asks for the will, does not doubt the power.

<h2 id='tocuniq117'>(Vers. 3.)</h2>

(Verse 3.) And Jesus, extending his hand, touched him, saying: I will it, be cleansed. And immediately his leprosy was cleansed. When the Lord extended his hand, the leprosy immediately fled. Also, consider how humble and without boasting his response was. He had said, if you will: the Lord responded, I will. He had said, you can cleanse me: the Lord joins in and says, be cleansed: Therefore, it is not, as many Latin speakers think, to be joined and read as 'I want to be cleansed', but separately, as first, he says, I want: then, commanding, he says, be cleansed.


<h2 id='tocuniq118'>(Vers. 4.)</h2>

(Verse 4) And Jesus said to him: See that you tell no one. And in truth, what was the necessity for him to boast in speech, which he surpassed in body?

44 But go, show yourself to the priests, and offer the gift that Moses commanded, as a testimony to them. He sends him to the priests for various reasons. First, out of humility, so that he may seem to defer honor to the priests. For it was commanded by the law that those who were cleansed from leprosy should offer gifts to the priests. Secondly, so that, seeing the leper cleansed, they either believe in the Savior or not believe. If they believe, they will be saved; if they do not believe, they will be without excuse. And at the same time, not to appear to violate the law with respect to that which they were most frequently accused of.

<h2 id='tocuniq119'>(Vers. 5 seq.)</h2>

(Verse 5 onwards) A centurion approached Him, begging Him and saying: Lord, my servant is lying at home paralyzed and suffering terribly. And Jesus said to him: I will come and heal him. But the centurion replied, saying: Lord, I am not worthy to have you come under my roof; but only say the word, and my servant will be healed. We should not accuse the Lord of boasting, because He immediately promises to go and heal, recognizing the faith, humility, and prudence of the centurion. He believed that a paralytic from the Gentiles could be healed by the Savior. He judged himself unworthy for the Lord to enter his house. He had the wisdom to see the hidden divinity within the flesh, knowing that what appeared to be unprofitable from the outside would be beneficial on the inside. Regarding this wisdom, he also said:

<h2 id='tocuniq120'>(Vers. 9.)</h2>

(Ver. 9.)  For I am also a man under authority ((or it can be added "appointed")), having soldiers under me: and I say to this one, go, and he goes: and to another, come, and he comes: and to my servant, do this, and he does it. Willing to show that the Lord can fulfill his will not only through the coming of his body, but also through the ministry of angels.

<h2 id='tocuniq121'>(Vers. 10.)</h2>

(Verse 10) And Jesus, hearing this, marveled and said to those following Him, 'I marvel that even my centurion understands my authority. For the weaknesses of the body needed to be driven away, as did the opposing strengths that often lead humans to weakness. And with the word of the Lord and the ministry of the angels, they were expelled.'

Truly I say to you, I have not found such great faith in Israel. He is speaking about the present, not about all the past patriarchs and prophets: unless perhaps the faith of the Gentiles is preferred over that of Israel.

<h2 id='tocuniq122'>(Vers. 11.)</h2>

(Verse 11.) But I say to you that many will come from the East and the West and sit down with Abraham, and Isaac, and Jacob in the kingdom of heaven. Because God, the creator of heaven, is the Father of Christ, therefore Abraham is also in the kingdom of heaven, with whom the nations that believe in Christ, the Son of the Creator, will recline. And likewise, that same meaning is fulfilled, which we mentioned earlier, in the faith of the centurion, that the privilege would be given to the nations: as the peoples who will believe from the East and the West are mentioned.


<h2 id='tocuniq123'>(Vers. 12.)</h2>

(Verse 12) But the children of the kingdom shall be cast out into outer darkness. The children of the kingdom refers to the Jews, over whom God reigned before. They shall be cast out into outer darkness. Darkness is always internal, not external. But since one who is expelled by the Lord leaves behind the light, therefore outer darkness is the term used.

There will be weeping and the gnashing of teeth. If there is weeping of the eyes, and the gnashing of teeth demonstrates the bones: therefore the resurrection of the bodies and the same members that had fallen is true.

<h2 id='tocuniq124'>(Vers. 14.)</h2>

(Verse 14) And when Jesus came into Peter's house, he saw his mother-in-law lying down and having a fever (alternate reading: burning with fever). And he touched her hand, and the fever left her. The hand of the woman is touched, and with his healing works, the weakness of sin flees. It is the nature of humans in this way, that after the fever, their bodies become even more weak: and as health begins, they feel the troubles of illness. But the health that is given by the Lord restores everything at once, and it is not enough to be healed; but to show an increase in strength, it is added:

<h2 id='tocuniq125'>(Vers. 15.)</h2>

(Verse 15.) And he arose, and served them. The hand that had been touched and healed also served." }

<h2 id='tocuniq126'>(Vers. 16-18.)</h2>

(Vers. 16-18.) And when evening came, they brought to him many who were possessed by demons, and he cast out the spirits with a word and healed all who were sick, so that what was spoken by the prophet Isaiah might be fulfilled: 'He took away our infirmities and bore our diseases.' And seeing the crowds around him, Jesus commanded his disciples to go across the sea. Everyone is healed, not in the morning or at noon, but in the evening, when the sun is setting. Like a grain of wheat that dies in the ground to produce many fruits (John 12).


<h2 id='tocuniq127'>(Vers. 19, 20.)</h2>

(Verse 19, 20.) And a certain scribe approaching said to him: Master, I will follow you wherever you go. And Jesus said to him: Foxes have dens, and birds of the sky have nests, but the Son of Man has nowhere to lay his head. This scribe of the law, who only knew the letter that kills, if he had said: Lord, I will follow you wherever you go, he would not have been rejected by the Lord; but because he esteemed one teacher among many, and was a mere scholar, which is more significantly said in Greek, γραμματεὺς, and not a spiritual listener: therefore, he has no place where Jesus can lay his head. It is shown to us, and for this reason the scribe is rejected, that seeing the greatness of the signs, he wanted to follow the Savior in order to seek profits from the miracles of his works, desiring the same thing that Simon Magus had wanted to purchase from Peter (Acts 8). Such faith, therefore, is rightly condemned by the Lord's judgment, and he says to him: Why do you desire to follow me for the sake of wealth and worldly gain, when I am so poor that I don't even have a place to stay, and I don't have a roof of my own to use?


<h2 id='tocuniq128'>(Vers. 21.)</h2>

(Verse 21.) Another of his disciples said to him: Lord, allow me first to go and bury my father. What is the similarity between a scribe and a disciple? The former calls him master, the latter confesses him Lord. The former desires to go and bury his father due to a matter of piety: the latter promises to follow him wherever he goes, not seeking a master, but seeking gain from the master.

<h2 id='tocuniq129'>(Vers. 22.)</h2>

(Verse 22.) But Jesus said to him: follow me, and let the dead bury their own dead. Whoever does not believe is dead. But if a dead person buries the dead, we should not be concerned with the dead, but with the living: lest while we are anxious about the dead, we ourselves also be called dead.

<h2 id='tocuniq130'>(Vers. 23.)</h2>

(Verse 23) And when he got into the boat, his disciples followed him. And behold, there was a great storm on the sea, so that the boat was being covered by the waves. The fifth sign he performed was when he got into the boat from Capernaum, he commanded the winds and the sea. The sixth sign was when he gave power to the demons in the region of the Gerasenes and they entered into the pigs. The seventh sign was when he entered his own city and healed a paralytic man lying on a bed. For the first is the paralyzed boy of the centurion.

<h2 id='tocuniq131'>(Vers. 24, 25.)</h2>

(Verse 24, 25.) But he was sleeping. And they came to him and woke him up, saying, 'Lord, save us! We are perishing!' And Jesus said to them, 'Why are you afraid, O you of little faith?' We read in the story of Jonah (Jonah 1) the foreshadowing of this sign, when, as others were in danger, he himself was secure, asleep, and awakened; and by the power and mystery of his passion, he saved those who woke him up.

<h2 id='tocuniq132'>(Vers. 26.)</h2>

(Verse 26) Then, rising up, he commanded the winds and the sea, and there was a great calm. And from this place we understand that all creatures feel the Creator. For those which are rebuked and those which are commanded, feel the one who commands: not by the error of the heretics, who think that all things are animate; but by the majesty of the Creator, which to us is imperceptible, but to them is perceptible.

<h2 id='tocuniq133'>(Vers. 27-29.)</h2>

(Verses 27-29.) And the men marveled, saying: What kind of man is this, that even the winds and the sea obey him? And when Jesus came across the sea to the region of the Gerasenes, two men with demons met him, coming out of the tombs, so fierce that no one could pass by that way. And behold, they cried out, saying. Not the disciples, but the sailors, and others who were in the boat, marveled. But if anyone wants to argue that those who marveled were disciples, we will answer that they were rightly called men who had not yet known the power of the Savior.


<h2 id='tocuniq134'>(Vers. 30, 31.)</h2>

(Verse 30, 31.) What have we to do with you, Jesus, Son of God? Have you come here before the time to torment us? Now there was a herd of many pigs feeding not far from them. And the demons begged him, saying, 'This is not a voluntary confession, which is followed by the reward of the confessor, but a forced confession, which compels the unwilling, as if runaway slaves, to see their master after a long time: they pray for nothing else but to be spared from the beatings.' And so, when the demons saw the Lord suddenly present on earth, they believed that they had come to be judged. The presence of the Savior is torment for the demons. Some people foolishly think that the demons know the Son of God and are ignorant of the Devil; because these demons are of lesser evil than the one whose servants they are. Since all knowledge of the disciples is to be referred to the teacher, and both demons and the Devil are more suspicious of the Son of God than they are capable of understanding or knowing. No one knows the Father except the Son, and anyone to whom the Son chooses to reveal him (Matthew 11:27).

<h2 id='tocuniq135'>(Vers. 32, 33.)</h2>

(Verse 32, 33.) If you drive us out, send us into the herd of pigs. And he said to them: Go. So they came out and went into the pigs. And behold, with a great rush, the whole herd rushed down the steep bank into the sea, and they died in the water. The shepherds fled, and coming into the city, they reported all these things, and concerning those who had demons. Not because the Savior granted what the demons requested, but he said, go: so that through the destruction of the pigs, an opportunity for salvation would be given to men. For when the shepherds saw this, they immediately announced it to the city. Let Manichaeus be ashamed, if souls of humans and animals are of the same substance and from the same author, how is it that for the salvation of one man, two thousand pigs are suffocated?

<h2 id='tocuniq136'>(Vers. 34.)</h2>

(Verse 34.) And behold, the whole city went out to meet Jesus, and when they saw him, they begged him to pass through their territory. They are making this request not out of pride, as some think, but out of the humility with which they considered themselves unworthy of the Lord's presence, just as Peter fell to his knees before the Savior, saying: Depart from me, Lord, for I am a sinful man (Luke 5:8).

<h2 id='tocuniq137'>(Chap. IX.—Vers. 1, 2.)</h2>

(Chapter 9, Verses 1, 2.) And Jesus, getting into a boat, crossed over and came to his own city. And behold, they brought to him a paralyzed man lying on a bed. And when Jesus saw their faith, he said to the paralyzed man, 'Take courage, my son, your sins are forgiven.' By 'his own city' we understand Nazareth, from where he was also called Nazarene. They brought to him, as we have said before, a paralyzed man lying on a bed, because he was unable to enter himself. But Jesus, seeing not the faith of him who was being offered, but of those who were offering, said to the paralytic: Have confidence, son, your sins are forgiven you. O wondrous humility, calling despised and weak, fragmented in all the joints of his limbs, a son whom the priests did not deign to touch. Indeed, he is called a son because his sins are forgiven him. According to the tropology, sometimes the soul lying in its body, with all the powers of its limbs dissolved, is offered to the Lord to be healed by the perfect teacher. If she is healed by his mercy, she receives so much strength that she immediately carries her bed.


<h2 id='tocuniq138'>(Vers. 3, 4.)</h2>

(Ver. 3, 4.) And behold, some of the scribes said among themselves: He blasphemes. And when Jesus saw their thoughts, he said: Why do you think evil in your hearts? We read in the Prophet, saying God: I am the one who blots out your iniquities (Isaiah 43:25). Therefore the scribes, because they thought him to be a man and did not understand the words of God, accuse him of blasphemy. But the Lord, seeing their thoughts, shows himself to be God who can know the secrets of the heart, and he speaks in a somewhat silent manner: With the same majesty and power with which I behold your thoughts, I can also forgive sins to humans. Understand what the paralytic encounters from you.

<h2 id='tocuniq139'>(Vers. 5, 6.)</h2>

(Verses 5, 6.) What is easier to say: 'Your sins are forgiven' or 'Rise up and walk'? But so that you may know that the Son of Man has authority on earth to forgive sins,” then He said to the paralytic. There is a great difference between saying and doing. Only the one who forgives knew whether the sins of the paralytic were forgiven. But both the paralytic who rose up and those who saw him rise could approve of it. Therefore, a physical sign is given in order to prove the spiritual, although it has the same power to forgive the vices of both body and soul. And intelligence is given to us, because many bodily weaknesses occur due to sins. And perhaps your sins are forgiven first, so that with the causes of weakness removed, health may be restored.

<h2 id='tocuniq140'>(Vers. 7, 8.)</h2>

(Verses 7, 8.) Rise, take up your bed, and go to your house. And he arose, and went to his house. And when the multitudes saw it, they marveled, and glorified God, who had given such power to men. And if the paralyzed soul rises, if it regains its former strength, it carries its bed in which it lay before in pieces, and carries it to the home of its virtues.

<h2 id='tocuniq141'>(Vers. 9.)</h2>

(Verse 9) And as Jesus passed from there, he saw a man named Matthew sitting at the tax collector's booth. And he said to him, 'Follow me.' And he rose and followed him. The other evangelists, out of respect and honor for Matthew, did not want to mention his name publicly, but they said, 'Levi,' for he had two names. However, Matthew himself, according to what is commanded by Solomon, says, 'The righteous one is his own accuser at the beginning of his speech' (Prov. 18:17). And in another place: Declare your sins, that you may be justified (Isaiah 43:26). He calls Matthew and the tax collector to show those who read the Gospel that no one should despair of salvation if they have turned to better things; for he himself was suddenly changed from a tax collector to an apostle. Porphyry and Julian the Emperor argue in this place, either the incompetence of a lying historian or the foolishness of those who immediately followed the Savior, as if they unreasonably followed anyone who called them, when there were so many virtues and signs that the Apostles undoubtedly saw before they believed. Certainly, the very radiance and majesty of hidden divinity, which also shone forth in his human face, could attract those who saw it from the first sight. For if it is said that this power exists in a magnet and amber, so that it can attract rings, straws, and twigs to itself, how much more could the Lord of all creatures attract those whom he willed?

<h2 id='tocuniq142'>(Vers. 10 seq.)</h2>

(Verse 10 and following) And it happened, as he was reclining at table in the house, behold, many tax collectors and sinners came and were reclining with Jesus and his disciples. And when the Pharisees saw this, they said to his disciples, "Why does your teacher eat with tax collectors and sinners?" But when Jesus heard it, he said, "Those who are well have no need of a physician, but those who are sick. Go and learn what this means: 'I desire mercy, and not sacrifice.' For I came not to call the righteous, but sinners." They saw the tax collector who had repented of his sins and had found a place of repentance, and because of this they do not despair of salvation. They do not remain in their former vices but come to Jesus, as the Pharisees and scribes grumble. But they are repenting, as the following words of the Lord indicate, saying:

<h2 id='tocuniq143'>(Vers. 13.)</h2>

(Verse 13.) I desire mercy, and not sacrifice. For I came not to call the righteous, but sinners. Now the Lord was going to the feasts of sinners, so that he might have an opportunity to teach and provide spiritual food to his invited guests. Finally, although it is frequently mentioned that he went to feasts, nothing else is reported except what he did there, what he taught, in order to demonstrate both the humility of the Lord in going to sinners and the power of his teaching in the conversion of the penitent. But go ye and learn what that meaneth, I will have mercy, and not sacrifice: for I am not come to call the righteous, but sinners to repentance. (Matthew 9:13). And: I am not come to call the righteous, but sinners to repentance (Mark 2:17), giving testimony of the prophet, Jesus rebukes the scribes and Pharisees, who considered themselves righteous, for avoiding the company of sinners and tax collectors.

<h2 id='tocuniq144'>(Vers. 14.)</h2>

(Verse 14.) Then the disciples of John approached him, saying: Why do we and the Pharisees fast often, but your disciples do not fast? This is a proud question, full of the arrogance of the Pharisees. Certainly, if we may say so, their boastful fasting should be criticized. The disciples of John could not avoid blame, for they were slandering him, whom they knew had been preached by their teacher, and were joining with the Pharisees, whom they knew had been condemned by John, saying (above, III, 7): "You brood of vipers, who warned you to flee from the coming wrath?


<h2 id='tocuniq145'>(Vers. 15.)</h2>

(Verse 15.) And Jesus said to them: Can the children of the bridegroom mourn as long as the bridegroom is with them? But the days will come when the bridegroom will be taken away from them, and then they will fast. Christ is the bridegroom: the Church is the bride. From this holy and spiritual marriage, the Apostles are born, who cannot mourn as long as they see the bride in the bridal chamber and know that the bridegroom is with the bride. But when the wedding is over and the time of passion and resurrection has come, then the children of the bridegroom will fast." } Some believe that after forty days of the Passion, fasting should be observed: although immediately the days of Pentecost and the Holy Spirit coming indicate a feast to us. And on this occasion, Montanus, Prisca, and Maximilla also observe Lent after Pentecost, because with the spouse removed, the children of the spouse should fast. However, the custom of the Church comes to the passion of the Lord and the resurrection through the humility of the flesh, so that we may be prepared for the spiritual richness of fasting of the body. According to the tropology, it must be known that as long as the bridegroom is with us and we are in joy, we cannot fast or mourn. But when he departs from us because of our sins, then fasting must be observed, then mourning received.

<h2 id='tocuniq146'>(Vers. 16, 17.)</h2>

(Verse 16, 17.) However, no one puts a piece of unshrunk cloth on an old garment. For the patch pulls away from the garment, and a worse tear is made. Nor do people put new wine into old wineskins. If they do, the skins burst, the wine is spilled, and the skins are destroyed. But they put new wine into fresh wineskins, and both are preserved. These were the words he spoke to them. What he meant was, until someone is born again and has put off the old self, through my suffering, and has put on the new self, they cannot bear the stricter rules of fasting and self-control, so as not to lose even the faith that they seem to have now, through excessive austerity. However, he gave two examples, both of the old and the new, and of the garment. The old wineskins, we must understand, represent the scribes and the Pharisees. The new patch of clothing and the new wine represent the teachings of the Gospel, which the Jews cannot bear, lest a greater tear be made. The Galatians also desired to do something similar, mixing the precepts of the Law with the Gospel, and putting new wine into old wineskins; but the Apostle speaks to them: O foolish Galatians! Who has bewitched you into not obeying the truth? (Galatians III, 1). Therefore, the Evangelical message must be imparted to the apostles rather than the scribes and Pharisees who, corrupted by the traditions of their ancestors, could not uphold the sincerity of Christ's teachings. For the purity of a virgin soul is different from that which has been tainted by the contamination of previous vices, as are the impurities of someone who has succumbed to the lusts of many.

<h2 id='tocuniq147'>(Vers. 18, 19.)</h2>

(Verse 18, 19.) Look, one ruler approached and worshipped him, saying: My daughter has just died, but come, lay your hand upon her, and she will live. And Jesus rose and followed him, and so did his disciples. This is the eighth sign, in which the ruler asks for his daughter to be raised, not wanting to be excluded from the mystery of true circumcision; but a woman with a flow of blood enters, and is healed in the eighth place, so that the ruler's daughter comes in ninth, according to what is said in the Psalms: Ethiopia will stretch out her hands to God. (Ps. 68:32). And so, all Israel will be saved; as it is written: 'The deliverer will come out of Zion; he will turn away ungodliness from Jacob. And this is my covenant with them when I take away their sins.' (Romans 11:25-26)

<h2 id='tocuniq148'>(Vers. 20.)</h2>

(Verse 20) And behold, a woman who had been suffering from a flow of blood for twelve years came up behind him and touched the fringe of his garment. In the 53rd Gospel according to Luke, it is written that the ruler's daughter was twelve years old (Luke 8). Note therefore that at that time this woman, that is, the Gentile people, began to get sick, when the people of the Jewish race believed. For unless vice is shown by comparison of virtues. But this woman, who was flowing with blood, does not approach the Lord in the house or in the city, because according to the Law she was excluded from the cities (Lev. 15, Num. 5); but on the road, as the Lord was walking, so that while He went to another, another might be healed. Hence the apostles also say: It was necessary to preach the word of God to you; but since you have judged yourselves unworthy of salvation, we turn to the Gentiles (Acts 13, 46).

<h2 id='tocuniq149'>(Vers. 21.)</h2>

(Verse 21.) For she said within herself: If I shall touch only his garment, I shall be saved. But Jesus, turning and seeing her, said: According to the Law, whoever touches a woman who is menstruating or flowing with blood is unclean (Leviticus 20:25). She touches the Lord for this reason, so that she herself may be cured of the defect of blood.

<h2 id='tocuniq150'>(Vers. 22.)</h2>

(Verse 22.) Trust, daughter, your faith has saved you: and the woman was saved from that hour. Therefore, daughter, because your faith has saved you. He did not say, your faith will save you, but has saved you. In what you believed, you have already been made whole.

<h2 id='tocuniq151'>(Vers. 23.)</h2>

(Verse 23) And when Jesus came into the ruler's house: and saw the minstrels and the people making a noise, He said: Give place, for the girl is not dead, but sleeps. And they laughed him to scorn. And when the multitude was put forth, he went in, and took her by the hand. And the maid arose." }

<h2 id='tocuniq152'>(Vers. 24.)</h2>

(Verse 24.) Step back, for the girl is not dead, but sleeping. And they laughed at him. Because all things live for God.

<h2 id='tocuniq153'>(Vers. 25.)</h2>

(Verse 25) And when the crowd had been expelled, he entered. For they were not worthy to witness the mystery of the resurrection, as they had ridiculed the one who raises the unworthy with insults.

<h2 id='tocuniq154'>(Vers. 26.)</h2>

(Verse 26.) And he took her by the hand. And the girl arose: And this news went throughout all that land. Unless the hands of the Jews, which are filled with blood, are first cleansed, their synagogue will not rise again.

<h2 id='tocuniq155'>(Vers. 27.)</h2>

(Verse 27.) And as Jesus passed on from there, two blind men followed him, crying out and saying, 'Have mercy on us, Son of David.' And when he entered the house, the blind men came to him, and Jesus said to them, 'Do you believe that I am able to do this?' They said to him, 'Yes, Lord.' Then he touched their eyes, saying, 'According to your faith be it done to you.' And their eyes were opened. The aforementioned sign that we have explained about the daughter of the ruler and the hemorrhaging (or sick) woman is followed by this: that as in those cases there was death and weakness, here blindness is demonstrated. For both peoples were blind, as the Lord passed through this world and desired to return to his home. Unless they confess and say, 'Have mercy on us, Son of David,' and Jesus asks, 'Do you believe that I am able to do this?' Respond to him: Certainly, Lord, he does not receive his former sight. In another Gospel, one blind man is mentioned, with torn garments, sitting in Jericho, who is forbidden by the apostles to cry out; but he receives his healing through his impudence (Mark 10). This passage properly belongs to the crowd of Gentiles, and it should be explained in its own volume.

<h2 id='tocuniq156'>(Vers. 28, 29.)</h2>

(Verse 28, 29.) Have mercy on us, Son of David. And when he entered the house, the blind approached him, and Jesus said to them: Do you believe that I can do this for you? They said to him: Certainly, Lord. Then he touched their eyes, saying: Let it be done for you according to your faith. And their eyes were opened. Let Marcion and Manichaeus, and the other heretics who tear apart the Old Testament, hear and learn that the Savior is called the Son of David; for if he were not born in the flesh, how would he be called the son of David?


<h2 id='tocuniq157'>(Vers. 30, 31.)</h2>

(Ver. 30, 31.) And Jesus warned them, saying: Take care that no one knows. But when they went out, they spread the news about him throughout that whole land. And the Lord, in order to avoid the glory of boasting, had commanded this. And they, because of the gratitude of the miracle, cannot keep silent about the goodness. Therefore, it is noted that something contrary was commanded between them. These blind men are healed in the tenth place.

<h2 id='tocuniq158'>(Vers. 32.)</h2>

(Verse 32) And when they had departed, behold, they brought to Him a mute man possessed with a demon. And when the demon was cast out, the mute spoke. The eleventh mute received his tongue to speak. However, what is called 'κωφὸν' in Greek is more commonly understood in ordinary speech as 'deaf' rather than 'mute'. But it is the custom of the Scriptures to use 'κωφὸν' interchangeably, meaning either 'mute' or 'deaf'. Spiritually, just as the blind receive sight, so too are the mute able to speak as their tongue is loosened, to confess the One whom they had previously denied.


<h2 id='tocuniq159'>(Vers. 33, 34.)</h2>

(Vers. 33, 34) And the crowds marveled, saying, 'Never has anything like this been seen in Israel.' But the Pharisees said, 'He casts out demons by the prince of demons.' The crowd acknowledges the works of God and says, 'Never has anything like this been seen in Israel.' In the crowd, there is the confession of nations. However, because the Pharisees could not deny the power of God, they slander his works and say, 'He casts out demons by the prince of demons,' thus demonstrating the unbelief of the Jews through their slander to this day.


<h2 id='tocuniq160'>(Vers. 35.)</h2>

(Verse 35.) And Jesus went around all the cities and villages, teaching in their synagogues and preaching the Gospel of the kingdom, and healing every disease and every sickness. You see that he preached the Gospel equally to both villages and cities, that is, to both great and small, so that he would not consider the power of nobles but the salvation of believers. He went around the cities, having this work that the Father had commanded: and he had this hunger, to save the unbelievers with his teaching. But he taught in the synagogues and villages the Gospel of the kingdom: and after preaching and teaching he cured every sickness and every infirmity; so that those whom his words did not persuade, his actions did persuade. It is said specifically of the Lord: Curing every sickness and every infirmity, for nothing is impossible for him.

<h2 id='tocuniq161'>(Vers. 36.)</h2>

(Verse 36) But seeing the crowds, he had compassion on them, because they were harassed and helpless, like sheep without a shepherd. Then he said to his disciples, 'The distress of the flock and the sheep and the crowds is the fault of the shepherds and the vice of the leaders.' Hence, it follows.

<h2 id='tocuniq162'>(Vers. 37, 38.)</h2>

(Verse 37, 38.) The harvest is indeed plentiful, but the laborers are few. Therefore, pray to the Lord of the harvest to send out laborers into his harvest. The abundant harvest represents a multitude of people: 56 few laborers, a scarcity of workers. And he commands them to pray to the Lord of the harvest to send out laborers into his harvest. These are the workers of whom the Psalmist speaks, saying: 'Those who sow in tears will reap with shouts of joy.' They went out, they went, and they wept, carrying their seeds. But when they come, they will come with joy, carrying their sheaves. (Psalm 126:7-8). And to speak more clearly, the abundant harvest is the whole crowd of believers. However, there are few workers, and the apostles, and those who imitate them, are sent to the harvest.

<h2 id='tocuniq163'>(Chap. X.—Vers. 1.)</h2>

(Chapter X, Verse 1) And having summoned his twelve disciples, he gave them power over unclean spirits, to cast them out and to heal every sickness and every disease. The kind and merciful Lord and Master does not withhold his powers from his servants and disciples. And just as he healed every sickness and every disease, he also gave his apostles the power to heal every sickness and every disease among the people. But there is a great difference between having and giving, donating and receiving. Whatever he does, he acts by the power of the Lord: they, if they do anything, confess their weakness and the power of the Lord, saying: In the name of Jesus, rise up and walk (Acts 3:6). However, it should be noted that in the twelfth place, the power of performing miracles is granted to the apostles.

<h2 id='tocuniq164'>(Vers. 2.)</h2>

(Ver. 2.) However, the names of the twelve apostles are as follows. The catalog of the apostles is given in order to exclude those who are to become false apostles.

<h2 id='tocuniq165'>(Vers. 3.)</h2>

(Verse 3) The first is Simon, who is called Peter, and Andrew his brother; James the son of Zebedee, and John his brother. Philip and Bartholomew, Thomas and Matthew the tax collector, James the son of Alphaeus, and Thaddaeus. The order and merit of the apostles was distributed by him who probes the secrets of the heart. The first is written Simon, called Peter; to distinguish him from the other Simon, who is called the Cananaean, from the village of Cana in Galilee, where the Lord turned water into wine (John 2). He also calls James the son of Zebedee, because another James, the son of Alphaeus, follows. And he associates pairs of apostles. He joins together Peter and Andrew as brothers, not so much in flesh as in spirit. James and John, who left the bread of the body behind, followed the true Father. Philip and Bartholomew, as well as Thomas and Matthew the tax collector. The other evangelists, in the order of names, first mention Matthew; and then Thomas, but they do not attribute the name of tax collector, so as not to appear to mark the Evangelist by recalling his former occupation. Truly, as we said above, he uses himself and calls himself a sinner, so that where sin has abounded, grace may also superabound (Rom. V, 20).

<h2 id='tocuniq166'>(Vers. 4.)</h2>

(Verse 4.) Simon the Cananean. He is the one who is written about in another Gospel (Luke VI) as the Zealot. Cana indeed is interpreted as zeal. Thaddeus the apostle, as the Church's history teaches, was sent to Edessa to King Abgarus of Osrhoene, who is called Judas the son of James by the evangelist Luke, and elsewhere is called Lebbaeus (Acts I), which is interpreted as little heart. And it is to be believed that he had a triple name: Just as Simon is also called Peter (Mark III); and the Sons of Zebedee, Boanerges (alternatively Banerges), were named because of the firmness and greatness of their faith.


And Judas Iscariot, who also betrayed him. He took his name either from the village or city where he was born, or from the tribe of Issachar: so that it could be understood that he was born for his own condemnation by a certain prophecy. For Issachar is interpreted as 'reward' in order to signify the price of the traitor.

<h2 id='tocuniq167'>(Vers. 5, 6.)</h2>

(Vers. 5, 6.) Do not go into the way of the Gentiles, and do not enter into the cities of the Samaritans. But go rather to the lost sheep of the house of Israel. This place is not contrary to the commandment that is said later: Go and teach all nations, baptizing them in the name of the Father, and of the Son, and of the Holy Spirit (Matt. XXVIII, 19). For this was commanded before the resurrection, while that was commanded after the resurrection. And it was necessary to first announce the coming of Christ to the Jews, so that they would not have a just excuse for rejecting Him; because He sent the apostles to the Gentiles and to the Samaritans. According to the tropology, it is commanded to us who are called by the name of Christ, that we do not walk in the error of the way of the Gentiles and heretics, so that as their religion is separated, so let their way of life be separated.

<h2 id='tocuniq168'>(Vers. 7, 8.)</h2>

(Vers. 7, 8.) But going forth, preach, saying: 'The kingdom of heaven is at hand.' Heal the sick, raise the dead, cleanse the lepers, cast out demons. Give freely to the country people and those without eloquence, who are uneducated and illiterate, so that no one would believe the promise of the kingdom of heaven. They promise to heal the sick, cleanse the lepers, cast out demons, in order to prove the greatness of their promises through the greatness of their signs. And because spiritual gifts (if the reward is material) always become less valuable, condemnation of greed is added.

Freely you have received, freely give. As a master and Lord, I am giving this to you without cost, and you also give it without cost, so that the grace of the Gospel may not be corrupted.

<h2 id='tocuniq169'>(Vers. 9, 10.)</h2>

(Verses 9, 10.) Do not possess gold, nor silver, nor money in your belts. Do not take a bag on the road, nor two tunics, nor sandals, nor a staff. For the worker deserves his food. Therefore, he gives these precepts to the evangelizers of the truth, to whom he had said before: Freely you have received, freely give. For if they preach in such a way that they do not accept payment, the possession of gold, silver, and money is unnecessary. For if they had gold and silver, they seemed to preach not for the sake of the salvation of men, but for the sake of profit. Nor was there any money in their purses. He who cut off wealth also cut off, almost entirely, the necessities of life, so that the apostles, the teachers of true religion, who taught that all things are governed by the providence of God, showed by their example that they thought nothing of tomorrow. No bag on the way. From this commandment he refutes the philosophers, who are commonly called Bactroperitae, because they despised the world and regarded everything as worthless, and carried a storeroom with them. Not only two tunics. In two tunics, it seems to me that a double garment is being shown. Not that in the regions of Scythia and freezing snow one should be content with just one tunic: but rather so that we understand the garment in the tunic: that we may not clothe ourselves in one thing and preserve ourselves from the fear of future events with another. Not even footwear. And Plato advised that the two highest parts of the body should not be covered, nor should we become accustomed to the softness of the head and feet. When these things have firmness, the rest are stronger. Neither a rod: Why do we seek the aid of a staff, we who have the help of the Lord? 59 And because he had sent the apostles to preach in a certain manner and speedily, and the condition of the teachers seemed difficult, he tempered the severity of the instruction with the following statement, saying: Worthy is the worker of his wages. Only take, he says, what is necessary for you in food and clothing. And the Apostle repeats: Having food and clothing, let us be content with these (1 Tim. 6:8). And in another place: But let him who is being catechized communicate the word to him who catechizes him in all good things (Gal. 6:6), so that those who reap spiritual things may make them partakers of their carnal things, not out of greed, but out of necessity. These things we have said historically. But according to the anagoge, it is not permissible for teachers to possess gold and silver, and money that is in belts. We often read gold for meaning, silver for conversation, bronze for voice; these are not permitted for us to receive from others, but are given to possess by the Lord. Nor should we accept the teachings of heretics and philosophers and perverse doctrines, nor be oppressed by the weight of the world, nor have a double mind, nor have our feet bound by deadly chains, but rather, entering the holy land, be naked; nor should we have a staff that turns into a serpent, nor rely on any support of the flesh, for such a staff is made of reed, if you press it a little bit, it breaks and pierces the hand of the one pressing on it.


<h2 id='tocuniq170'>(Vers. 11.)</h2>

(Verse 11) In whatever city or town you enter, inquire who is worthy in it, and stay there until you go out. Concerning the ordination of bishops and deacons, Paul speaks, 'Moreover, they must have a good testimony from those who are outside.' (I Tim. III, 7). When the apostles entered a new city, they could not know what kind of person he was. Therefore, a host must be chosen based on the reputation of the people and the judgment of the neighbors, so that the dignity of the preaching may not be tarnished by the infamy of the recipient. When everyone should preach, one guest is chosen, not giving a benefit to the one who is about to stay, but receiving, for it is said, who is worthy in it, that he may know himself more capable of receiving grace than giving.

<h2 id='tocuniq171'>(Vers. 12, 13.)</h2>

(Verses 12, 13.) But when you enter the house, greet it. And if the house is worthy, let your peace come upon it; but if it is not worthy, let your peace return to you. He expresses the hidden greeting of the Hebrew and Syriac language. For what is said in Greek, χαῖρε, and in Latin, ave, in the Hebrew and Syriac language is called Salom Lach or Salom Emmach, which means peace be with you. And what he commands is this: When you enter the house, greet the guest with peace, and as much as you can, settle disputes and conflicts. But if a contradiction arises, you will receive a reward for the offered peace: those who wish to have war will possess it.

<h2 id='tocuniq172'>(Vers. 14.)</h2>

(Verse 14) And whoever shall not receive you, nor hear your words, when you depart from that house or city, shake off the dust from your feet. The dust is shaken off from their feet as a testimony against them, that they entered the city and the apostolic preaching reached them. Whether the dust is shaken off so that they receive nothing from them, not even necessary sustenance, who have rejected the Gospel.


<h2 id='tocuniq173'>(Vers. 15.)</h2>

(Verse 15.) Truly I say to you, it will be more tolerable for the land of Sodom and Gomorrah on the day of judgment than for that city. If it will be more tolerable for the land of Sodom and Gomorrah ((or Gomorthea)) than for that city which did not receive the Gospel, and therefore more tolerable, because to Sodom and Gomorrah the Gospel was not preached, but to this city it was preached, and yet it did not receive the Gospel: therefore, among sinners, there are different punishments.


<h2 id='tocuniq174'>(Vers. 16.)</h2>

(Verse 16) Behold, I send you out as sheep in the midst of wolves. He calls them wolves, scribes and Pharisees, who are the clerics of the Jews.

<h2 id='tocuniq175'>(Vers. 17, 18.)</h2>

(Verse 17, 18.) Therefore be shrewd as serpents, and innocent as doves. But beware of men: for they will deliver you up in councils, and they will scourge you in their synagogues. And you will be led before governors and kings for my sake, as a testimony to them and to the Gentiles. So that they may avoid traps through prudence, and not do evil through simplicity. The shrewdness of the serpent is set as an example: because it hides its head with its whole body, and protects the part where life is. In this way, let us also guard our head, which is Christ, with our whole being at great risk. The simplicity of doves is demonstrated by the appearance of the Holy Spirit. Hence the Apostle says: Be innocent in evil (I Cor. XIV, 20).

<h2 id='tocuniq176'>(Vers. 19, 20.)</h2>

(Verse 19, 20.) But when they hand you over, do not worry about how or what you are to say; for it will be given you in that hour what you are to say. For it is not you who speak, but it is the Spirit of your Father who speaks in you. Earlier He had said: For they will hand you over to courts and to synagogues, and you will be flogged in their synagogues, and you will also be brought before governors and kings for My sake. So when they hand you over, do not worry about how or what you are to say; for it will be given you in that hour what you are to say. Moreover, Christ himself who dwells in us will speak for himself, and the grace of the Holy Spirit will be supplied in responding.

<h2 id='tocuniq177'>(Vers. 21.)</h2>

(Verse 21.) But brother will deliver brother over to death, and the father his child, and children will rise against parents and have them put to death. And you will be hated by all for my name's sake. We often see this happening during persecutions: there is no faithful affection among them, as their beliefs are different.

<h2 id='tocuniq178'>(Vers. 22.)</h2>

(Verse 22) But he who perseveres until the end, he will be saved. For it is not to begin, but to complete virtue.

<h2 id='tocuniq179'>(Vers. 23, 24.)</h2>

(Verse 23, 24.) But when they persecute you in this city, flee to another. Amen I say to you, you will not have finished going through the cities of Israel, until the Son of Man comes. A disciple is not above his teacher, nor a servant above his master. It is enough for the disciple to be like his teacher, and the servant like his master. This is to be understood in reference to that time when the apostles were being sent out to preach, to whom it is also specifically said: Do not go into the way of the Gentiles, and do not enter into the cities of the Samaritans (above, v. 5), which means that they should not fear persecution, but should avoid it. Which indeed we see (or rather, saw), in the beginning they did who believed: when a persecution arose at Jerusalem, they were scattered into all Judea, that the occasion of tribulation might become the seedbed of the Gospel. But spiritually we can say: When they persecuted us in one city, that is, in one book of the Scriptures or testimony, let us flee to other cities, that is, to other volumes. Although the persecutor may be contentious, the protection of the Savior will come before victory is granted to the adversaries.


<h2 id='tocuniq180'>(Vers. 25.)</h2>

(Verse 25) If they called the head of the household Beelzebub, how much more his household members! Therefore, do not be afraid of them. Beelzebub is an idol of Acaron, which is called in the Book of Kings the idol of flies (2 Kings 1). Beel is the same as Bel or Baal; Zebub means fly. So they named the prince of demons using the most despicable name of the idol, which means fly, because of the filthiness that destroys the sweetness of oil (Ecclesiastes 10).


<h2 id='tocuniq181'>(Vers. 26.)</h2>

(Verse 26.) For there is nothing hidden that will not be revealed, and nothing secret that will not be known. And how, in the present age, are the vices of many unknown? But concerning the future time, it is written, when God will judge the hidden things of men and will illuminate the dark places, and will make the counsels of hearts manifest. And the meaning is: Do not fear the cruelty of persecutors and the rage of blasphemers, for the day of judgment will come, in which both your virtue and their wickedness will be demonstrated.


<h2 id='tocuniq182'>(Vers. 27.)</h2>

(Verse 27) What I tell you in the dark, speak in the light; and what you hear whispered in the ear, proclaim from the housetops. What you have heard in secret, proclaim openly; what you have learned in private, speak publicly. What I have taught you in a small place in Judea, proclaim boldly in all the cities and throughout the whole world.

<h2 id='tocuniq183'>(Vers. 28.)</h2>

(Verse 28) And do not fear those who kill the body but cannot kill the soul. Rather fear him who can destroy both soul and body in hell. Truly, the soul is invisible and incorporeal, according to the denser substance of our body. However, it will certainly be punished and experience torments when it receives its original body, so that it may be punished with the one with whom it sinned.

But rather fear him who is able to destroy both soul and body in Gehenna. The name Gehenna is not found in the old books, but is first mentioned by the Savior. Let us therefore inquire what is the occasion of this discourse. We read in the third book of Kings that there was an idol of Baal near Jerusalem at the foot of Mount Moriah, where the Siloam flows, not once. This valley and the plain of the small fields were irrigated and wooded, full of delights, and a grove consecrated to the idol was in it. But the people of Israel had fallen into such great madness that they used to sacrifice animals in the deserted vicinity of the temple and overcome the strictness of religion with indulgences, and they would burn or initiate their own children with demons. And that place was called Gehenna, that is, the Valley of the Sons of Hinnom. This is written in detail in the Books of Kings (2 Kings 23), Chronicles (2 Chronicles 28), and Jeremiah (Jeremiah 7, 19, and 32). And God threatens that he will fill the place itself with the corpses of 63 dead, so that it may by no means be called Tophet and Baal, but be called Polyandrium, that is, a tomb of the dead. Therefore, the future punishments and eternal torments by which sinners are tortured are indicated by the name of this place. But we read in the Book of Job (Job 24) that there are two kinds of hell, the excessive fire and coldness.

<h2 id='tocuniq184'>(Vers. 29 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 29 onwards) Are not two sparrows sold for a penny? Yet not one of them will fall to the ground apart from your Father. And even the hairs of your head are all numbered. So do not be afraid; you are worth more than many sparrows. Therefore, whoever confesses me before men, him I will also confess before my Father who is in heaven. But whoever denies me before men, him I will also deny before my Father who is in heaven. The speech of the Lord clings to Himself, and the following depend on the previous statements. Wise reader, always beware of a superstitious understanding; so that you do not adapt the Scriptures to your own sense, but connect your sense with the Scriptures and understand what follows. Above, He had said, 'Do not fear those who kill the body but cannot kill the soul'; now He speaks as a consequence, 'Are not two sparrows sold for a penny? And not one of them will fall to the ground apart from your Father.' And there is this understanding: If small and worthless animals do not perish without God as their author, and there is providence in all things, and what is destined to perish in them does not perish without God's will: you who are eternal should not fear that you live without God's providence. This understanding and what is said above is: Look at the birds of the air, for they neither sow nor reap nor gather into barns; and yet your heavenly Father feeds them. Aren't you worth more than them? And furthermore: Consider the lilies of the field, how they grow, and so on. But if God so clothes the grass of the field, which is here today and tomorrow is thrown into the oven, how much more will he clothe you, O you of little faith! Some interpret the two sparrows as representing soul and body. Five sparrows, according to Luke (Luke XII), which are sold for two pennies, represent the senses. But how that understanding relates to the whole body of the Gospel message is not a small difficulty. But even the hairs of your head are all numbered. So do not be afraid; you are worth more than many sparrows. The clearer meaning of our previous exposition is expressed: that those who can kill the body should not be afraid, for they cannot kill the soul, since even small animals do not fall without God's knowledge, how much more so a man, who is supported by apostolic dignity! What it means when it says 'But even the hairs of your head are all numbered' shows immense providence of God towards humans, and signifies an incomprehensible affection, that nothing about us escapes God, and even small and idle words do not escape His knowledge. They mock ecclesiastical intelligence in this place, those who deny the resurrection of the flesh, as if we were to say that all the hairs that have been counted and cut by the barber will rise again, when the Savior did not say, 'But all the hairs of your head will be saved,' but 'they are numbered.' Where there is a number, the knowledge of number is demonstrated, not the preservation of the same number.

<h2 id='tocuniq185'>(Vers. 34.)</h2>

(Verse 34) Do not think that I have come to bring peace to the earth: I have not come to bring peace, but a sword. As he had said before: What I tell you in the dark, speak in the light; and what you hear whispered, proclaim on the housetops. Now he explains what follows after the preaching. By the faith of Christ, the whole world has been divided against itself: every house has had both unbelievers and believers, and therefore a good war has been sent to break the evil peace. Such is reported in Genesis that God, in opposition to rebellious men who had been moved from the East and were hastening to build a tower (Gen. XI), by which they might penetrate the heights of heaven, caused their languages to be divided. Therefore, in the psalm David prays: Scatter, O Lord, the people who desire war (Ps. LXVII, 32).

<h2 id='tocuniq186'>(Vers. 35.)</h2>

(Verse 35.) For I came to set a man at variance against his father, and the daughter against her mother, and the daughter in law against her mother in law. And a man's foes shall be they of his own household. This passage, with almost the same words, is written in the book of Micah the prophet (Micah 7). And it should be noted that whenever a testimony from the Old Testament is cited, it is important to determine whether it is just the meaning or also the wording that is being referred to.

<h2 id='tocuniq187'>(Vers. 37.)</h2>

(Verse 37.) Whoever loves father or mother more than me is not worthy of me. And whoever loves son or daughter more than me is not worthy of me. He who had said before: I did not come to bring peace, but a sword; and to divide people against father and mother, and mother-in-law, so that no one would put love of family before religion, added saying, Whoever loves father or mother more than me. And in the Song of Songs we read: Set me as a seal upon your heart (Song 2:4). This order is necessary in every affection. Love God the Father first, love the mother, love the children. But if necessity arises, that the love of parents and children is compared to the love of God, and both cannot be preserved, let there be hatred towards one's own, and piety towards God. Therefore, he did not prohibit loving the father or mother, but expressly added: Whoever loves the father or mother more than me.

<h2 id='tocuniq188'>(Vers. 38, 39.)</h2>

(Verse 38, 39.) And whoever does not take up their cross and follow me is not worthy of me. Whoever finds their life will lose it, and whoever loses their life for my sake will find it. In another Gospel it is written: Whoever does not take up their cross daily. Let us not think that the ardor of faith can be enough once, the cross must always be carried, so that we may always teach ourselves to love Christ.

<h2 id='tocuniq189'>(Vers. 40.)</h2>

(Verse 40.) Whoever receives you, receives me; and whoever receives me, receives the one who sent me. Beautiful order. He sends for preaching, teaches not to fear dangers, subjects his feelings to religion. He had taken gold above, had taken off his sword belt. The condition of the evangelists is difficult. So where did he get the resources, where did he get the necessary food? He tempers the severity of the commandments with the hope of promises. Whoever receives, he says, you, receives me; and whoever receives me, receives the one who sent me, so that in receiving the apostles, each of the believers may consider that they have received Christ.


<h2 id='tocuniq190'>(Vers. 41.)</h2>

(Verse 41.) Whoever receives a prophet in the name of a prophet will receive a prophet's reward. And whoever receives a righteous person in the name of a righteous person will receive a righteous person's reward. Whoever receives a prophet because they are a prophet, and understands their speaking about the future, will receive a prophet's reward. Therefore, the Jews, understanding the prophets in a carnal way, will not receive the reward of the prophets. Another way: In every profession, there is a mixture of weeds with wheat. He had previously said: Whoever receives you, receives me; and whoever receives me, receives the one who sent me. He had called the students to the reception of teachers. The response of the believers could have been hidden; therefore, we must also receive false prophets and the traitor Judas, and provide them with sustenance. The Lord, pre-proclaiming this, says that it is not individuals who should be received, but names; and that those who receive should not lose their reward, even if the one who is received is unworthy.

<h2 id='tocuniq191'>(Vers. 42.)</h2>

(Verse 42.) And whoever gives a drink to one of these little ones, only a cup of cold water, in the name of a disciple, amen I say to you, he will not lose his reward. We read in the prophet David: To excuse excuses in sins (Psalm 140:4): that many present their sins as legitimate occasions, so that what they do wrongfully, they may seem to do out of necessity: the Lord, who examines hearts and kidneys, observes future thoughts in each individual. He said, 'Whoever receives you, receives me.' But this commandment could be hindered by many false prophets and false preachers; he also healed this scandal, saying, 'Whoever receives a righteous person in the name of a righteous person, will receive the reward of a righteous person.' Again, another could argue and say, 'I am prohibited by poverty, my thinness keeps me, so I cannot be hospitable.' And he diluted this excuse with a very light precept, that we should offer a cup of cold water with our whole heart. He said that cold water, not hot, was the cause of poverty and lack of firewood, both in hot weather and in cold. The Apostle also advised the Galatians (as we have already mentioned) to share everything good with the one who instructs them in the word, and he encourages disciples to provide refreshment for their teachers. Because anyone could claim poverty and evade the commandment, he addresses the imminent question before it is posed, saying: Do not be deceived, God is not mocked. For whatever a man sows, that he will also reap. And the meaning is: you complain about poverty in vain; when your conscience tells you something else: you can deceive me encouragingly; but know that however much you sow, that much you will also harvest.

<h2 id='tocuniq192'>Second Book</h2>

Second Book

<h2 id='tocuniq193'>67 (Chap. XI.—Vers. 1, 2.)</h2>

Chapter 11, verses 1, 2: And it came to pass, when Jesus had finished these sayings, he departed from Galilee, and came into the coasts of Judaea beyond Jordan; And great multitudes followed him; and he healed them there. And as the disciples were ignorant, he asked where Lazarus was buried, so that they could prepare themselves for faith and witness the resurrection of the dead. In the same way, John sent his disciples to Christ to see the signs and miracles, and believe in him. But the disciples of John, in their arrogance against the Lord, and with some bitterness and envy, also demonstrated their superiority in questioning, as the Evangelist reports: Then the disciples of John approached him, saying, Why do we and the Pharisees fast often, but your disciples do not fast (cf. John 9:14)? And elsewhere: Master, to whom you have borne ((or shown)) witness at the Jordan, behold, his disciples are baptizing, and everyone is coming to him (cf. John 3:26), as if they were saying: We are being abandoned, while he is attracting a crowd.


<h2 id='tocuniq194'>(Vers. 3.)</h2>

(Verse 3.) Are you the one who is to come, or should we expect another? He does not say: You are the one who came, but rather, You are the one who is to come. And the meaning is: Send me, for I am about to descend into the underworld, whether I should announce your coming to the dead, I who have announced your coming to the living? Does it not befit the Son of God to taste death, and then send another to these sacraments?

<h2 id='tocuniq195'>(Vers. 4, 5.)</h2>

(Verses 4, 5.) And Jesus answering, said to them: Go and relate to John what you have heard and seen. The blind see, the lame walk, the lepers are cleansed, the deaf hear, the dead rise again. John had sent his disciples to ask him: Art thou he that art to come, or look we for another? Christ showeth forth his miracles, and leaveth John to his own thoughts. And Jesus making answer, said to them: Go and relate to John what you have heard and seen. The blind see, the lame walk, the lepers are cleansed, the deaf hear, the dead rise again. And what is not less than these,

The poor are evangelized. Either the poor in spirit, or certainly the poor in wealth (or works), so that there is no difference in preaching between the noble and the lowly, the rich and the poor. These affirm the rigor of the teacher, these confirm the truth of the instructor, for in his eyes, everyone who can be saved is equal. But what he says is:

<h2 id='tocuniq196'>(Vers. 6.)</h2>

(Verse 6.) Blessed is he who is not scandalized by me. He strikes down the messengers, as will be shown in the following.

<h2 id='tocuniq197'>(Vers. 7.)</h2>

(Verse 7.) But as they were going away, Jesus began to speak to the crowds about John: What did you go out into the wilderness to see? A reed shaken by the wind? But what did you go out to see? A man dressed in soft clothing? Behold, those who wear soft clothing are in kings' houses. If a harsh judgment had been passed against John, as many suppose, then why is he now being praised so highly? But because the surrounding crowd did not know the mystery of the question, and thought that John doubted Christ, whom he had pointed out with his finger, so that they understood that John was not questioning himself, but his disciples: Why, he said, do you go out into the desert? Is it perhaps to see a reed shaken by every wind, and to doubt in your mind about him whom he had previously preached? Or is it by the prickings of envy that he is forced, and his preaching seeks empty glory, so that he might gain profit from it? Why does he desire riches, so that he may abound in delicacies? He feeds on locusts and wild honey. Should he be dressed in soft clothing? The covering of his body is made from camel hair. Such food and clothing are received in the lodging of a prison, and the proclamation of truth has such a dwelling. But those who are flatterers, and pursue profits, and seek riches, and abound in pleasures, and are dressed in soft clothing, these are in the houses of kings. From which it is shown that a rigorous and austere life and preaching should avoid the courts of kings, and decline the palaces of soft people.


<h2 id='tocuniq198'>(Vers. 8.)</h2>

(Verse 8.) But why did you go out to see, a prophet? I tell you, and even more than a prophet. Among those born of women, John the Baptist is greater than the prophets, because he pointed out with his finger the one whom they had prophesied to come, saying: Behold the Lamb of God, behold he who takes away the sins of the world. And because to the privilege of prophethood the reward also came to John the Baptist, that he should baptize his Lord, it follows the increase of merits, making a testimony of Malachi, in whom even an angel is foretold (Malachi II). However, we cannot say that the term 'angel' here refers to John by nature, but by the dignity of his office, that is, a messenger who announced the coming of the Lord.

<h2 id='tocuniq199'>(Vers. 11.)</h2>

(Verse 11.) Truly I say to you, among those born of women there has not risen anyone greater than John the Baptist. Among those born of women, I tell you, no one is greater than him. He is greater than those who are born of women and of the union of a man and a woman, and greater than he who is born of the Virgin and the Holy Spirit. Although when he said, 'No one greater has risen among those born of women than John the Baptist,' he did not elevate John above the other prophets and patriarchs and all other men, but he considered them equal to John. For it does not immediately follow that if others are not greater, that he is greater than others; but rather that he has equality with the other saints.

But whoever is least in the kingdom of heaven is greater than he. Many want to understand this about the Savior, that whoever is least in time, is greater in dignity. But let us simply understand: that every saint, who is now with God, is greater than he who is still engaged in battle. For it is one thing to possess the crown of victory, another to still fight in the field. Some want to accept that the last angel in heaven, serving the Lord, is better than any first man who dwells on earth.


<h2 id='tocuniq200'>(Vers. 12.)</h2>

(Verse 12) But from the days of John the Baptist until now the kingdom of heaven suffers violence, and the violent take it by force. For if John had come to you in the way of righteousness, then you would have repented; but I tell you, it shall be more tolerable for Sodom in the Day of Judgment than for you. The kingdom of heaven is forcibly advancing, and the forceful ones seize it. For truly, great is the force, that we, who are born on earth, seek the heavenly throne and possess it through virtue, which we did not obtain through nature.


<h2 id='tocuniq201'>(Vers. 13.)</h2>

(Verse 13) For all the prophets and the Law prophesied until John. Not that after John the Prophets are excluded. For we read in the Acts of the Apostles (Acts 11:21) that Agabus prophesied, as well as the four daughters of Philip. But what the Law and the prophets, which we read in writing, have prophesied, they have foretold about the Lord. Therefore, when it is said, 'All the prophets and the Law prophesied until John,' it indicates the time of Christ, so that John's coming would show that the one whom they said would come had come.


<h2 id='tocuniq202'>(Vers. 14, 15.)</h2>

(Vers. 14, 15.) And if you are willing to receive, he is Elijah who is to come. He who has ears to hear, let him hear. The statement, 'If you are willing to receive, he is Elijah,' is to be understood as mystical and requiring understanding, as the following words of the Lord indicate, saying: He who has ears to hear, let him hear. For if the meaning were clear and the sentiment evident, why would it be necessary for us to be prepared for understanding? Therefore, John is called Elijah, not according to foolish philosophers and certain heretics who introduce the concept of transmigration, but because, according to another testimony of the Gospel, he came in the spirit and power of Elijah, having the same holy Spirit or grace, or measure. But the strictness of life and the austere mind of Elijah and John are similar. For Elijah lived in the desert, and so did John: Elijah was girded with a leather belt, and John had a similar belt.
