Elijah, because he accused King Ahab and Jezebel of impiety, was compelled to flee (3 Kings 19); and John, because he accused Herod and Herodias of unlawful marriages, was beheaded. Some think that John is called Elijah because just as Elijah will precede the second coming of the Savior according to Malachi, and will announce the coming Judge, so John did in the first coming; and both are messengers of either the first coming of the Lord or the second.


<h2 id='tocuniq203'>(Vers. 16 seq.)</h2>

(Vera. 16 seq.) To what shall I compare this generation? It is like children sitting in the marketplace, who call to their companions and say: 'We played the flute for you, and you did not dance; we mourned to you, and you did not lament.' For John came neither eating nor drinking, and they say, 'He has a demon.' The Son of Man came eating and drinking, and they say, 'Look, a glutton and a winebibber, a friend of tax collectors and sinners.' And wisdom is justified by her children. To the boys sitting in the forum and shouting and saying to their peers: We have sung to you, but you have not danced; we have mourned, but you have not wailed; the generation of the Jews is compared, as the Scripture says: To whom shall I compare this generation? It is like the boys sitting in the forum, and so on. Therefore, free intelligence and passive interpretation of allegories are not attributed to us, but whatever we are about to say about the boys is to be referred to the likeness of the generation. You were the children who sit in the marketplace, of whom Isaiah speaks: Behold, I and the children whom God has given to me (Isa. VIII, 18). And in the eighteenth psalm (Verse 8): The testimony of the Lord is faithful, giving wisdom to little ones. And elsewhere: Out of the mouths of babes and sucklings you have perfected praise (Ps. VIII, 3). Therefore, these children sat in the forum, or ἐν ἀγορᾶς, which is more significantly said in Greek, where many things are for sale. And because the people of the Jews did not want to listen, they not only spoke to them but shouted with full throats: We sang to you, and you did not dance; we called you to do good works to our song, and to dance to our pipe, just as David danced before the Ark of the Lord (2 Samuel 6), and you did not want to. We lamented, and we provoked you to repentance, and you did not want to do this either, despising both preaching, both the exhortation to virtues, and repentance after sins. It is not surprising that you have despised both the fasting of God, and also fullness in the same way. 72 If you prefer fasting, why did John displease you? If you prefer indulgence, why did the Son of Man displease you? You call the one possessed by a demon and the other a glutton and a drunkard. Therefore, because you refused to accept both forms of discipline, wisdom has been justified by her children; that is, by God's dispensation and teaching. And I, who am the power and wisdom of God, have been deemed just by my apostolic children, to whom the Father has revealed the things that had been hidden from the wise and prudent. In some Gospels it is read: Wisdom is justified by her works (Luke 7:35). For indeed, wisdom does not seek the testimony of words, but of works.

<h2 id='tocuniq204'>(Vers. 20.)</h2>

(Verse 20) Then he began to reproach the cities where most of his miracles had been performed, because they did not repent. The reproach of the cities of Chorazin and Bethsaida and Capernaum is set forth in this chapter. And the reason he reproached them was that after performing many miracles and signs, they did not repent.

<h2 id='tocuniq205'>(Vers. 21, 22.)</h2>

(Verse 21, 22) Woe to you, Chorazin; woe to you, Bethsaida: for if the mighty works had been done in Tyre and Sidon, which have been done in you, they would have repented long ago in sackcloth and ashes. But I say to you, it will be more tolerable for Tyre and Sidon at the day of judgment than for you. Chorazin and Bethsaida, cities of Galilee, are mourned by the Savior, because after so many signs and wonders they did not repent, and Tyre and Sidon, idolatrous and sinful cities, are preferred over them."  } However, they are preferred because Tyre and Sidon have trampled only the natural law, but these, after transgressing the natural law, have also disregarded the signs that were performed among them. We are looking for where it is written that the Lord performed signs in Chorazin and Bethsaida. Above, we read: And he went around all the cities and villages, teaching in their synagogues, and healing every disease and sickness, and so on (Above, IV, 23). Therefore, among the other cities and villages, it is to be assumed that the Lord also performed signs in Chorazin and Bethsaida.


<h2 id='tocuniq206'>(Vers. 23.)</h2>

(Verse 23) And you, Capernaum, will you be exalted to heaven? No, you will be brought down to Hades! In another version, we find: And you, Capernaum, who were exalted to heaven, will be brought down to the depths of Hades. And there are two ways to understand this. Either you will descend to Hades because you have resisted my preaching in the most arrogant manner. Or, because you were exalted to heaven by my hospitality, and by my signs and miracles, having such a great privilege, you will be punished with even greater torments, because you refuse to believe in them as well.


<h2 id='tocuniq207'>(Vers. 23, 24.)</h2>

(Verse 23, 24) For if the miracles that have been done in you had been done in Sodom (or Sidon), they would have remained until this day. However, I tell you that the land of Sodom will be treated more lightly on the day of judgment than you. Let the wise reader ask and say: if Tyre, Sidon, and Sodom were able to repent at the preaching of the Savior and the signs of miracles, they are not at fault for not believing; rather, the fault lies in the one who does not wish to preach repentance to those who will act. To which an easy and open response is: to be ignorant of the judgments of God, and to not know the sacraments of His dispensations. It was the purpose of the Lord not to exceed the boundaries of Judea, so as not to give the Pharisees and priests a just occasion for persecution. Therefore, before His passion, He commanded the apostles: Do not go on the way of the Gentiles, and do not enter the cities of the Samaritans (Matthew 10:5). Therefore, Chorazin and Bethsaida are condemned because they refused to believe in the present Lord. Tyre and Sidon are justified because they believed in his apostles. Do not seek the times when you behold the salvation of the believers. In Capernaum, however, which is interpreted as the most beautiful city, unbelieving Jerusalem is condemned, to whom it is said through Ezekiel: Sodom is justified because of you (Ezek. XVI, 52).

<h2 id='tocuniq208'>(Vers. 25.)</h2>

(Verse 25.) At that time, Jesus responded and said: I will confess to You, Father, Lord of heaven and earth. Confession, not always repentance, but also signifies thanksgiving; as we often read in the psalms. Let those who accuse the Savior of not being born but created hear that He calls His Father Lord of heaven and earth. For if He Himself is a creature, and a creature can call its creator father, it would have been foolish not to also call the Lord of Himself and of heaven and earth, or the Father in the same way.


74 Because you have hidden these things from the wise and understanding, and have revealed them to little children. Thanks and rejoices in the Father, because the coming of his apostles has revealed the sacraments, which the scribes and Pharisees, who consider themselves wise, have ignored, and in their own sight have acted prudently. Wisdom is justified by her children.

<h2 id='tocuniq209'>(Vers. 26.)</h2>

(Verse 26.) Yes, Father, because it was pleasing before you. Speaking with affectionate persuasion to the Father, that the begun favor may be completed in the apostles.

<h2 id='tocuniq210'>(Vers. 27.)</h2>

(Verse 27) All things have been handed over to me by my Father. And understand mystically the one who hands over the Father, and the one who receives the Son. Otherwise, if we want to feel according to our frailty, when the one receiving begins to have, the one who gave will begin not to have. However, all things handed over to him are not to be understood as heaven, and earth, and the elements, and the others which he himself made and established: but those who have access to the Father through the Son, and who were previously rebellious, began to feel God afterwards.


And no one knows the Son except the Father, nor does anyone know the Father except the Son, and to whomever the Son wills to reveal Him. Let Eunomius be ashamed for claiming to have such knowledge of the Father and the Son as they have of each other. But if he insists on this, and consoles himself in his madness, let him consider: And to whomever the Son wills to reveal Him. It is one thing to know by the equality of nature what you know, and another by the graciousness of the revealer.

<h2 id='tocuniq211'>(Vers. 28, 29.)</h2>

(Verse 28, 29.) Come to me, all you who labor and are burdened, and I will refresh you. Take up my yoke upon you, and learn from me, because I am gentle and humble of heart; and you will find rest for your souls. The Prophet Zacharias testifies that the burdens of sin are heavy, saying, 'iniquity sits upon a talent of lead' (Zacch. 5). And the Psalmist laments, 'My iniquities are weighed down upon me' (Psal. 37:6). Indeed, it certainly invites those who were oppressed by the heavy burden of the Law to the grace of the Gospel.

<h2 id='tocuniq212'>(Vers. 30.)</h2>

(Verse 30.) For my yoke is easy, and my burden is light. How is the Gospel easier than the Law, when in the Law there is condemnation for murder, but in the Gospel there is condemnation for anger? By what rationale is the grace of the Gospel easier, when in the Law there is adultery, but in the Gospel there is punishment for desire? In the Law there are many commandments, which the Apostle teaches cannot be fully fulfilled (Acts 15). In the Law, works are required, and whoever does them shall live by them (Ezekiel 20:11). In the gospel, the will is sought: even if it does not have the desired effect, it does not lose its reward. The gospel commands what we are able to do: namely, not to desire. This is within our power. The law does not punish the will, it punishes the action, so that you do not commit adultery. Imagine a virgin who is forced into prostitution during a persecution. In the gospel, she is accepted because she did not sin willingly, but in the law she is rejected as if corrupted.


<h2 id='tocuniq213'>(Chap. XII.—Vers. 1.)</h2>

(Chapter 12, Verse 1) At that time, Jesus went through the grainfields on the Sabbath; His disciples were hungry and began to pluck heads of grain and eat. In another Gospel, we read that because of their insistent hunger, they didn't even have a place to eat, and so they were hungry like any other people (Mark 2 and Luke 6). The fact that they rubbed the heads of grain with their hands and satisfied their hunger is a sign of a stricter way of life; they sought simple foods, not prepared feasts.


<h2 id='tocuniq214'>(Vers. 2.)</h2>

(Verse 2) But the Pharisees, seeing this, said to him: Look, your disciples are doing what is not lawful on the Sabbath. Note that the first apostles of the Savior destroyed the observance of the Sabbath, against the Ebionites, who, while accepting the other apostles, reject Paul as a violator of the law.

<h2 id='tocuniq215'>(Vers. 3, 4.)</h2>

(Verses 3, 4.) But he said to them: Have you not read what David did when he was hungry, and those who were with him: how he entered the house of God and ate the bread of the presence, which it was not lawful for him to eat, nor for those who were with him, but only for the priests? To refute the Pharisees' accusation, he recalls an old story, when David, fleeing from Saul, came to Nob and was received by the priest Ahimelech, and he asked for food. Since he did not have any ordinary bread, Ahimelech gave him consecrated bread, which was not allowed to be eaten except by the priests and Levites alone. And he only asked if there were children of the world born from women: and when he answered that from yesterday and the day before yesterday, he did not hesitate to give bread, considering it better to deliver people from the danger of hunger, as the prophet says: I desire mercy, and not sacrifice (Hosea, VI, 6), than to offer sacrifice to God. For a merciful offering is pleasing to God, and it is the salvation of men. Therefore, the Lord opposes and says: If even David, who is holy, and the high priest Achimelech are not reproached by you, although they have both transgressed the commandment of the Law with probable excuse, and hunger is the cause, why do you not approve the same hunger in the apostles, which you approve in others? Although there is also a great difference in this. Those people rub the spikes in their hands on Saturday, those Levite ate bread, and they approached the solemnity of the Sabbath and the days of the New Moon, on which he was asked to flee from the royal palace. Note that neither David nor his servants took the bread of the offering until they answered that they were clean from women.

<h2 id='tocuniq216'>(Vers. 5.)</h2>

(Verse 5.) Have you not read in the Law that on the Sabbath the priests in the temple violate the Sabbath and yet are without guilt? But I tell you, the disciples have been falsely accused, for they have passed through the fields and have crushed the heads of grain out of necessity due to hunger, while you yourselves violate the Sabbath in the temple by sacrificing animals, slaughtering bulls, and burning offerings on a heap of wood. And according to another Gospel (John 6), you even circumcise infants on the Sabbath, so that while you desire to keep another Law, you destroy the Sabbath. However, the Laws of God are never contrary to themselves. And wisely, where the disciples could be accused of transgression, David and Achimelech cite examples followed: but a true and unfounded violation of the Sabbath is attributed to those who had committed slander.

<h2 id='tocuniq217'>(Vers. 6.)</h2>

(Verse 6.) But I tell you that here is something greater than the temple. Here, not a pronoun but an adverb of place; that the place may be greater than the temple, which holds the Lord of the temple.

<h2 id='tocuniq218'>(Vers. 7.)</h2>

(Verse 7) But if you knew what this means, 'I desire mercy, and not sacrifice' (Hosea 6:6): you would never have condemned the innocent. We have already explained what it means, 'I desire mercy, and not sacrifice.' But what follows, 'you would never have condemned the innocent,' refers to the apostles. And the meaning is this: If you approved of Achimelech showing mercy to David and his men who were in danger of starvation, then why do you condemn my disciples who have done nothing of the sort?


<h2 id='tocuniq219'>(Vers. 8.)</h2>

(Verse 8.) And when He had passed from there, He came into their synagogue. And behold, there was a man with a withered hand. This is the thirteenth miracle, which is performed in the synagogue. And it should be noted that the withered hand was healed not on a journey or outside, but in the gathering of the Jews.

<h2 id='tocuniq220'>(Vers. 9.)</h2>

(Ver. 9.) And they questioned him, saying: Is it lawful to heal on the sabbath day? That they might accuse him. But he had already defended himself against the accusation of the Pharisees regarding the healing on the sabbath day, using a convincing example, so now they want to slander him. And they ask whether it is lawful to heal on the sabbath day, so that if he does not heal, they can accuse him of cruelty or weakness; but if he does heal, they can accuse him of transgression.

<h2 id='tocuniq221'>(Vers. 10 seqq.)</h2>

(Ver. 10 and following) But he said to them: Which one of you, if he has one sheep and it falls into a pit on the Sabbath, will not take hold of it and lift it out? How much more valuable is a man than a sheep! Therefore, it is lawful to do good on the Sabbath. In this way, he resolved the proposed question, to condemn those who were asking out of greed. If you, he said, hurry to rescue a sheep or any other animal that falls into a pit on the Sabbath, not because of the animal, but because of your own greed, how much more should I, who is much better than a sheep, set free a man!" }


<h2 id='tocuniq222'>(Vers. 13.)</h2>

(Verse 13) Then he said to the man: Stretch out your hand. And he stretched it out, and his health was restored as the other. In the Gospel used by the Nazarenes and Ebionites (which we have recently translated from Hebrew into Greek, and which is called by many the authentic Gospel of Matthew), this man, who has a withered hand, is described as a mason, praying for help in these words: I was a mason, seeking my livelihood with my hands. I pray to you, Jesus, to restore my health, so that I may not shamefully beg for food. Until the coming of the Savior, the hand of God was dry in the synagogue of the Jews, and His works were not done in it. But after He came into the world, His right hand was given back to the believing apostles, and the former work was restored.

<h2 id='tocuniq223'>(Vers. 14.)</h2>

(Verse 14.) But the Pharisees, going out, plotted against him how they might destroy him. The envy is the cause that they contrive a snare for the Lord. For what had he done, that he might provoke the Pharisees to his own death? Surely it was because he had stretched out his hand. For who among the Pharisees has not stretched out his hand on the Sabbath day, carrying food and extending the cup, and all other things that are necessary for sustenance? Therefore, if to stretch out one's hand and lift up food or drink on the Sabbath is not a crime, why do they accuse him of this when they themselves are being reproved for doing the same, especially since this carpenter has not carried anything like that, but has only stretched out his hand in accordance with the commandment of the Lord?


<h2 id='tocuniq224'>(Vers. 15 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 15 and following) But Jesus, knowing this, withdrew from there, and many followed him, and he healed them all. And he commanded them, not to make him known, so that what was spoken by the prophet Isaiah might be fulfilled, saying, Knowing their plots, that they wanted to destroy their Savior, he withdrew from there, in order to remove from the Pharisees the opportunity for impiety against him.

<h2 id='tocuniq225'>(Vers. 18.)</h2>

(Verse 18) Behold my servant, whom I have chosen; my beloved, in whom my soul is well pleased. I will put my Spirit upon him, and he will proclaim justice to the Gentiles. He will not contend, nor cry out. This is spoken by the Father through the prophet Isaiah: I will put my Spirit upon him (Isaiah 42:1). The Spirit is not placed upon the Word of God or upon the Only Begotten, who proceeds from the Father's bosom, but upon him, of whom it is said: Behold my servant (Ibid.)." }


<h2 id='tocuniq226'>(Vers. 19.)</h2>

(Verse 19.) And no one will hear his voice in the streets. For the way is broad and spacious that leads to destruction, and many enter through it (Above VIII). Those who do not hear the voice of the Savior are many, because they are not on the narrow path, but on the spacious one.

<h2 id='tocuniq227'>(Vers. 20, 21.)</h2>

(Verse 20, 21.) He will not break a bruised reed, and he will not extinguish smoking flax, until he brings forth judgment unto victory. And in his name the Gentiles will hope. He who does not extend his hand to the sinner, nor bears the burden of his brother, breaks a bruised reed. And he who despises a small spark of faith in the little ones, extinguishes smoking flax. Christ did neither of these things; for this reason he came, to save what was lost.


<h2 id='tocuniq228'>(Vers. 22.)</h2>

(Verse 22.) Then a demon-possessed man who was blind and mute was brought to him, and he healed him so that the man could both speak and see. All the crowds were astonished and said, 'Could this be the Son of David?' But when the Pharisees heard this, they said, 'This man does not cast out demons except by Beelzebul, the ruler of the demons.' Three signs were performed at once in this man: the blind could see, the mute could speak, and the one possessed by a demon was set free. This was done in a physical sense at that time, but it is also fulfilled daily in the conversion of believers, as they are freed from the power of the demon and first see the light of faith, then open their mouths in praise of God.


<h2 id='tocuniq229'>(Vers. 25.)</h2>

(Verse 25.) But Jesus, knowing their thoughts, said to them: Every kingdom divided against itself will be made desolate, and every city or house divided against itself will not stand. The crowds were amazed and confessed that he who performed such great signs was the son of David. But the Pharisees attributed the works of God to the prince of demons. To them, the Lord did not respond to their words, but to their thoughts, so that they might be compelled to believe in the power of him who could see the secrets of their hearts.


<h2 id='tocuniq230'>(Vers. 26.)</h2>

(Verse 26.) And if Satan casts out Satan, he is divided against himself; so how then will his kingdom stand? A kingdom and a city cannot stand divided against themselves; but just as unity makes small things grow, so discord destroys great things. Therefore, if Satan fights against himself, and a demon is an enemy of a demon, then the end of the world should have already come; so that there would be no place for opposing powers, whose war is peace among humans. But if you think, O Scribes and Pharisees, that the casting out of demons is by the obedience of their prince, so that they may deceive ignorant men by deceitful simulation, what can you say about the healings of bodies which the Lord has performed? It is something else if the weaknesses of limbs and the signs of spiritual virtues are also assigned to demons.

<h2 id='tocuniq231'>(Vers. 27.)</h2>

(Verse 27.) And if I cast out demons by Beelzebub, by whom do your sons cast them out? Therefore they will be your judges. He refers to the sons of the Jews, or the exorcists of that nation, or the apostles, who were born from their lineage. If they were exorcists who expelled demons by invoking God, he cleverly limits them with this question, so that they may confess that the work is of the Holy Spirit. 80 If the casting out of demons, he says, is attributed to God in your sons, and not to demons, why should the same work and cause not have the same meaning in me?" } Therefore, they themselves will be your judges, not by power, but by comparison: while they assign the expulsion of demons to God; you to Beelzebub, the prince of demons. But if it is said about the apostles, which we should understand even more, they themselves will be their judges: because they will sit on twelve thrones, judging the twelve tribes of Israel (Matthew XIX, and Luke XX).

<h2 id='tocuniq232'>(Vers. 28.)</h2>

(Verse 28.) But if I cast out demons by the Spirit of God, then the kingdom of God has come upon you. In Luke, we read this passage as follows: But if I cast out demons by the finger of God (Luke 11:20). This is the finger which the Magi confessed, who were making signs against Moses and Aaron, saying: This is the finger of God (Exodus 4:29), by which the stone tablets were written on Mount Sinai (Deuteronomy 9). Therefore, if the hand and arm of God is the Son, and his finger is the Holy Spirit, then the essence of the Father, Son, and Holy Spirit is one substance. Let not the inequality of the members scandalize you, when unity builds the body.


Therefore, the kingdom of God has come upon you. It also signifies himself, about whom it is written elsewhere: The kingdom of God is among you (Luke 17:21). And: There is one standing among you whom you do not know (John 26). Or certainly that kingdom which both John and the Lord himself preached: Repent, for the kingdom of heaven is at hand (Matthew 3:2). There is also a third kingdom of Holy Scripture, which is taken away from the Jews and given to a nation producing its fruits (Matthew 21).


<h2 id='tocuniq233'>(Vers. 29.)</h2>

(Verse 29.) Or how can anyone enter the house of a strong man and plunder his goods, unless he first binds the strong man? And then he will plunder his house. We should not be secure: Our adversary is strong, proven also by the voices of the victor. His house is the world, which is in the power of the evil one (1 John 5), not by the greatness of the Creator, but by the wrongdoing of the transgressor. We were once his possessions. The strong man has been bound and bound in Tartarus, and has been crushed by the foot of the Lord. And with the tyrant's seats plundered, captivity has been led captive.


<h2 id='tocuniq234'>(Vers. 30, 31.)</h2>

(Verse 30, 31) Whoever is not with me is against me, and whoever does not gather with me scatters. Therefore I tell you, every sin and blasphemy will be forgiven people, but the blasphemy against the Spirit will not be forgiven. Let no one think that this is said about heretics and schismatics (although it can also be understood in that way from what is superfluous), but it is referred to the devil by the following and the context of the discourse: because they cannot be compared to the works of the Savior with the works of Beelzebub. He desires to keep captive the souls of men; the Lord desires to liberate. He preaches idols; this one brings knowledge of the one God. He draws towards vices; this one calls back to virtues. How then can they have concord with each other, when their works are divided (or different)?

<h2 id='tocuniq235'>(Vers. 32.)</h2>

(Verse 32.) And whoever speaks a word against the Son of Man will be forgiven, but whoever speaks against the Holy Spirit will not be forgiven, either in this age or in the age to come. And how is it that some of our bishops and priests, after blaspheming against the Holy Spirit, are restored to their position, when the Savior says that all sins and blasphemies will be forgiven, except for blasphemy against the Holy Spirit, which will not be forgiven in either the present time or in the future? Unless perhaps we take that example about Mark the evangelist, who expressed the causes of such anger more clearly, saying: Because they were saying, He has an unclean spirit. Therefore, whoever attributes the works of the Savior to Beelzebul, the ruler of demons, and says that the Son of God has an unclean spirit, to this person blasphemy will never be forgiven. Or perhaps this passage should be understood as follows: Whoever speaks a word against the Son of Man, offending my flesh and considering me only a man, thinking that I am the son of a carpenter and have brothers named James, Joseph, and Judas, and that I am a glutton and a drunkard, such an opinion and blasphemy, although it lacks the guilt of error, yet it may have forgiveness on account of the lowliness of the body. But those who clearly understand the works of God, since they cannot deny the power, are driven by the same envy to slander; and they say that Christ, the Word of God, and the works of the Holy Spirit are Beelzebub: these will not be forgiven in this age or in the age to come.

<h2 id='tocuniq236'>(Vers. 33.)</h2>

(Verse 33.) Either make the tree good and its fruit good, or make the tree bad and its fruit bad. For a tree is known by its fruit. He constrains them with an irrefutable syllogism, which the Greeks call ἄφυκτον, and we can call it inevitable: it concludes from interrogations here and there, and it presses on both horns. If, he says, the devil is evil, he cannot do good works. But if the works you see are good, it follows that it is not the devil who does them. For it is not possible for good to arise from evil, nor for evil to arise from good. But what follows:

<h2 id='tocuniq237'>(Vers. 34.)</h2>

(Verse 34.) Brood of vipers, how can you speak good when you are evil? For out of the abundance of the heart the mouth speaks. He shows them a corrupt tree, which bears bad fruits of blasphemy, which have the seeds of the devil.

<h2 id='tocuniq238'>(Vers. 35.)</h2>

(Verse 35.) A good person brings forth good things from a good treasure. And a bad person brings forth bad things from a bad treasure. It either shows the Jews themselves blaspheming the Lord, from what kind of treasure they bring forth blasphemies, or with the previous question the opinion is stuck, that just as a good person cannot bring forth bad things, nor can a bad person bring forth good things: in the same way, Christ cannot do evil and the devil cannot do good works.

<h2 id='tocuniq239'>(Vers. 36, 37.)</h2>

(Verse 36, 37.) But I say unto you, that every idle word that men shall speak, they shall give account thereof in the day of judgment. For by thy words thou shalt be justified, and by thy words thou shalt be condemned. This also agrees with what was said before. The meaning is: If idle words, which do not benefit those who hear them, are not without danger for the one who speaks them, and each person will have to give an account of their words on the day of judgment, then how much more will you, who slander the works of the Holy Spirit and say that I cast out demons by Beelzebub, be accountable for your slander! An idle word is one that is spoken by the speaker and heard by the listener without any utility: if, setting aside serious matters, we speak of trivial things and tell ancient stories. However, whoever responds with foolishness, and dissolves into laughter and utters something indecent, this person will be considered guilty not of idle speech, but of a crime.

<h2 id='tocuniq240'>(Vers. 38.)</h2>

(Verse 38.) Then some of the scribes and Pharisees answered him, saying: Master, we want to see a sign from you. They request a sign as if the signs they had seen were not enough. But in another Gospel, it is explained more fully what they were asking for: We want to see a sign from heaven (Mark 8:11). Either they wanted fire to come down from above like Elijah, or they wanted thunder to roar, lightning to flash, and rain to pour down out of season like Samuel, as if they could not accuse Him of doing these things through hidden and various disturbances of the atmosphere. For you who falsely accuse the things that you see with your eyes, hold in your hand, and feel in usefulness: what will you do with those things that come from heaven? Certainly you will answer, and say that the magicians in Egypt performed many signs from heaven (Exod. VII).

<h2 id='tocuniq241'>(Vers. 39.)</h2>

(Verse 39.) And he, answering, said to them: A wicked and adulterous generation. Excellently said adulterous: because she had left her husband, and according to Ezechiel, she had joined herself with many lovers (Ezek. 16).

<h2 id='tocuniq242'>(Vers. 40.)</h2>

(Verse 40) He seeks a sign, and a sign will not be given to him, except the sign of Jonah the prophet (John 2). For as Jonah was in the belly of the whale for three days and three nights, so the Son of Man will be in the heart of the earth for three days and three nights. We have discussed this passage more fully in the Commentaries of the prophet Jonah: therefore, we refer the diligence of the reader to that place. Having briefly said this, we are content to understand that the whole is meant by a part: not that the Lord stood in hell for all three days and three nights, but that in part the preparation day, and the Lord's day, and the whole Sabbath day, are understood as three days and three nights.


<h2 id='tocuniq243'>(Vers. 41.)</h2>

(Verse 41.) The men of Nineveh will rise at the judgment with this generation and condemn it, because they repented at the preaching of Jonah. They were not condemned by the power of judgment, but by the example of comparison.

And behold, there is more than Jonah here. Here, understand 'here' as an adverb of place, not as a pronoun. Jonah, according to the Septuagint translators, preached for three days: I for so much time. He to the unbelieving Assyrian nation: I to the Jewish people, the people of God. He to foreigners: I to fellow citizens. He spoke to them plainly, doing nothing of signs: I doing so many signs, yet I endure the slander of Beelzebub. Therefore, there is more Jonah here, that is, at present among you.


<h2 id='tocuniq244'>(Vers. 42.)</h2>

(Verse 42.) The Queen of Austria will rise in judgment with this generation, and will condemn it because she came from the ends of the earth to hear the wisdom of Solomon. And behold, there is someone greater than Solomon here. In the same way, the Queen of Austria will condemn the people of Judah, just as the men of Nineveh condemned the unbelieving Israel. But this is the Queen of Sheba, of whom we read in the Book of Kings and Chronicles: she came to Judea amidst so many difficulties, leaving behind her people and kingdom, to hear the wisdom of Solomon, and she brought him many presents. But in Nineveh also, the queen of Sheba, secretly, the faith of the nations is preferred to Israel.

<h2 id='tocuniq245'>(Vers. 43.)</h2>

(Verse 43) But when an unclean spirit goes out of a man, it passes through dry places, seeking rest and finding none. Then it says, 'I will return to my house from which I came.' And when it comes, it finds it empty, swept, and put in order. Then it goes and takes with it seven other spirits more wicked than itself, and they enter and dwell there. And the last state of that man is worse than the first. For heretics are in a much worse condition than pagans: because in the former, there is hope of faith, and in the latter, the battle of discord. When this understanding prefers a certain applause and color of doctrine, I do not know whether it has the truth. For from the fact that a finite or parable or example follows: It will be the same for this wicked generation: we are not compelled to refer to heretics and any other people, but to the Jewish people, so that the context of the passage does not fluctuate passively and vaguely in various directions, and is disturbed in the manner of fools, but rather adheres to itself and responds to either previous or subsequent things. The unclean spirit went out from the Jews, when they received the Law, and walked through dry places, seeking rest for itself. Being expelled, of course, by the Jews, it walked through the desolate places of the Gentiles: which, when they later believed in the Lord, he, not finding a place among the nations, said:

<h2 id='tocuniq246'>(Vers. 44.)</h2>

(Verse 44.) I will return to my house, from which I came out. This means, I will go to the Jews, whom I had previously sent away.

<h2 id='tocuniq247'>(Vers. 45.)</h2>

(Verse 45.) And coming, he finds it empty, swept clean, and adorned. Then he goes and takes with him seven other spirits more wicked than himself, and they enter and dwell there, and the last state of that man becomes worse than the first. So it will be with this wicked generation. For the temple of the Jews was empty, and it did not have Christ as a guest, who said: "Rise, let us go from here" (John 14:31). And in another place: "Your house is left to you desolate" (Luke 13:35). Since, therefore, they had no protection from God and the angels, and they were burdened with excessive observances of the Law and the traditions of the Pharisees, the devil returns to his former seat: and with the addition of seven demons to himself, he dwells in his former house, and the last state of that people becomes worse than the first. For now they are possessed by a much greater number of demons, blaspheming Christ Jesus in their synagogues, than they were possessed by in Egypt before the knowledge of the Law: for it is one thing to not believe in the coming, and another thing to not receive him who has come. But the number seven is attributed either to the devil, because of the Sabbath, or because of the number of the Holy Spirit: just as in Isaiah it is narrated that the seven spirits of virtues descended upon the rod from the root of Jesse, and the flower that rises from the root (Isa. XI); so likewise the number of vices is consecrated in the devil.

<h2 id='tocuniq248'>(Vers. 46 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 46 and following) While he was still speaking to the crowd, behold, his mother and brothers stood outside, seeking to speak to him. And someone said to him, 'Behold, your mother and your brothers are standing outside, seeking you.' But he replied to the man who told him, 'Who is my mother, and who are my brothers?' And stretching out his hand toward his disciples, he said, 'Here are my mother and my brothers. For whoever does the will of my Father in heaven is my brother and sister and mother.' Then someone announces to Savior that his mother and brothers are standing outside, looking for him. It seems to me that this person who announces is not doing so by chance and simply: but rather to lay a trap for Savior, whether he prefers spiritual work over flesh and blood. Hence, the Lord, not because he denied his mother and brothers, ignored their request to come out; but because he responded to the one laying a trap, extending his hand towards his disciples, he said:

<h2 id='tocuniq249'>(Vers. 49, 50.)</h2>

(Verse 49, 50.) Behold, my mother and my brothers. For whoever does the will of my Father who is in heaven, he is my brother, and sister, and mother. These are my mother, who daily give birth to me in the souls of believers. These are my brothers, who do the works of my Father. Therefore, he did not deny his mother, as Marcion and Manichaeus claimed, so that he would be considered born from a phantom; but he preferred the apostles to his blood relatives, so that we too, in comparison to our love for the flesh, would prefer the spirit. Behold, your mother and your brothers are standing outside, seeking you. Some of the Lord's brothers suspect that Joseph had children from another wife, following the delusions of the apocryphal writings and inventing a certain Melcha or Escha as a little woman. However, as it is stated in the book that we wrote against Helvidius, by the term 'brothers of the Lord,' we understand not the sons of Joseph, but the cousins of the Savior, the children of Mary's sister, who is called the mother of James the Less and Joseph and Judas, whom we read about as the brothers of the Lord in another place in the Gospel. But the brothers are called cousins, as all Scripture demonstrates. Let us say it another way: the Savior speaks to the crowds, he educates the nations from within. His mother and brothers, that is, the synagogue and the Jewish people, stand outside and desire to enter, but they are unworthy of his speech. And when they have asked and searched and sent a messenger, they will receive the answer, that they are free to enter and can do so if they themselves believe and are willing. However, they will not be able to enter unless they ask others.


<h2 id='tocuniq250'>87 (Chap. XIII.—Vers. 1.)</h2>

In that day Jesus went out of the house and sat by the sea. And great multitudes were gathered together to Him, so that He got into a boat and sat; and the whole multitude stood on the shore. The people couldn't enter the house of Jesus, nor be where the apostles heard the mysteries. Therefore, the merciful and compassionate Lord went out from His house and sat by the sea of this world, so that great multitudes would gather to Him and hear on the shore what they didn't deserve to hear inside. He got into a boat and sat, and the whole multitude stood on the shore. Jesus is in the midst of the waves, being beaten by the sea from all sides, but in His majesty He is secure, and He makes His boat approach the shore. But the people, having no endurance for danger and not surrounded by temptations that they could not bear, stand firmly on the fixed shore, so that they may hear what is being said.

<h2 id='tocuniq251'>(Vers. 3.)</h2>

(Verse 3) And he spoke to them many things in parables, saying. The crowd is not of one opinion, but of different desires in each person. Therefore, he speaks to them in many parables, so that they may receive diverse teachings according to their various desires. And it should be noted that he did not speak everything to them in parables, but many things. For if he had said everything in parables, they would have departed without benefit to the people. He mixes the clear with the obscure, so that through the things they understand, they may be provoked to knowledge of those things which they do not understand.


<h2 id='tocuniq252'>(Vers. 4.)</h2>

(Verse 4.) Behold, the one who sows went out to sow. And while he was sowing, he was inside, at home, speaking to the disciples about the mysteries. Therefore, the one who sows the word of God went out from his home, in order to sow among the crowds. However, it is signified that this sower who sows is the Son of God, and he sows the word of the Father among the people. And at the same time, observe that this is the first parable, which is given with its interpretation. And we must be careful whenever the Lord explains his teachings, and when asked by the disciples, he explains privately, so that we do not want to understand anything else, or more or less, than what he has explained.


<h2 id='tocuniq253'>(Vers. 5 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 5 and following) Some fell along the path, and the birds of the air came and devoured it. Others fell on rocky ground, where they did not have much soil, and immediately they sprang up, since they had no depth of soil. And when the sun rose, they were scorched. And since they had no root, they withered away. Others fell among thorns, and the thorns grew up and choked them. Others fell on good soil and produced grain, some a hundredfold, some sixty, some thirty. Valentinus takes up this parable to confirm his own heresy, introducing three natures: spiritual, natural or animal, and earthly; while there are four here: one, by the way; another rocky, a third full of thorns; the fourth good soil. We delay for a little while the interpretation of it with the disciples, desiring to hear privately what is said.

<h2 id='tocuniq254'>(Vers. 9.)</h2>

(Verse 9.) He who has ears to hear, let him hear. We are challenged to understand these sayings whenever we are engaged with these words.

<h2 id='tocuniq255'>(Vers. 10, 11.)</h2>

(Verses 10, 11.) And the disciples came to him and said, 'Why do you speak to them in parables?' And he answered them, 'To you it has been given to know the secrets of the kingdom of heaven, but to them it has not been given. For whoever has, to him more will be given, and he will have abundance; but whoever does not have, even what he has will be taken away from him. This is why I speak to them in parables, because seeing they do not see, and hearing they do not hear, nor do they understand. Therefore I speak to them in parables, because they seeing, see not, and hearing they hear not, neither do they understand.' It is necessary to understand how the disciples come to him, when Jesus is sitting in the boat; unless, perhaps, it is understood that some time ago they boarded the ship with him, and there, standing, they inquired about the interpretation of the parable.


<h2 id='tocuniq256'>(Vers. 12.)</h2>

(Verse 12) For whoever has, to him more will be given, and he will have an abundance; but whoever does not have, even what he has will be taken away from him. It is not added to those who have an equal judgment, and what they seem to have is taken away from those who do not have; but to the apostles who have faith in Christ, even if they have less virtuous acts, it is granted. But to the Jews who did not believe in the Son of God, even if they possess any natural good, it is taken away. For those who do not have wisdom, they cannot understand anything intelligently.

<h2 id='tocuniq257'>(Vers. 13, 14.)</h2>

(Verse 13, 14.) Therefore I speak to them in parables: because seeing, they do not see; and hearing, they do not hear, nor do they understand. And in them the prophecy of Isaiah is fulfilled, which says: You will listen indeed, but will not understand; and you will look, but will not see. This is spoken about those who stand on the shore, and are separated from Jesus, and do not hear clearly what is being said because of the noisy sound of the waves; and the prophecy of Isaiah is fulfilled in them: You will listen indeed, but will not understand; and you will look, but will not see (Isaiah 6:9)." } These things are prophesied about the crowds, which stand on the shore, and do not deserve to hear the word of God. Therefore, let us also approach Jesus with the disciples, and let us ask him for an explanation of the parable, so that we do not seem to have ears and eyes in vain with the crowds.

<h2 id='tocuniq258'>(Vers. 15.)</h2>

(Verse 15) For the heart of this people has grown fat, and they have heard heavily with their ears. They see and do not see, and hear and do not hear, because, he says, the heart of this people has grown fat, and they have heard heavily with their ears. And lest we perhaps think that the thickness of the heart and the heaviness of the ears are by nature and not by will, he adds the blame of choice and says:

And they closed their eyes: lest they should see with their eyes, and hear with their ears, and understand with their heart, and be converted, and I should heal them. But blessed are your eyes, because they see: and your ears, because they hear.

<h2 id='tocuniq259'>(Vers. 16)</h2>

(Verse 16) But blessed are your eyes, because they see: and your ears, because they hear. Unless we had read above that the hearers were provoked to understanding, with the Savior saying: He who has ears to hear, let him hear, we would now think that the eyes and ears which receive blessedness are understood to be physical (or bodily). But to me those blessed eyes seem to be the ones that can recognize the sacraments of Christ, and those which Jesus commanded to be lifted up on high, so that they may behold the shining harvest (John 4:35); and those blessed ears, of which Isaiah speaks: The Lord has given me an ear (Isaiah 50:5).


<h2 id='tocuniq260'>(Vers. 17, 18.)</h2>

(Verse 17, 18.) Truly I say to you, many prophets and righteous people desired to see what you see, and did not see it; and to hear what you hear, and did not hear it. Therefore, listen to the parable of the sower. It seems that this passage is contrary to what is said elsewhere: Abraham desired to see my day and saw it and rejoiced (John 8:56). However, it does not say that all prophets and righteous people desired to see what you see, but many. Among many, it can happen that some see, while others do not see: although in this interpretation can be dangerous, as it seems we make any discretion among the merits of the saints. Therefore Abraham saw in a riddle, he did not see in a clear form: but you hold him in the present, and you have your Lord, and you ask according to your will, and you dine with him.

<h2 id='tocuniq261'>(Vers. 19.)</h2>

(Verse 19.) Everyone who hears the word of the kingdom, and does not understand it. Before saying this, He exhorts us to listen more carefully to what is being said.

<h2 id='tocuniq262'>(Vers. 20, 21.)</h2>

(Verse 20, 21.) The evil one comes and snatches away what was sown in his heart: this is the one who was sown along the path. As for the one who was sown on rocky ground, this is the one who hears the word and immediately receives it with joy, but he has no root in himself, and endures for a while, and when tribulation or persecution arises on account of the word, immediately he falls away. The evil one snatches away the good seed. And also understand what was sown in the heart and the different types of soil are the souls of believers.

But in fact, in both tribulation and persecution, he is scandalized constantly because of the word. Pay attention to what is said, he is scandalized constantly. Therefore, there is a distinction between someone who is compelled to deny Christ by many tribulations and punishments, and someone who is immediately scandalized and falls at the first persecution.

<h2 id='tocuniq263'>(Vers. 22.)</h2>

(Verse 22.) But he who was sown among thorns, this is he who hears the word, and the care of this worldly age and the deceitfulness of riches choke the word, and it becomes unfruitful. It seems to me that what is said literally to Adam: Among thorns and thistles you shall eat your bread (Gen. III, 18), signifies mystically that whoever gives himself to the pleasures and cares of this world, shall eat heavenly bread and true food among thorns. And he cleverly added: the fallacy of riches suffocates the word. For riches are deceitful, promising one thing and doing another. The possession of them is slippery, as they are carried here and there, and those who have them either abandon them or those who do not have them seek them out. Therefore, the Lord asserts that it is difficult for the rich to enter the kingdom of heaven, as the word of God is suffocated by riches and weakened by the rigor of virtues.


<h2 id='tocuniq264'>(Vers. 23.)</h2>

(Verse 23) But he who was sown on good soil, this is the one who hears the word and understands it, who indeed bears fruit and yields, one a hundredfold, another sixty, and another thirty. As for the seed sown on bad soil, there were three different types: by the wayside, on rocky ground, and among thorns. Similarly, in good soil, there are three different types of fruit: a hundredfold, sixtyfold, and thirtyfold. And in both the good and the bad soil, the substance does not change, but the will; and it is the hearts of both the unbelievers and the believers that receive the seed. He comes, he said, the evil one, and snatches away what was sown in his heart; and second and third, this is he, he says, who hears the word. In the explanation of the good ground also, this is he who hears the word. Therefore, first we must hear, then understand, and after understanding, yield the fruits of teachings, and produce either a hundredfold, or sixtyfold, or thirtyfold, of which we have spoken more fully in the book against Jovinian, and now we briefly touch upon: a hundredfold to virgins, sixtyfold to widows and the continent, thirtyfold to chaste marriage. For honorable are the nuptials, and the marriage-bed undefiled (Heb. 13:3, 4). Some of our people refer the hundredth fruit to the martyrs: if this is the case, the holy fruit of marriage is excluded from the good fruit." }

<h2 id='tocuniq265'>(Vers. 24 seqq.)</h2>

(Vers. 24 seqq.) Another parable He put forth to them, saying: “The kingdom of heaven is like a man who sowed good seed in his field; but while men slept, his enemy came and sowed tares among the wheat and went his way. But when the grain had sprouted and produced a crop, then the tares also appeared. So the servants of the owner came and said to him, ‘Sir, did you not sow good seed in your field? So where does the darnel come from? He replied to them: 'An enemy has done this.' The servants said to him: 'Do you want us then to go and gather them?' He said: 'No, lest perhaps while gathering the darnel, you uproot the wheat along with it. Allow both to grow together until the harvest, and at the time of harvest I will say to the reapers: Gather the darnel first, and bind it into bundles to be burned; but gather the wheat into my barn.' This is the second parable with its interpretation not immediately given, but explained after other parables were inserted. For here it is proposed, and afterwards the crowds are dismissed and they come to his house and his disciples approach him, asking: Explain to us the parable of the weeds in the field, and the rest. Therefore we should not seek with hasty desire to understand before his knowledge is sought, than to be explained by the Lord.

<h2 id='tocuniq266'>(Vers. 31.)</h2>

(Verse 31) He proposed another parable to them, saying: The Lord was sitting in a boat, and the crowd was standing on the shore: those far away, the disciples heard more closely: he proposed another parable to them, as if a rich father of the family providing food for invited guests, so that each one according to the nature of his stomach would receive various foods. Hence, in the previous parable, he did not say another one, but another. For if he had mentioned another one, we could not expect a third, so he mentioned another one, so that more would follow.


<h2 id='tocuniq267'>(Vers. 32.)</h2>

(Verse 32) The kingdom of heaven is like a mustard seed, which a man took and planted in his field. It is the smallest of all seeds, but when it grows, it is the largest of garden plants and becomes a tree, so that the birds come and perch in its branches. It should not be burdensome to the reader if we present all the parables. For those that are obscure, they should be explained more fully, so that they are not enveloped in too much brevity and their meaning is not clarified. The kingdom of heaven is the preaching of the Gospel and the knowledge of the Scriptures which leads to life. And concerning this it is said to the Jews: 'The kingdom of God will be taken away from you and given to a nation producing its fruits' (Matthew 21:43). Therefore, the kingdom of God is like a grain of mustard seed, which a man took and sowed in his field. The man who sows in his field is understood by most to be the Savior, who sows in the souls of believers. By others, the man himself sowing in his field is understood to be in himself and in his heart. Who is the one who sows, if not our perception and mind, which, receiving the seed of preaching, and nurturing the seed with the moisture of faith, makes it sprout in the field of one's heart? The preaching of the Gospel is the smallest of all disciplines. For in the first teaching, it does not have the faith of truth, preaching a man as God, God as dead, and the scandal of the cross. Compare this teaching with the dogmas of the philosophers and their books, the splendor of eloquence, and the composition of speeches, and you will see how much smaller it is than the other seeds of the seed of the Gospel. But when it grows, it shows nothing biting, nothing lively, nothing vital, but everything weak, withered, and softened boils down into vegetables and herbs, which quickly dry up and decay. However, this preaching, which seemed small in the beginning, when it has been sown either in the soul of the believer or in the whole world, does not spring up in vegetables, but grows into a tree: so that the birds of the sky (which we should understand as either the souls of believers or the strengths bound to the service of God) may come and dwell in its branches. The branches of the Evangelical tree, which grew from the grain of mustard, are diverse dogmas, in which each of the aforementioned birds finds rest. Let us also assume the wings of the dove (Ps. LIV), so that flying to higher things, we may dwell in the branches of this tree and make nests for ourselves of teachings, fleeing earthly things and hastening to heavenly things. Many, reading the grain of mustard as the smallest of all seeds, and that which is said in the Gospel by the disciples: 'Lord, increase our faith' (Luke XVII, 6); and it is answered to them by the Savior: 'Amen I say to you, if you have faith like a grain of mustard, and you say to this mountain, move from this place, it shall move', think that the apostles are either asking for a small faith or doubting the Lord's small faith; whereas the apostle Paul considers faith compared to a grain of mustard as the greatest. For what does he say? If I shall have all faith, so as to remove mountains, but do not have charity, it profits me nothing (I Cor. XIII, 2). Therefore, what the Lord said to be done by faith, which is compared to a mustard seed, the Apostle teaches can be done with all faith.

<h2 id='tocuniq268'>(Vers. 33.)</h2>

(Verse 33) He spoke another parable to them. The kingdom of heaven is like yeast, which a woman took and hid in three measures of flour until it was all leavened. The stomachs of different people are different: some are delighted by bitter foods, others by sweet, others by more austere, and others by mild. Therefore, the Lord presents, as we have already said, various parables, so that there may be different remedies according to the variety of wounds. That woman, who took the leaven and hid it in three measures of flour, until the whole was leavened, seems to me to represent the apostolic preaching or the Church, which is gathered from various nations. She takes the leaven, namely knowledge and understanding of the Scriptures, and hides it in three measures of flour, so that the spirit, soul, and body, brought together as one, do not differ from each other; but when two or three come together, they may obtain from the Father whatever they ask for (Matthew 18:19). This place is being discussed, and in another way. We read in Plato, and the commonly held belief of philosophers is that there are three passions in the human soul: the rational (which we can interpret as reasonable), the spirited (which we call full of anger or irascible), and the appetitive (which we refer to as concupiscent). And that philosopher believes that our reason dwells in the brain, anger in the gallbladder, and desire in the liver. And therefore if we receive the Gospel leaven of the Holy Scriptures, of which it was said above, three human passions will be brought together into one, so that we may possess the prudence of reason: in anger, hatred against vices; in desire, the longing for virtues; and all this will be accomplished through the Gospel teaching, which the Mother Church has provided for us. I will also speak of a third interpretation, so that the curious reader may choose from among many what pleases him: This woman and the Church itself are interpreted, which has sufficiently mixed the faith of man with the flour for the Father, the Son, and the Holy Spirit's credulity. And when it is leavened into one, it leads us to the knowledge not of a threefold God, but of the unity of divinity. Also, three seeds sown are brought together into one substance, as long as there is no difference in each seed's nature. A pious sense, indeed, but it can never advance to the authority of doctrines through parables and the understanding of doubtful riddles. And the sown seed is a measure, according to the custom of the province of Palestine, containing one and a half bushels. Other things are said about this parable, but it is not the purpose of this material to discuss everything.

<h2 id='tocuniq269'>(Vers. 34.)</h2>

(Verse 34.) Jesus spoke all these things in parables to the crowds, and he did not speak to them without parables. He speaks in parables to the crowds, not to the disciples; and even today, the crowds listen to parables: the disciples ask the Savior at home.

<h2 id='tocuniq270'>(Vers. 35.)</h2>

(Ver. 35) That which was spoken by the prophet might be fulfilled, saying: I will open my mouth in parables; I will utter things hidden since the foundation of the world. This testimony is taken from the 77th Psalm (Ver. 2). In some codices it is read, and a diligent reader may find the same in the place where we have placed 95, and the Vulgate edition has: That which was spoken by the prophet might be fulfilled, saying, there written, by the prophet Isaiah, saying. Because it was not found in Isaiah, I think it was later removed by wise men. But it seems to me that it was originally written like this: What was written by the prophet Asaph, saying. For the seventieth psalm, about which this testimony is taken, is inscribed with the title of Asaph the prophet. And the first writer did not understand Asaph, and thought it was an error of the writer, and corrected the name of Isaiah, whose name was more evident. It should be known, therefore, that in the psalms and hymns and songs of God, not only David, but also the others whose names are mentioned, are to be called prophets: namely Asaph and Heman and Idithun and Eman the Ezrahite, and Ethan and the sons of Korah, and the rest whom Scripture mentions. And the saying of the Lord is attributed to them: I will open my mouth in parables; I will declare hidden things from the foundation of the world, to be considered more attentively and to be found described, the departure of the children of Israel from Egypt and all the signs which are contained in the story of Exodus. From this we understand that all those things which are written should be understood figuratively: not only the clear letter sounding, but also hidden mysteries; for the Savior promises that He will declare Himself in parables, and will bring forth hidden things from the creation of the world.

<h2 id='tocuniq271'>(Vers. 36.)</h2>

(Verse 36) Then he dismissed the crowds and went into the house. And his disciples came to him, saying, 'Explain to us the parable of the weeds of the field.' Jesus sent the crowds away and went into the house so that his disciples could come to him and privately ask him what the people were not deserving to hear or understand. 'Explain to us the parable of the weeds of the field.'

<h2 id='tocuniq272'>(Vers. 37 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 37 and following) And he answered, saying: The one who sows good seed is the Son of Man. But the field is the world. And the good seed, these are the sons of the kingdom. But the weeds are the sons of the evil one. And the enemy who sowed them is the devil. And the harvest is the end of the age. And the reapers are angels. Therefore, just as the weeds are gathered and burned with fire, so it will be at the end of the age. The Son of Man will send his angels, and they will gather out of his kingdom all causes of sin and those who do lawlessness, and they will throw them into the fiery furnace. In that place there will be weeping and gnashing of teeth. He clearly explained that the field is the world: the sower, the Son of Man; the good seed, the children of the kingdom; the weeds, the children of the evil one; the enemy who sows the weeds, the devil; the harvest, the end of the world; the reapers, the angels. All scandals are attributed to the weeds; the righteous are considered as children of the kingdom. Therefore, as I said above, we must apply our faith to what has been explained by the Lord. However, those things that are left unspoken and abandoned by our understanding must be briefly examined. Understand the people who sleep as the leaders of the churches. Do not accept anyone other than the angels, who daily see the face of the Father (Matthew 18). The devil, however, is called the enemy of man because he ceased to be God. And it is written about him in the ninth psalm: Arise, O Lord, let not man prevail (Psalm 9:20). Therefore, let not the one who is in charge of the Church sleep, lest through his negligence the enemy sows weeds, that is, the teachings of heretics. But what is said: Lest while you gather up the cockle, you root up the wheat also together with it. Give place to repentance, and be admonished not to cut off hastily a brother who may, to-morrow, rise again changed from his fault, and begin to defend the truth. That which follows also seems to be opposed to this precept: Let both grow together until the harvest (Deut. XIII, 5) ; but this seems inconsistent with the command: Take away the evil one from among you (Isai. I); and there should by no means be any fellowship with those who are called brethren, and are fornicators and adulterers. For if uprooting is forbidden and patience must be maintained until the harvest, how are some to be expelled from among us? Between wheat and weeds, which we call darnel, there is a great similarity, and in distinguishing them there is either no difference or a very difficult one. Therefore, the Lord warns us not to hastily pronounce judgment when there is any ambiguity, but to leave the judgment to God: so that when the day of judgment comes, He may cast out not a mere suspicion of guilt, but a clear accusation from the gathering of the saints. But what he said, that the bundles of the tares are to be burned with fire, and the wheat gathered into barns, is manifest, that heretics and hypocrites are to be consumed by the fires of hell; but the saints who are called wheat, are to be received into barns, that is, into celestial mansions.

<h2 id='tocuniq273'>(Vers. 43.)</h2>

(Verse 43.) Then the righteous will shine like the sun in the kingdom of their Father. He who has ears to hear, let him hear. In the present age, the light of the saints shines before men; but after the end of the world, the righteous themselves will shine like the sun in the kingdom of their Father.

<h2 id='tocuniq274'>(Vers. 44.)</h2>

(Verse 44.) The kingdom of heaven is like treasure hidden in a field, which a man found and hid; and for joy over it he goes and sells all that he has and buys that field. Hindered by frequent obscurities of parables, we surpass the interpretive commentary, so that it seems we have almost passed from one type of interpretation to another. This treasure is either all the treasures of wisdom and knowledge hidden, or God is the Word, who appears hidden in the flesh of Christ (Colossians 2), or it is the holy Scriptures, in which the knowledge of the Savior is stored: and when someone finds Him in them, they must disregard all the benefits of this world, in order to possess Him whom they have found." } But what follows: When a man finds him he hides him in 98: for this reason it is said, not that he does this out of envy, but that out of fear of losing him, and unwilling to lose him, he hides him in his heart, whom he preferred to his former abilities.

<h2 id='tocuniq275'>(Vers. 45, 46.)</h2>

(Vers. 45, 46.) Again, the kingdom of heaven is like a merchant seeking fine pearls. When he found one pearl of great value, he went and sold all that he had and bought it. In other words, the good pearls that the merchant seeks are the Law and the prophets. Listen, Marcion; listen, Manichaeus: the good pearls are the Law and the prophets, and the knowledge of the Old Testament. But there is one most precious pearl, the knowledge of the Savior, and the sacrament of his passion, and the mystery of his resurrection. When a merchant, like the apostle Paul, discovers this, he despises all the mysteries of the law and the prophets, and the former observances in which he lived blamelessly, like worthless trash, in order to gain Christ (Philippians III). Not that the discovery of a new pearl condemns the old pearls, but that in comparison to it, every other gem is of lesser value.


<h2 id='tocuniq276'>(Vers. 47 seqq.)</h2>

(Vers. 47 seqq.) Again, the kingdom of heaven is like a net cast into the sea and gathering fish of every kind. When it was full, they pulled it ashore, sat down, and sorted the good into vessels and threw away the bad. So it will be at the end of the age: the angels will come out and separate the evil from the righteous, and throw them into the fiery furnace, where there will be weeping and gnashing of teeth. With the fulfillment of Jeremiah’s prophecy, saying: ‘Behold, I am sending many fishermen to you’ (Jeremiah XVI, 16): after hearing this, Peter and Andrew, James and John, the sons of Zebedee, said: ‘Follow me, and I will make you fishers of men’ (Matthew IV, 19). They wove together a net of the teachings of the Evangelists from the Old and New Testaments, and cast it into the sea of this age: which even to this day is spread out in the midst of the waves, catching everything that falls into it, that is, both good and bad men, and the very best and the very worst fish. But when the consummation and end of the world comes, as he explains more clearly below, then the net will be drawn out to the shore: then the true judgment of separating the fish will be shown, and as if in a very calm port, the good will be sent into the vessels of celestial mansions: but the wicked will be received by the flame of hell to be burned and dried up.

<h2 id='tocuniq277'>(Vers. 51.)</h2>

(Verse 51.) Did you understand all these things? They said to him: Yes. He said to them: To the apostles, this is specifically spoken; and to them it is said: Did you understand all these things; For he does not only want to hear them as a people, but to understand them as future teachers.

<h2 id='tocuniq278'>(Vers. 52.)</h2>

(Verse 52.) Therefore every scribe who has been instructed in the kingdom of heaven is like a master of a house who brings out of his treasure what is new and what is old. The apostles, scribes, and notaries of the Savior were instructed to record his words and teachings in the tablets of their fleshly hearts, in the sacraments of the heavenly realms, and they had the wealth of the master of the house, bringing out of their treasure what is new and what is old: so that whatever they preached in the Gospel, they could confirm with the words of the law and the prophets. And the bride says in the Song of Songs: I have kept for you, my brother, both the new and the old (Cant. VII, 13).

<h2 id='tocuniq279'>(Vers. 53, 54.)</h2>

(Vers. 53, 54.) And it came to pass, when Jesus finished these parables, he departed from there. And coming to his own country, he taught them in their synagogue, so that they were amazed and said, 'After the parables that he spoke to the people, and which only the apostles understand, he goes to his own country to teach more openly there.'

Where does this wisdom and these virtues come from? The folly of the Nazarenes is astonishing: they marvel at where wisdom has its wisdom, and where virtue has its virtues; but the mistake is obvious, that they suspect the son of a carpenter.

<h2 id='tocuniq280'>(Vers. 55, 56.)</h2>

(Verse 55, 56.) Isn't this the carpenter's son? Isn't his mother called Mary, and his brothers James and Joseph and Simon and Judas? And aren't all his sisters with us? Where then did he get all these things? And they were offended by him. The error of the Jews is our salvation, and the condemnation of the heretics. For they saw Jesus Christ merely as a man, so that the carpenters thought he was their own son: Isn't this the carpenter's son? Are you surprised if they are mistaken about his brothers, when they are mistaken about his father? This place is more fully explained in the aforementioned book against Helvetius.

<h2 id='tocuniq281'>(Vers. 57.)</h2>

(Verse 57.) But Jesus said to them, “A prophet is not without honor, except in his own country and in his own house.” It is almost natural for citizens to always envy fellow citizens. For they do not consider the present works of a man, but they remember the fragile nature of his childhood, as if they themselves did not go through the same stages of age to reach maturity.

<h2 id='tocuniq282'>(Vers. 58.)</h2>

(Verse 58.) And he did not do many miracles there because of their unbelief. Not that he was unable to do many miracles for them, even though they were unbelievers; but because by doing many miracles, he would condemn the unbelieving citizens. It can also be understood in another way, that Jesus is despised in his own house and country, that is, among the Jewish people. And therefore, he performed few signs there, so that they would not become altogether inexcusable. However, greater signs are performed daily among the Gentiles through the apostles, not so much in the healing of their bodies, but in the salvation of their souls.


<h2 id='tocuniq283'>(Chap. XIV.—Vers. 1, 2.)</h2>

(Chapter 14 - Verses 1, 2.) At that time Herod the Tetrarch heard the news about Jesus and said to his servants, 'This is John the Baptist; he has risen from the dead; and that is why these miraculous powers are at work in him.' Some interpreters of the Church seek the reasons why Herod suspected this, that he believed John had risen from the dead, and that is why miraculous powers were at work in him, as if it were necessary to give us an explanation for an alien error, or to find an opportunity for the doctrine of reincarnation from these words, since at the time when John was beheaded, the Lord was already thirty years old; but the doctrine of reincarnation says that after many cycles of years, souls enter into different bodies.


<h2 id='tocuniq284'>(Vers. 3, 4.)</h2>

(Vers. 3, 4.) For Herod had seized John and bound him and put him in prison because of Herodias, the wife of his brother Philip. For John had been saying to him, 'It is not lawful for you to have her.' The old story tells that Philip, the son of Herod the Great (under whom the Lord fled to Egypt), married Herodias, the daughter of King Aretas; later on, when grievances arose between Herodias and her former husband, Herod, who was his enemy, her father took her away and married her to his son, thus causing sorrow for her former husband. However, the evangelist Luke provides a fuller account of who this Philip is: In the fifteenth year of the reign of Tiberius Caesar, when Pontius Pilate was governor of Judea; Herod was tetrarch of Galilee; his brother Philip was tetrarch of Ituraea and Trachonitis regions (Luke 3:1). Therefore, John the Baptist, who had come in the spirit and power of Elijah, with the same authority that Elijah had rebuked Ahab and Jezebel (1 Kings 21), rebuked Herod and Herodias for their unlawful marriage and for Herod taking Herodias as his wife while his brother was still alive. John preferred to risk his life by confronting the king rather than to compromise and be forgetful of God's commandments due to flattery.


<h2 id='tocuniq285'>(Vers. 5.)</h2>

(Verse 5) And wanting to kill him, he feared the people, because they held him as a prophet. Indeed, he truly feared the sedition of the people because of John, from whom he knew that many crowds had been baptized in the Jordan; but he was overcome by love for his wife, because of her fervor, he had even neglected God's commandments. (Genesis 40)

<h2 id='tocuniq286'>(Vers. 6.)</h2>

(Verse 6.) However, on Herod's birthday, the daughter of Herodias danced in the midst, and it pleased Herod. We found no one else who observed his birthday, except Herod and Pharaoh, so their impiety would be on par, and there would be a celebration together.

<h2 id='tocuniq287'>(Vers. 7.)</h2>

(Verse 7.) So when he had promised with an oath to give her whatever she might ask of him. But she, being forewarned by her mother, asked for the head of John the Baptist. I do not excuse Herod, because against his will and reluctantly he committed a murder under oath, who perhaps swore this in order to prepare the devices of a future killing. Otherwise, if he says that he did it because of an oath, if he had asked for the death of his father or mother, would he not have done it? Therefore, since he was ready to repudiate ((or had repudiated)) it in himself, he ought to have despised and rejected it in the prophet.


<h2 id='tocuniq288'>(Vers. 8.)</h2>

(Verse 8) Give me, he said, here on a platter, the head of John the Baptist. Herodias, fearing that Herod might come to his senses someday, or that he might become friendly with his brother Philip and dissolve their unlawful marriage, instructs her daughter to ask for the head of John immediately at the banquet: a fitting reward for the dance, a worthy prize for the blood.

And the king was sad. It is the custom of the Scriptures, as the historian narrates the opinion of many, to tell how it was believed by everyone at that time. Just as Joseph was called the father of Jesus by Mary herself, so now Herod is said to be sad, because they thought this while reclining at the table (Luke 2). For he was a dissembler of his own mind and a skillful murderer, he showed sadness on his face while having joy in his mind.


<h2 id='tocuniq289'>(Vers. 9, 10.)</h2>

(Vers. 9, 10.) However, because of the oath and because of those who were reclining together, he commanded it to be given. And he sent and beheaded John in prison. Crime excuses an oath, so that under the guise of piety, the impious act would be done. But what he added: And because of those who were reclining together, he wants them all to be partners in his crime, so that they would be brought into a luxurious and impure feast of bloody banquets.

<h2 id='tocuniq290'>(Vers. 11.)</h2>

(Verse 11.) And his head was brought in on a platter, and given to the girl, and she brought it to her mother. We read in Roman history that the Roman leader Flamininus, who was lying next to a prostitute who claimed she had never seen a beheaded man, agreed to be accused of a capital crime and be executed at a banquet. He was expelled from the Senate by the censors because he had mixed the feast with blood and because he had given preference to the delight of another over the death of a guilty man, so that lust and murder were combined. How wicked Herod and Herodias and the girl who danced, demanded the price of the prophet's blood, so that she may have power over the tongue that condemned their unlawful marriage. This was fulfilled literally; but even today we see that the Jews have lost Christ, who is the head of the prophets, in the person of John the Baptist.

And his disciples, coming forward, took his body and buried it. Josephus reports in a certain town of Arabia that John was beheaded. And that which follows: His disciples, coming forward, took the body, both of him, and of the Savior, we can understand.

<h2 id='tocuniq291'>(Vers. 13.)</h2>

(Verse 13) And they came and told Jesus. When Jesus heard this, He departed from there in a boat to a deserted place by Himself. They announced the death of John the Baptist to the Savior, which, when He heard, He went away into a deserted place. Not, as some suppose, out of fear of death, but sparing His enemies, lest they should join murder to murder. Or perhaps postponing His own death until the day of His Passover, on which the Lamb had to be sacrificed because of the sacrament, and the doorposts of believers had to be sprinkled with blood (Exodus 12). Or perhaps he departed in order to provide us an example of avoiding those who offer themselves unnecessarily to danger: because not all have the same perseverance in torments as they offer themselves to be tormented. For this reason, he also instructs in another place: When they persecute you in this city, flee to another (Matt. X, 23). The evangelist elegantly does not say, flee to a deserted place, but departed, so that he may avoid the persecutors more than fear them. Another: After the Jews and the king of the Jews had cut off the head of the prophets and lost their language and voice among them, Jesus went into the desert, a place which the Church had not previously had a man.

And when the crowds heard, they followed him on foot from the cities. It is possible that, for another reason, upon hearing of the death of John, they withdrew to a deserted place, in order to confirm the faith of the believers. Finally, the crowds followed him on foot, not on mounts, not in various vehicles, but by their own labor of feet, to demonstrate their fervor of mind. If we wish to explain the reasons for each word, we exceed the brevity of the intended work. However, it must be said briefly that after the Lord came into the desert, great crowds followed him. For before he came into the wilderness of the nations, he was worshipped by only one people.

<h2 id='tocuniq292'>(Vers. 14.)</h2>

(Verse 14) 104 And going out, he saw a great crowd, and he had compassion on them, and he healed their sick.
