In the Gospel speeches, the letter is always connected to the spirit, and whatever seems cold at first sight, if you touch it, it becomes warm. The Lord was in a deserted place; the crowds followed him, leaving their cities, that is, their former ways of life and the various teachings. But Jesus going out signifies that the crowds had indeed the will to go, but they did not have the power to arrive: therefore the Savior goes out of his place and goes to meet them, just as in another parable he had met the repentant son (Luke 15). Seeing the crowd, he had compassion on them and healed their diseases, so that full faith would immediately receive a reward.

<h2 id='tocuniq293'>(Vers. 15.)</h2>

(Verse 15) When evening came, his disciples approached him, saying: This is a deserted place, and the hour has already passed; send the crowds away, so that they may go to the villages and buy themselves food. Everything is filled with mysteries. He left Judea and went to a deserted place; the crowds followed him, leaving their cities; Jesus went out to them, had compassion on the crowds, and healed their sick. He did this not in the morning, not as the day was growing, not at noon, but in the evening, when the sun of righteousness set.


<h2 id='tocuniq294'>(Vers. 16.)</h2>

(Verse 16) But Jesus said to them: They do not need to go. They do not need to search for different foods and buy themselves unknown breads, when they have heavenly bread with them.

On that day, He commanded you to eat. He challenged the apostles to the breaking of the bread, so that the greatness of the sign may become more known to them, as they bear witness to it.

<h2 id='tocuniq295'>(Vers. 17.)</h2>

(Verse 17.) They replied to him: We only have here five loaves and two fish. In another Gospel it is written: There is a boy here who has five loaves (John 6:9); this boy seems to signify Moses. As for the two fish, we can understand them as representing both Testaments, or because the number two is often associated with the Law. Therefore, before the passion of the Savior and the shining forth of the Gospel, the apostles had nothing more than five loaves and two little fish, which were found in salty waters and the waves of the sea.


<h2 id='tocuniq296'>(Vers. 18.)</h2>

(Verse 18) He said to them: Bring me those here. Listen, Marcion, listen, Manichaee, Jesus commands to have five loaves and two small fish brought to him, so that he may sanctify and multiply them.

<h2 id='tocuniq297'>(Vers. 19.)</h2>

(Verse 19.) And when he had commanded the multitude to sit down on the hay. The clear meaning is this: let us unfold the mysteries of spiritual interpretation. They are commanded to sit down on the hay, and according to another Evangelist (Luke 9), on the ground, in groups of fifty or a hundred, so that after trampling on their flesh and all its pleasures, like hay that has dried up, they may then, through penance represented by the number fifty, ascend to the pinnacle of perfection represented by the number one hundred.


After receiving five loaves of bread and two fish, looking up to heaven, he blessed and broke them, and gave the loaves to the disciples. He looked up to heaven, to teach that our eyes should be directed there. He took the five loaves and two fish in his hands, and broke them, and gave them to the disciples. When the Lord broke them, a great quantity of food was produced. For if they had remained whole and not divided, they could not have fed such a great multitude of crowds, children, and women. Therefore, the law is broken with the prophets, and is torn into pieces, and its mysteries are brought into the open, so that what was whole and enduring in its original state may nourish the multitude of nations when divided into parts.

<h2 id='tocuniq298'>(Vers. 20.)</h2>

(Verse 20.) However, the disciples gave to the crowds. And all ate and were satisfied. The crowds received food from the Lord through the apostles.

And they took the remains of twelve baskets full of fragments. Each of the apostles fills his basket with the remains of the Savior, so that he has either to provide food for the nations afterwards, or to teach from the remains that the loaves were truly multiplied afterwards. And at the same time wonder, how in the wilderness and in such a vast solitude loaves are not found, except only five, and two fish, 106 and how easily twelve baskets are found.


<h2 id='tocuniq299'>(Vers. 21.)</h2>

(Verse 21.) Now, the number of those who ate was five thousand men, not counting women and children. According to the number of five loaves and the multitude of five thousand men who ate, the number had not yet reached the sevenfold number mentioned in another place, which is four thousand men who eat, close to the number in the Gospels. However, those who ate were five thousand men who had grown into perfect men, and they followed him of whom Zacharias says: Behold the man, his name is the Rising Sun. (Zach. VI, 12.) But women, and children, the weaker sex and the younger age, are unworthy of being counted by number. Therefore, in the book of Numbers, whenever the priests and Levites, and the armies or crowds of fighters are described, slaves and women, and children, and the common people are omitted without number.

<h2 id='tocuniq300'>(Vers. 22.)</h2>

(Verse 22.) And immediately Jesus compelled his disciples to get into a boat and go ahead of him across the sea, until he dismissed the crowds. He commanded the disciples to cross over, and he forced them to get into the boat. This shows, by his words, that they unwillingly separated from the Lord, as they did not want to be separated from him even for a moment, due to their love for their teacher.

<h2 id='tocuniq301'>(Vers. 23.)</h2>

(Verse 23) And after dismissing the crowd, he went up the mountain alone to pray. And when evening came, he was there alone. If Peter, James, and John, who had seen his glory being transformed, had been with him, perhaps they would have gone up the mountain with him. But the crowd cannot follow to lofty places unless it has been taught by the sea on the shore and nourished in the desert. However, the fact that he went up alone to pray should not be attributed to the one who fed five thousand people with five loaves, excluding children and women; but to the one who, upon hearing of John's death, withdrew into solitude. Not that we should separate the person of the Lord, but that his works are divided between God and man.


<h2 id='tocuniq302'>107 (Vers. 24.)</h2>

107 (V. 24.) But the boat was being tossed in the middle of the sea by the waves: for the wind was contrary. Rightly, as if unwillingly, and the apostles, pulling away, had departed from the Lord, so that they would not suffer shipwreck in his absence. Finally, while the Lord was staying on the mountaintop, immediately a contrary wind arises, and the sea is disturbed, and the apostles are in peril, and the imminent shipwreck persists as long as Jesus does not come.

<h2 id='tocuniq303'>(Vers. 25.)</h2>

(Verse 25.) But in the fourth watch of the night, he came to them, walking on the sea. Military stations and watches are divided into intervals of three hours. Therefore, when he says that the Lord came to them in the fourth watch of the night, he shows that they were in danger throughout the night, and in the last part of the night, and that help will be given to them at the end of the world.

<h2 id='tocuniq304'>(Vers. 26.)</h2>

(Verse 26.) And seeing him walking on the sea, they were troubled, saying: It is a ghost. If, according to Marcion and Manichaeus, our Lord was not born of the Virgin, but appeared in a phantom, why are the apostles now afraid of seeing a phantom?

And they cried out from fear. The confused noise and uncertain voice are signs of great fear.

<h2 id='tocuniq305'>(Vers. 27.)</h2>

(Verse 27.) Immediately Jesus spoke to them, saying: Have confidence, it is I, do not be afraid. He takes care of what was first involved in the matter, and commands those who fear, saying: Have confidence, do not be afraid. And what follows, I am, does not add who he is, either they could understand from his familiar voice that he was speaking, who was speaking through the darkness of the obscure night, or they were asking if he himself was the one who spoke to Moses, whom they knew had said: This you will say to the children of Israel: He who is, has sent me to you (Exodus 3:14).


<h2 id='tocuniq306'>(Vers. 28, 29.)</h2>

(Verse 28, 29.) But Peter, answering, said: Lord, if it is you, command me to come to you on the water. And he said: Come. In all places Peter is found to have the most ardent faith. When the disciples were asked who they said Jesus, the Son of God, was, he confessed. When he wanted to go to his passion, he was prohibited: and although he may have erred in understanding, he did not err in his affection: not wanting him to die, whom he had just confessed as the Son of God a little while earlier. He is the first to ascend the mountain with the Savior among the first, and he alone follows during the Passion. He immediately washes away the sin of denial, which had descended from sudden fear, with bitter tears. After the Passion, when they were in the lake of Genesareth and fishing, and the Lord was standing on the shore, while others were gradually sailing, he does not tolerate delay, but, girded with his tunic, he immediately plunges into the waves. Therefore, with the same fervor of faith that he always had, even now, while the others are silent, he believes that he can do, through the will of the teacher, what the teacher could do through nature. Command me to come to you on the water. You command, and immediately the waves will be calmed, and the body, which is naturally heavy, will become light.

And Peter, descending from the little boat, walked on the water to come to Jesus. Let those who think that the body of the Lord was not true because he walked on soft and airy waters, explain how Peter also walked, whom they certainly cannot deny was a true human being.

<h2 id='tocuniq307'>(Vers. 30.)</h2>

(Verse 30.) But seeing a strong wind, he was afraid. And when he began to sink, he cried out, saying: Lord, save me. The faith of his soul burned, but human weakness dragged him into the depths. Therefore, a little bit of temptation is left, so that faith may grow and understand that it is not by the ease of his request, but by the power of the Lord that he is saved.

<h2 id='tocuniq308'>(Vers. 31, 32.)</h2>

(Verse 31, 32.) And immediately Jesus stretched out his hand, took hold of him, and said to him: O you of little faith, why did you doubt? And when he had gotten into the boat, the wind ceased. If to the apostle Peter, of whom we have spoken above concerning the faith and ardor of his mind, who confidently asked the Savior, saying: Lord, if it is you, command me to come to you on the waters, because he feared a little, it is said: O you of little faith, why did you doubt? What must we say, who have even a small portion of this little faith?" }


<h2 id='tocuniq309'>(Vers. 33.)</h2>

(Verse 33) But those who were in the boat came and worshipped him, saying, Truly you are the Son of God. At the sight of this one sign, the calm of the sea being restored, which sometimes happens after severe storms by chance, the sailors and passengers truly confess the Son of God, and Arius preaches a creature in the Church.

<h2 id='tocuniq310'>(Vers. 34.)</h2>

(Verse 34.) And when he had crossed over, they came to the land of Genesareth. If we knew what Genesareth would sound like in our language, we would understand how Jesus, through the image of the apostles and the ship, leads the Church liberated from the shipwreck of persecution to the shore, and makes it rest in the most peaceful harbor.

<h2 id='tocuniq311'>(Vers. 35.)</h2>

(Verse 35.) And when the men of that place recognized him, they sent throughout all that region. They knew him by reputation, not by appearance, or certainly not for the magnitude of the signs he was performing among the people; he was also well-known by his face to many. And see how great is the faith of the people in the land of Genesareth, that they are not satisfied with the healing of those who are present, but send to other cities in the surrounding area, so that everyone may come to the doctor.

<h2 id='tocuniq312'>(Vers. 36.)</h2>

(Verse 36.) And all those who were sick brought themselves forward and begged him to touch even the fringe of his garment. And whoever touched it, they were healed. Those who are sick, do not touch the body of Jesus nor his entire garment, but only the edge of the fringe, and whoever touches it will be healed. The fringe of his garment, or rather understand the smallest commandment: whoever transgresses it will be called the least in the kingdom of heaven. And through the assumption of the body, by which we come to the Word of God, and afterwards enjoy His majesty.

<h2 id='tocuniq313'>(Chap. XV.—Vers. 1.)</h2>

(Chapter 15, Verse 1) Then the scribes and Pharisees came to him from Jerusalem, saying, 'Why do your disciples break the tradition of the elders? For they do not wash their hands when they eat.' How foolish are the Pharisees and scribes, accusing the Son of God of not keeping the traditions and precepts of men.

<h2 id='tocuniq314'>(Vers. 1, 2.)</h2>

(Verse 1, 2.) For they do not wash their hands when they eat bread. Hands, that is, works, not certainly of the body, but of the soul, are to be washed, so that the word of God may be made in them.

<h2 id='tocuniq315'>(Vers. 3.)</h2>

(Verse 3) But he answered and said to them, Why do you also transgress the commandment of God because of your tradition? He refutes false accusation with a true response. For, he says, you neglect the precepts of the Lord because of human tradition, why do you think my disciples should be accused, because they disregard the orders of the elders, in order to keep the knowledge of God?

<h2 id='tocuniq316'>(Vers. 4 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 4 and following) For God said, 'Honor your father and mother, and whoever curses his father or mother shall be put to death.' But you say, 'Whoever says to his father or mother, 'Whatever help you might otherwise have received from me is a gift devoted to God,' he need not honor his father.' So you have made void the word of God because of your tradition. You hypocrites! Well did Isaiah prophesy of you, when he said: 'This people honors me with their lips, but their heart is far from me' (Exodus 20, Leviticus 20). But they worship me without cause, teaching doctrines and commandments of men. And he called the crowds to him and said to them: Hear and understand. Honor in the Scriptures is not only felt in greetings and official deference, but also in acts of charity and offering of gifts (Exod. XX and XXI, and Lev. XX). The Apostle says, 'Honor widows who are truly widows' (I Tim. V, 3); here, honor is understood as a gift. And in another place: Elders should be honored with a double honor, especially those who labor in the word and doctrine of God (Ibid., 17). And by this command we are ordered not to close the mouth of an ox that treads out the corn (Deut. 25). And may the worker be worthy of his wages (Luke 10). The Lord had commanded, taking into consideration the weakness, the age, or the poverty of the parents, that the children should honor their parents even in the necessary things of life. Desiring to overturn this most provident law of God, the scribes and Pharisees, in order to introduce impiety under the name of piety, taught wicked children that if anyone wanted to offer to God those things which should be offered to parents (who is the true Father), the offering of the Lord should take precedence over the gifts to the parents, or certainly the parents themselves, seeing that they were dedicated to God, would avoid incurring the crime of sacrilege and would be consumed by poverty. And so it happened that the offering of the children, under the pretext of the temple of God, would be given to the profits of the priests. This worst tradition of the Pharisees came about on another occasion. Many, having debts to others and not wanting to repay what was owed to them, delegated to the priests so that the money collected would serve the needs of the temple and their own use. This can also be understood briefly. Convert, he says, the sons to say to their parents: whatever gift I was going to offer to God, I consume it on your food, and it benefits you, oh father and mother, that they, fearing to accept what is dedicated to God, prefer to live in need rather than eat from the consecrated things." }


<h2 id='tocuniq317'>(Vers. 11.)</h2>

(Verse 11) It is not what enters into the mouth that defiles a person, but what comes out of the mouth, this defiles a person. The word, properly spoken, is what defiles, and it is not worn out in everyday speech. The Jewish people, boasting to be a part of God, call common foods those which all people consume. For example, pork, oysters, hares, and similar animals that do not split the hoof, do not chew the cud, and are not scaly in fish. And in the Acts of the Apostles it is written: What God has sanctified, do not call common (Acts 10:15). Therefore, that which is common and is open to other people, and is not from God's side, is called unclean. It is not what enters the mouth that defiles a person, but what proceeds out of the mouth that defiles a person. Let a wise reader object and say: If what enters the mouth does not defile a person, then why do we not eat idol sacrifices? And the Apostle writes: 'You cannot drink the cup of the Lord, and the cup of demons' (I Cor. X, 20). It should be known then that indeed, food itself, and every creature of God, is clean: but the invocation of idols and demons makes it unclean.

<h2 id='tocuniq318'>(Vers. 12.)</h2>

(Verse 12.) Then his disciples approached him and said: Do you know that the Pharisees were scandalized when they heard this word? From one sermon, all the superstition of Jewish observances was abolished; those who believed that their religion was based on the abominable and acceptable foods. And because it is often used in Ecclesiastical Scriptures, let us briefly explain what 'scandal' means. Σκῶλον and scandal, we can say it means offense, or ruin and stumbling block. When, therefore, we read: 'Whoever causes scandal to one of these little ones, it is understood that he has given occasion for ruin to anyone, either by word or by deed.'

<h2 id='tocuniq319'>(Vers. 13.)</h2>

(Verse 13) But he answered and said, Every plant which my heavenly Father hath not planted, shall be rooted up. Even those things which seem plain in the Scriptures are full of questions. Every plant, he says, which my heavenly Father hath not planted, shall be rooted up. Therefore that plantation also shall be rooted up, of which the Apostle saith: I have planted, Apollo watered  (1 Corinthians 3:6) . But the question is resolved by what follows: But God gave the increase  (ibid., 9) . He also says: You are God's agriculture, you are God's building (3 John 8). And in another place: We are God's co-workers. If, however, we are co-workers, therefore, God plants and waters with His co-workers (or workers), with Paul planting and Apollo watering. Those who introduce different natures abuse this passage, saying: If the planting that the Father did not plant will be uprooted, therefore, what He did plant cannot be uprooted. But let them hear that of Jeremiah; I have planted you a true vineyard, how have you been turned into the bitterness of an alien vine? (Jer. II, 21) For indeed God has planted, and no one can uproot His planting. But since this planting is in the will of one's own free choice, no one else can uproot it unless it gives its consent.

<h2 id='tocuniq320'>(Vers. 14.)</h2>

(Verse 14) Let them alone; they are blind guides of the blind. And if a blind man leads a blind man, both will fall into a pit. This is what the Apostle commanded: Avoid a heretical man, after a first and second admonition, knowing that he is perverted and condemned by himself (Titus 3:10). In this sense, the Savior also commanded that the worst teachers should be left to their own devices, knowing that they are difficult to be brought to the truth and that they are blind, leading a blind people into error.


<h2 id='tocuniq321'>(Vers. 15, 16.)</h2>

(V. 15, 16.) 114 Peter, answering, said to him: Explain to us this parable. But he said: Are you also still without understanding? What had been openly said and was clear to the hearing, the apostle Peter thinks was said in a parable and seeks a mystical understanding in a matter that is evident. And he is rebuked by the Lord for thinking that what was clearly spoken was said in a parable. From this we observe the flawed nature of the listener, who either wants to understand obscure things clearly or clearly spoken things in an obscure manner.


<h2 id='tocuniq322'>(Vers. 17, 18.)</h2>

(Verse 17, 18.) Do you not understand that everything that enters the mouth goes into the stomach and is expelled into the sewer? But the things that come out of the mouth come from the heart and defile a person. All the passages of the Gospels with the heretics and the perverse are full of scandals. And some people slander from this little sentence, that the Lord, ignorant of physiolog And there are many who, due to a weakness of the stomach, constantly endure vomiting, immediately vomiting up what they have ingested after meals and snacks, and yet they are corpulent: because at the first touch, more liquid food and drink are poured through the limbs. But while these types of people want to criticize the incompetence of others, they show their own. For even though the food and drink is thin and liquid, once it has been digested and processed in the veins and limbs, it flows down to the lower parts through the hidden channels of the body, which the Greeks call 'poroi', and passes into the rectum.


<h2 id='tocuniq323'>(Vers. 19, 20.)</h2>

(Vers. 19, 20.) For from the heart come evil thoughts, murders, adulteries, fornications, thefts, false testimonies, blasphemies: these are the things that defile a person. But to eat with unwashed hands does not defile a person. For from the heart, he says, come evil thoughts. Therefore, the principal part of the soul, not according to Plato in the brain, but according to Christ, is in the heart: and those who believe that evil thoughts are inspired by the devil and not born from one's own will can be argued against with this statement. The Devil can be a helper and instigator of evil thoughts, but he cannot be the author. However, if he is always lying in wait, he may kindle a small spark of our thoughts with his own fuel, and we should not think that he also explores the hidden depths of the heart, but rather we should judge what we are inwardly from the outward appearance and actions of the body. For example, if he sees us frequently gazing at a beautiful woman, he understands that our heart has been wounded by the arrow of love.


<h2 id='tocuniq324'>(Vers. 21, 22.)</h2>

(Verse 21, 22.) And Jesus went out from there and withdrew to the regions of Tyre and Sidon. And behold, a Canaanite woman from those borders came out and cried out to Him, saying. You neglect the scribes and Pharisees who accuse you, and you go to the regions of Tyre and Sidon to heal the Tyrians and Sidonians. But the Canaanite woman goes out from her former borders, in order to implore health for her daughter, crying out. Note that in the fifteenth place, the daughter of the Canaanite will be healed.


Have mercy on me, O Lord, Son of David. For he already knew how to call himself the Son of David, because he had already gone out of his own borders and had forsaken the error of the Tyrians and Sidonians in the exchange of place and faith.

My daughter is tormented by an evil spirit. I believe that the Canaanite people, who were tormented by evil spirits, were ignorant of the Creator and worshipped idols.

<h2 id='tocuniq325'>(Vers. 23.)</h2>

(Verse 23) He did not respond to him with a word. Not out of Pharisaic pride, nor from the disdain of the Scribes; but so that he himself would not seem to be going against his own command, by which he had ordered: Do not go into the way of the Gentiles, and do not enter into the cities of the Samaritans (above, X, 5). For he did not want to give occasion to the slanderers and reserved the perfect salvation of the Gentiles for the time of his passion and resurrection.

And his disciples approached him, saying: Send her away, for she is crying out after us. At that time, the disciples, still unaware of the mysteries of the Lord, or moved by mercy, were begging for the Canaanite woman, whom another Evangelist calls the Syrophoenician woman (Mark 7), or desiring to be free from her importunity; for she was loudly calling not as a merciful one, but as a harsh physician.

<h2 id='tocuniq326'>(Vers. 24.)</h2>

(Verse 24) But he answered and said, I am not sent but unto the lost sheep of the house of Israel. Not that he was not sent also to the Gentiles; but that he was sent first to Israel, that, their not receiving the Gospel, the transmigration might be made to the Gentiles. And he said significantly, unto the lost sheep of the house of Israel; that from this place we may also understand one erring sheep out of another parable.

<h2 id='tocuniq327'>(Vers. 25, 26.)</h2>

(Verse 25, 26) But she came and worshipped him, saying: Lord, help me. And he answering, said: It is not good to take the bread of the children, and to cast it to the dogs. The faith, patience, and humility of the woman of Canaan are preached through this character. Faith, by which she believed that her daughter could be healed. Patience, by which she persevered in prayer despite being ignored so many times. Humility, by which she compared herself not to dogs, but to puppies. However, the term "dogs" refers to the ethnic dogs, who are devoted to idolatry and are said to become rabid with the consumption of blood and the flesh of the dead. Note that this Canaanite woman persistently calls first David her son, then the Lord, and finally worships him as God.

<h2 id='tocuniq328'>(Vers. 27, 28.)</h2>

(Vers. 27, 28.) But she said: Yes, Lord. Even the small dogs eat the crumbs that fall from their masters' table. Then Jesus answered and said to her: O woman, great is your faith: let it be done to you as you desire. And her daughter was healed from that hour. I know, she says, that I do not deserve the bread of the children, nor can I eat whole meals; nor can I sit at the table with the father; but I am content with the scraps of the puppies; so through the humility of the crumbs, I can receive the greatness of the whole bread." } Oh marvelous change of things! Israel once a son, now we are dogs. Because of the diversity of faith, the order of names is changed. Concerning them it is said afterwards: Many dogs have surrounded me (Ps. XXI, 17). And: Behold the dogs, behold the 117 evil workers, behold the concision (Philippians III). We have heard with the Syrophoenician woman and the woman who had a flow of blood: Your faith is great, let it be done for you as you wish. And: Daughter, your faith has made you well.


<h2 id='tocuniq329'>(Vers. 29, 30.)</h2>

(Verse 29, 30.) And when Jesus had passed from there, he came near the Sea of Galilee: and going up into a mountain, he sat there. And many crowds approached him, having with them mute people, blind people, lame people, weak people, and many others. And they cast them at his feet. In the place where the Latin interpreter translated, weak people, it is written in Greek as κυλλοὺς, which is not a general name for weakness, but the name of a specific weakness: just as someone is called lame who limps with one foot, so κυλλὸς can be called someone who has one weak hand. We do not have the possession of this word. Hence, the evangelist explained the healings of the others in the following narratives, but was silent about theirs. For what follows?

<h2 id='tocuniq330'>(Vers. 31.)</h2>

(Verse 31.) And he healed them, so that the crowds marveled, seeing the mute speaking, the lame walking, the blind seeing: and they magnified the God of Israel. He was silent about the crippled, because he had nothing to say in opposition. This is about one word. But let us consider that the healed daughter of the Canaanite return to Judea, and to the Sea of Galilee, and ascend the mountain: and like a bird provoking its young to fly; there she may sit, and crowds may gather around him, leading or carrying with them variously afflicted individuals: whom he cured, and gave them food; and when this work was accomplished, he got into a boat, and came to the region of Magdala. And he went up the mountain and sat there, and the crowds came to him. Notice that the mute, the lame, and the blind are brought to the mountain to be healed by the Lord.

<h2 id='tocuniq331'>(Vers. 32.)</h2>

(Verse 32.) But Jesus, having summoned his disciples, said: I have compassion on the crowd, because they have persevered with me for three days already, and they do not have anything to eat. And I do not want to send them away fasting, lest they faint on the way. He wants to feed those whom he has healed; first, he takes away their weaknesses, so that later he may offer food to the healthy. He also summons his disciples and speaks to them about what he is about to do, in order to give an example to the teachers, that they should share their plans with the disciples and the younger ones, or that they may understand the greatness of the sign from their conversation, answering that they do not have any bread in the desert. He said, 'I have compassion on the crowd, because they have persevered with me for three days now. Let the crowd be compassionate, because they believed in the number of three days, to the Father, the Son, and the Holy Spirit. And they have nothing to eat. The crowd is always hungry and in need of food, unless they are satisfied by the Lord. And I do not want to send them away hungry, lest they faint on the way. They were hungry after great hardships and patiently expected food in the future. Jesus does not want to send them away hungry, lest they faint on the way.' Therefore, he who hastens to reach the desired dwelling without heavenly bread is in danger. Hence, the angel speaks to Elijah: Rise up and eat, for you are about to walk a long way (3 Kings 19:7).

<h2 id='tocuniq332'>(Vers. 33 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 33 et seq.) And his disciples say to him: From where then would we get so many loaves in the wilderness, as to satisfy such a great crowd? And Jesus said to them: How many loaves do you have? And they said: Seven, and a few small fish. And he commanded the crowd to sit down on the ground. And taking the seven loaves and the fish, and giving thanks, he broke them and gave them to his disciples: and the disciples gave them to the crowd. And they all ate and were satisfied. And what remained of the fragments, they took up seven baskets full. Now those who had eaten were four thousand men, besides women and children. And after dismissing the crowd, he got into the boat and went to the region of Magadan ((Μαγδαλά)). We have already mentioned this sign above, and it is idle to repeat the same: let us only dwell on those things which differ. Above we read: When evening came, the disciples approached him, saying: The place is deserted (Above, XIV, 15), and the rest. Having called together his disciples, the Lord himself speaks: I have compassion on the crowd, because they have persevered with me for three days already. There were five loaves and two fish there; here there are seven loaves and a few small fish. There they recline on the grass; here on the ground. There those who eat are five thousand, according to the number of loaves they eat; here four thousand. There twelve baskets are filled with the remains of the fragments; here seven baskets. Therefore, in the previous sign, those who were close and near to the five senses, the Lord himself does not remember them, but the disciples remember them in the evening of the neighboring night, and with the sun already setting. But the Lord himself remembers and says that he has compassion and explains the reason for his compassion: because they have been persevering with me for three days now (also with him, and with themselves), and he does not want to send them away hungry, lest they faint on the way. Those who are nourished by the seven loaves, that is, in the sacred number and perfect number, are not five thousand, but four thousand: a number that is always praised, and a square stone does not sway, and is not unstable; and for this reason also the Gospels are consecrated in that number.


<h2 id='tocuniq333'>(Chap. XVI.—Vers. 1 seqq.)</h2>

(Chapter 16, verses 1 and following.) And the Pharisees and Sadducees came to him, testing him and asking him to show them a sign from heaven. But he answered and said to them, “When it is evening, you say, ‘It will be fair weather, for the sky is red.’ And in the morning, ‘It will be stormy today, for the sky is red and threatening.’ You know how to discern the appearance of the sky, but you cannot discern the signs of the times. An evil and adulterous generation seeks for a sign, and a sign will not be given to it except the sign of Jonah the prophet.” This is not found in most manuscripts: it is evident that, from the order and consistency of the elements, both clear and rainy days can be predicted. However, the scribes and Pharisees, who seemed to be the teachers of the law, could not understand the coming of the Savior from the prophecy of the prophets.

<h2 id='tocuniq334'>(Vers. 5.)</h2>

(Verse 5) And leaving them, he went away. And when his disciples had come across the sea, they forgot to take bread. He said to them: 'When you have left the scribes and Pharisees, to whom he had said, 'An evil and adulterous generation seeks a sign, and a sign will not be given to it except the sign of Jonah the prophet,' he rightly went away across the sea and followed the peoples of the Gentiles. But what the sign of Jonah means for them has already been said above.'

<h2 id='tocuniq335'>(Vers. 6, 7.)</h2>

(Vers. 6, 7.) Look and beware of the leaven of the Pharisees and Sadducees. But they were thinking among themselves, saying: Because we have not taken bread. Whoever beware of the leaven of the Pharisees and Sadducees, does not keep the precepts of the Law and the teachings of the letters, neglects the traditions of men, in order to fulfill the commandment of God.

<h2 id='tocuniq336'>(Vers. 8 seqq.)</h2>

(v. 8 seqq.) But Jesus, knowing this, said to them: Why do you think among yourselves, O you of little faith, that you have no bread? Do you not yet understand or remember the five loaves for the five thousand men, and how many baskets you took up? Nor the seven loaves for the four thousand men, and how many baskets you took up? Why do you not understand that I did not speak to you about bread: Beware of the leaven of the Pharisees and Sadducees. Then they understood that he did not say beware of the leaven of bread, but of the teaching of the Pharisees and Sadducees. By occasion of the precept which the Saviour enjoined, saying: 'Beware of the leaven of the Pharisees and Sadducees,' He teaches what the five loaves and the seven signify: the five thousand men, and the four thousand, which were satisfied in the desert; which, though the greatness of the miracles is open, yet also another thing is demonstrated in the spiritual understanding. For if the leaven of the Pharisees and the Sadducees signifies not bodily bread, but perverse traditions and heretical dogmas, why should not the foods, by which the people of God were nourished, signify the true and whole doctrine? Let someone inquire and say: How is it that the loaves they did not have, who immediately filled seven baskets, they got into the boat and came to the region of Magdala: and there they heard from the sailors that they should beware of the leaven of the Pharisees and Sadducees? But Scripture testifies that they forgot to take them with them. This is the leaven that the Apostle is speaking of; A little leaven corrupts the whole mass (1 Corinthians 5:6). Marcion, Valentinus, and all heretics had this kind of leaven, which should be avoided by all means. This fermentation has the power that if it is mixed with flour, which seemed small, it grows larger and draws the whole mixture to its own flavor. Similarly, heretical teaching, if it has thrown even a small spark into your heart, in a short time grows into a huge flame and draws the whole possession of the person to itself. Finally, it follows: Then they understood that he did not say to beware of the yeast of bread, but of the teaching of the Pharisees and Sadducees.


<h2 id='tocuniq337'>Third Book</h2>

Third Book

<h2 id='tocuniq338'>(Vers. 13.)</h2>

(Verse 13) 121 But Jesus came into the region of Caesarea Philippi. This Philip is the brother of Herod, of whom we spoke above, a tetrarch of Ituraea and Trachonitis, who built in honor of Tiberius Caesar Caesarea, which is now called Paneas, and in honor of Caesar, and also in honor of himself, he named it Caesarea Philippi, and it is in the province of Phoenicia: imitating his father Herod, who named Caesarea in honor of Augustus Caesar, which was previously called the tower of Strato, and he built it across the Jordan in the name of his daughter Julia. This place (which others call that place) is Caesarea Philippi, where the Jordan River rises at the foot of Mount Lebanon, and it has two springs, one called Jor, and the other Dan, which when mixed together, become the Jordan River.

And he asked his disciples, saying: Whom do men say that the Son of man is? He did not say, whom do men say that I am, but the Son of man: lest he should seem to boast of himself. And note, that wherever it is written in the Old Testament, son of man, in Hebrew it is written, son of Adam. As it is also written, which we read in the psalm: Sons of men, how long will you be of heavy heart (Psalm 4:3), which in Hebrew is said, sons of Adam. But beautifully he asks: Whom do people say that the Son of Man is? For those who speak of the Son of Man are human: but those who understand his divinity are not human, but are called gods.

<h2 id='tocuniq339'>(Vers. 14.)</h2>

(Verse 14.) But they said: Some say John the Baptist, others Elijah, and others Jeremiah, or one of the prophets. Jesus said to them, I marvel that some interpreters search for the causes of individual errors, and weave a very long discussion about why some believed our Lord Jesus Christ to be John, others Elijah, others Jeremiah, or one of the prophets, when they could have erred in Elijah and Jeremiah just as Herod erred in John, saying, 'I have beheaded John, but he has risen from the dead, and miracles are being performed by him' (Mark 6:16).


<h2 id='tocuniq340'>(Vers. 15, 16.)</h2>

(Verse 15, 16.) But who do you say that I am? Simon Peter answered, 'You are the Christ, the Son of the living God.' Wise reader, pay attention, for from the following words and the context of the discourse, the apostles are not called men, but gods. For when he said, 'Who do men say that the Son of Man is?' he added, 'But who do you say that I am?' They, being men, relying on human opinions; but you, who are gods, what do you think of me being? Peter, in the name of all the apostles, proclaims: You are the Christ, the Son of the living God. He calls Him the living God, in distinction from those gods who are thought to be gods, but are dead: Saturn, Jupiter, Venus, Minerva (or Ceres), Bacchus, Hercules, and the like, which are mere prodigies of idols.

<h2 id='tocuniq341'>(Vers. 17.)</h2>

(Verse 17.) But Jesus answered and said to him: Blessed are you, Simon Barjona, for flesh and blood has not revealed this to you, but my Father who is in heaven. The Apostles testify of themselves. Peter had said: You are the Christ, the Son of the living God; a true confession received a reward: Blessed are you, Simon Barjona. Why? because flesh and blood did not reveal this to you, but the Father revealed it. What flesh and blood could not reveal, was revealed by the grace of the Holy Spirit. Therefore, from confession he obtains the name, because he has a revelation from the Holy Spirit, of whom he is also to be called the son. For Barjona in our language means 'son of a dove', as others simply understand that Simon, that is, Peter, is the son of John, according to the question in another place: 'Simon of Jonas, lovest thou me?' (John 21:15). He answered: 'Lord, thou knowest.' And by an error of the writers, they corrupt it as Bar Joanna, that is, son of John, with one syllable being removed. However, Joanna is interpreted as 'by the grace of the Lord.' Both names can be understood mystically, as both the dove, the Holy Spirit, and the grace of God signify a spiritual gift. Also, what he says, 'For flesh and blood has not revealed this to you,' is compared to the Apostolic narrative where he says, 'I did not immediately consult with flesh and blood' (Galatians 1:16), 'flesh and blood' signifying the Jews, so that here also it may be shown in a different sense that Christ the Son of God was revealed to him not by the teaching of the Pharisees, but by the grace of God.


<h2 id='tocuniq342'>(Vers. 18.)</h2>

(Verse 18.) And I say to you. What is it that he says: And I say to you? Because you told me: You are the Christ, the Son of the living God: and I say to you, not in vain words, and having no effect, but I say to you: that what I have said, I have done.

Because you are Peter, and upon this rock I will build my Church. Just as he himself gave the light to the apostles, so that they were called the light of the world, and they received other names from the Lord: in the same way, he bestowed the name of Peter upon Simon, who believed in Christ the rock. But according to the metaphor of the rock, it is rightly said to him: I will build my Church upon you.

And the gates of hell shall not prevail against it. I consider the gates of hell to be vices and sins: or certainly the doctrines of heretics, through which deceived men are led to Tartarus. Therefore, let no one think that it is said concerning death, that the apostles were not subject to the condition of death, whose martyrdoms he sees shining.

<h2 id='tocuniq343'>(Vers. 19.)</h2>

(Verse 19) And I will give you the keys of the kingdom of heaven. And whatever you bind on earth shall be bound in heaven, and whatever you loose on earth shall be loosed in heaven. The bishops and priests who do not understand this passage assume something for themselves from the Pharisees, either to condemn the innocent or to consider themselves free when they are guilty; for before God, it is not the opinion of the priests but the life of the accused that is sought. In Leviticus (Chapter XIV) we read about leprosy, where they are commanded to show themselves to the priests, and if they have leprosy, then they are made unclean by the priest. Not that the priests make lepers unclean; but so that they have knowledge of who is leprous and who is not, and can discern who is clean and who is unclean. Just as in that case the priest declares the leper clean or unclean, so here the bishop and priest bind or loose, not those who are innocent or guilty; but according to their office, when they have heard the varieties of sins, they know who should be bound and who should be released.


<h2 id='tocuniq344'>(Vers. 20.)</h2>

(Verse 20.) Then he commanded his disciples not to tell anyone that he was Jesus Christ. Previously, when he sent the disciples to preach, he had instructed them to proclaim his coming: here he commanded them not to say that he was Jesus Christ. It seems to me that preaching Christ is one thing, and preaching Jesus Christ is another. Christ is a common name of dignity; Jesus is the proper name of the Savior. However, it is possible that before his passion and resurrection, he did not want to be proclaimed for this reason; and after the completion of the sacrament of his blood, he would more appropriately say to the apostles: Go and teach all nations (Matthew 28:19), etc. Lest anyone think that our understanding is only intellectual and not guided by the Gospel, the following reasons explain the prohibition of preaching at that time.

<h2 id='tocuniq345'>(Vers. 21.)</h2>

(Verse 21) Then Jesus began to show his disciples that he must go to Jerusalem and suffer many things from the elders and chief priests and scribes, and be killed, and on the third day be raised. And the meaning is: Proclaim me then, when I have suffered these things, for it is not profitable to publicly proclaim Christ and make known his majesty to the people, who will soon witness him being scourged and crucified, and suffering many things from the elders, chief priests, and scribes. And now Jesus suffers many things from those who crucify the Son of God again (Heb. VI): and while the elders are thought to be in the Church, and the chief priests, following the simple letter, kill the Son of God, who is fully felt in spirit.

<h2 id='tocuniq346'>(Vers. 22, 23.)</h2>

(Verses 22, 23.) And taking him, Peter began to rebuke him, saying: Far be it from you, Lord, this shall not be to you. But he turned and said to Peter: Go behind me, Satan, you are a stumbling block to me; for you are not mindful of the things of God, but the things of men. We have often said that Peter had excessive zeal and love for the Lord and Savior. Therefore, after his confession, in which he said: You are the Christ, the Son of the living God; and after hearing the Savior's reward: Blessed are you, Simon Barjona, for flesh and blood has not revealed this to you, but my Father who is in heaven, he suddenly hears from the Lord that he must go to Jerusalem and suffer many things from the elders and scribes and chief priests, and be killed, and on the third day rise again, he does not want his confession to be destroyed; nor does he think it possible for the Son of God to be killed; and he takes him into his affection, or leads him aside, so as not to appear to argue with the teacher in the presence of the other disciples, and with the affection of a lover, and desiring, he begins to say: Far be it from you, Lord; or as it is better expressed in Greek, ἵλεώς σοι, Κύριε, οὐ μὴ ἔσται σοι τοῦτο, which means, be propitious to yourself, Lord, this shall not be to you: it cannot happen, and my ears do not accept that the Son of God shall be killed. To whom the Lord turned, He said: Go away from me, Satan, you are a stumbling block to me. Satan is interpreted as adversary or opponent. Because you speak contrary to my will, you must be called an adversary. Many think that it was not Peter who was rebuked, but the spirit of the adversary who suggested these things to the Apostle. But to me, this is an apostolic error, coming from affection for piety, it will never seem like an incentive from the devil: Go away from me, Satan. The devil says: Go away. Peter listens: Go away from me, that is, follow my opinion: because you do not understand the things that are of God, but the things that are of men. It is my will, and the Father's (whose will I came to do (John 6)) to die for the salvation of mankind, while you, considering only your own will, do not want a grain of wheat to fall into the ground, so that it may bear much fruit (John 12). The prudent reader may inquire how, after such great blessings: Blessed are you, Simon Barona; and: You are Peter; and upon this rock I will build my Church; and the gates of hell shall not prevail against it; and: I will give you the keys of the kingdom of heaven; and: Whatever you bind on earth will be bound in heaven, and whatever you loose on earth will be loosed in heaven; now he hears: Go away from me, Satan, you are a stumbling block to me? But what kind of sudden conversion is this, that after so great rewards, he is called Satan? But if he who seeks this considers, he will understand that to Peter that blessing and beatitude, and power, and the edification upon him of the Church, are promised in the future, not given in the present. I will build, says He, my Church upon you, and the gates of hell shall not prevail against it. And: I will give you the keys of the kingdom of heaven. All these things are about the future, which if He had immediately given to him, the mistaken opinion would never have found a place in him.


<h2 id='tocuniq347'>(Vers. 24 seqq.)</h2>

(Verses 24 onward) Then Jesus said to his disciples: If anyone wants to come after me, let him deny himself and take up his cross and follow me. For whoever wants to save his life will lose it, but whoever loses his life for my sake will find it. For what will it profit a man if he gains the whole world but forfeits his soul? Whoever puts off the old man with his works (Colossians 3), denies himself, saying: I no longer live, but Christ lives in me (Galatians 2:20): and he takes up his cross and is crucified to the world. But to whom the world has been crucified, he follows the crucified Lord.

But what will a man give in exchange for his soul? For Israel, Egypt and Ethiopia are given in exchange, and Syene (Isaiah XLIII, 3, 4): for the human soul, that alone is the retribution, which the Psalmist sings: What shall I render to the Lord for all that he has rendered to me? I will take the cup of salvation, and call upon the name of the Lord (Psalm CXV, 3).

<h2 id='tocuniq348'>(Vers. 27.)</h2>

(Verse 27.) For the Son of Man is going to come in the glory of His Father with His angels, and then He will repay each one according to his deeds. Peter, shocked by the preaching of the Lord's death, was rebuked by the Lord's statement: the disciples were provoked to deny themselves, take up their cross, and follow their Master with a mindset of dying. A great terror for those who hear, and if possible, even to instill fear in the chief of the apostles; therefore, joyful things follow the sorrowful, and He says: the Son of Man is going to come in the glory of His Father with His angels. Fear death, listen to the glory of the triumphant. You fear the cross, listen to the ministries of the angels. And then, it says, he will render to each one according to his works (Rom. X, 12). There is no distinction between Jew and Gentile, man and woman, poor and rich, where not persons, but works are considered.

<h2 id='tocuniq349'>(Vers. 28.)</h2>

(Verse 28) Truly I tell you, there are some standing here who will not taste death until they see the Son of Man coming in his kingdom. He desired to heal the terror of the apostles with the hope of promises, saying: The Son of Man is coming in the glory of his Father with his angels. Moreover, with the authority of a judge added: and he will render to each one according to his works. The silent thought of the apostles could endure such a scandal: you say that death and killing will come now, but that you promise to be present in the glory of the Father with the ministries of angels and the power of a judge, this will happen day by day, and will be postponed for a long time. Therefore, foreseeing what the experts of hidden things could object, he offsets present fear with present reward. For what does he say? There are some standing here who will not taste death until they see the Son of Man coming in his kingdom; so that the manner in which he will come afterwards is demonstrated to you at the present time because of your disbelief.

<h2 id='tocuniq350'>(Chap. XVII.—Vers. 1.)</h2>

(Chapter 17 - Verse 1) And after six days, Jesus took Peter, and James, and John his brother. Why Peter, and James, and John are separated from the others in some places in the Gospels, or what privilege they have over the other apostles, we have frequently mentioned. Now it is asked how he took them after six days, and led them into a high mountain apart: since the evangelist Luke mentions the number eight (Luke 9). But the answer is easy, because here the middle days are included, the first and the last are added. For it is not said: After eight days Jesus took Peter, and James, and John; but on the eighth day.

He leads them to a high mountain apart. To lead disciples to the mountains is part of the kingdom. They are led apart, because many are called, but few are chosen (Matthew 20:16 and 22:14).

<h2 id='tocuniq351'>(Vers. 2.)</h2>

(Verse 2.) And he was transfigured before them. Just as he will be at the time of judgment, so he appeared to the apostles. Now when it is said: he was transfigured before them, no one can think that he lost or gave up his original form and appearance, or that he lost the reality of his body and assumed a spiritual or airy body; but how he was transformed, the evangelist explains, saying.

And his face shone like the sun, and his garments became white as snow. When the splendor of his face is revealed, and the whiteness of his garments is described, it is not the substance that is taken away, but the glory is changed. His face shone like the sun. Indeed, the Lord was transformed into that glory in which he will come afterwards in his kingdom. The transformation added splendor, it did not take away his face. Even if his body was spiritual, were his garments also changed, which were so white that another evangelist said: 'Such as no fuller on earth can make' (Mark 9:3)." } But what an eclipse can do over the Earth, is corporal, and is subject to touch, and is not spiritual and airy, so that it deceives the eyes, and can only be seen in an illusion.

<h2 id='tocuniq352'>(Vers. 3.)</h2>

(Verse 3.) And behold, Moses and Elijah appeared to them, speaking with him. When the scribes and Pharisees tested him, demanding signs from heaven, he did not want to give them, but refuted their evil request with a wise response. However, to increase the faith of the apostles, he gives a sign from heaven, with Elijah descending from where he had ascended, and with Moses rising from the underworld. This is also commanded to Ahaz through Isaiah, to ask for a sign from the highest or from the depths (Isa. VII and IV Kings II). For what was said: Moses and Elijah appeared to them, speaking with him; and in another Gospel it is reported that he had announced what he would suffer in Jerusalem (Luke 9): The law and the prophets are shown, who proclaimed with frequent words both the Lord's passion and resurrection.

<h2 id='tocuniq353'>(Vers. 4.)</h2>

(Verse 4.) But Peter, responding, said to Jesus: Lord, it is good for us to be here. He who had climbed the mountains does not want to descend to earthly things; but instead, to always persevere in the lofty things.

If you wish, let us make here three tabernacles: one for you, one for Moses, and one for Elijah. You are mistaken, Peter, as the other evangelist testifies. You do not know what you are saying (Luke 9). Do not seek three tabernacles, for there is one tabernacle of the Gospel, in which the Law and the Prophets are to be recapitulated. But if you seek three tabernacles, do not compare servants with the Lord, but make three tabernacles: indeed, one for the Father, and the Son, and the Holy Spirit; so that as they have one divinity, there may be one tabernacle also in your heart.


<h2 id='tocuniq354'>(Vers. 5.)</h2>

(Verse 5) While he was still speaking, behold a bright cloud overshadowed them. And behold a voice out of the cloud, saying: This is my beloved Son, in whom I am well pleased. Hear him. Because he had asked foolishly, he does not deserve the Lord's answer, but the Father answers for the Son, so that the word of the Lord may be fulfilled: I do not testify about myself, but the Father who sent me testifies about me (John 5:37, and 8:18). But the cloud appears bright and shadowed, so that those who sought the tabernacle made of branches or tents would be covered by the shade of the bright cloud. 131 A voice also from heaven is heard speaking of the Father, which also bears witness to the Son; and by removing Peter's error, teaches the truth: or rather, by Peter, the other apostles. This is, he says, my beloved Son: to him the tabernacle must be fixed, to him obedience must be given. Here is the son, those servants are: Moses and Elias must also prepare a tabernacle for the Lord in the innermost parts of their heart, along with you.

<h2 id='tocuniq355'>(Vers. 6.)</h2>

(Verse 6) And when the disciples heard this, they fell on their faces and were greatly afraid. They were terrified for three reasons: either because they knew they had made a mistake, or because a bright cloud had covered them, or because they had heard the voice of God the Father speaking. For human weakness cannot bear the sight of greater glory, and trembling with their whole being, they fall to the ground. The more someone seeks higher things, the more they will collapse into lower things if they are ignorant of their own limits.


<h2 id='tocuniq356'>(Vers. 7.)</h2>

(Verse 7.) And Jesus approached and touched them. Because they were lying down and unable to rise, he kindly approached and touched them, so that fear would depart with his touch and their weakened bodies would be strengthened.

And he said to them: Rise up and do not be afraid. Those whom he had healed with his hand, he heals with his command. Do not be afraid. The first fear is expelled, so that later instruction may be given.

<h2 id='tocuniq357'>(Vers. 8.)</h2>

(Verse 8) But lifting up their eyes, they saw no one except Jesus alone. Reasonably, after they had risen, they saw no one except Jesus alone: so that if Moses and Elijah had continued with the Lord, the uncertain voice of the Father would not be seen, to whom it would give testimony most of all. Therefore, they see Jesus standing, the cloud having been taken away, and Moses and Elijah vanishing: because after the shadow of the Law and the Prophets has departed, which had covered the apostles with its veil, both lights are found in the Gospel.


<h2 id='tocuniq358'>(Vers. 9.)</h2>

(Vers. 9.) And as they were coming down from the mountain, Jesus commanded them, saying: Tell no one the vision, until the Son of Man rises from the dead. The anticipation of the future kingdom and the glory of the triumphant were shown on the mountain. Therefore, he does not want this to be preached to the people, so that it would not be considered unbelievable because of the magnitude of the matter, and so that the cross that follows after such glory would not become a stumbling block for simple minds.

<h2 id='tocuniq359'>(Vers. 10.)</h2>

(Ver. 10.) And his disciples asked him, saying: Why then do the scribes say that Elias must first come? Unless we know the reasons why the disciples asked about the name of Elias, their questioning seems foolish and extraordinary. For what does it have to do with those things which are written above, to inquire about the coming of Elias? The tradition of the Pharisees is, according to the prophet Malachi (who is the last of the twelve), that Elias will come before the coming of the Savior and restore the hearts of the fathers to the children, and the hearts of the children to their fathers, and restore all things to their original state (Malachi 4)." } Therefore, the disciples estimate that this transformation of glory, which they see on the mountain, is the one they have been waiting for. And they say: If you have already come in glory, why does your forerunner not appear, especially since they saw Elijah depart. However, when they add: The scribes say that Elijah must come first: By saying 'first', they show that unless Elijah comes, the coming of the Savior according to the Scriptures will not happen.

<h2 id='tocuniq360'>(Vers. 11, 12.)</h2>

(Verse 11, 12) But he answered and said to them: Elijah indeed shall come first and restore all things. But I say to you, that Elijah is already come, and they knew him not, but have done unto him whatsoever they had a mind. So also the Son of man shall suffer from them. Then the disciples understood that he had spoken to them of John the Baptist.

And they did not recognize him, but they did to him whatever they wanted: That is, they rejected him and beheaded him.

<h2 id='tocuniq361'>(Vers. 13.)</h2>

(Verse 13.) And so the Son of Man is also going to suffer at their hands. Then the disciples understood that he had spoken to them about John the Baptist. However, it is wondered how they can also be said to have crucified Jesus when we read that he was killed by the scribes and Pharisees? And to answer briefly, it is because the faction of the Pharisees consented to the death of John, and Herod joined his will in the killing of the Lord: he sent him back to Pilate to be crucified after mocking and despising him.


<h2 id='tocuniq362'>(Vers. 14, 15.)</h2>

(Verse 14, 15.) Lord, have mercy on my son, for he is epileptic and suffers greatly; often he falls into fire and often into water. And I brought him to your disciples, and they could not heal him. For this reason, the demon, observing the course of the moon, tries to possess men and defame the Creator through his creatures, as we have said before. But it seems to me, according to the allegory, that the epileptic is someone who is constantly changing his vices from moment to moment, and does not persist in what he starts, but grows and diminishes: now he is thrown into the fire, where the hearts of adulterers are kindled (Hosea 7); now into waters that cannot extinguish love. But when he says, 'I have brought him to your disciples, and they could not heal him,' he is secretly accusing the apostles, since the inability to heal is sometimes not due to the weakness of those who heal, but to the faith of those who need healing, as the Lord says, 'It shall be done to you according to your faith' (Mark 5:34 and 10:52).

<h2 id='tocuniq363'>(Vers. 16.)</h2>

(Verse 16.) But Jesus answered and said: O unbelieving and perverse generation, how long will I be with you? How long shall I bear with you? Bring him here to me. Not that he has been overcome with weariness, and is gentle and meek, who did not open his mouth as a lamb before the shearer (Isaiah 53), nor did he burst forth in words of fury; but rather, like a physician, if he sees a sick person behaving contrary to his instructions, he may say: How long shall I come to your house, until I lose the skill of my profession, me commanding one thing, and you committing another? But he was not angry with the man, but with the fault; and because of one man, he accused the Jews of unfaithfulness, so he immediately said: Bring him here to me.

<h2 id='tocuniq364'>(Vers. 17.)</h2>

(Verse 17.) And Jesus rebuked him, and the demon came out of him, and the boy was healed from that hour. It was not the boy who was suffering, but the demon who deserved to be rebuked. Whether he rebuked the boy and the demon came out of him, because he had been oppressed by the demon due to his sins.

<h2 id='tocuniq365'>(Vers. 18.)</h2>

(Verse 18.) And they said, why were we not able to cast him out? Jesus said to them: Because of your unbelief. Amen, I say to you. This is what he says in another place: Whatever you ask in my name, believing, you shall receive (John 15:2). Therefore, whenever we do not receive, it is not an impossibility on the part of the one who grants, but a fault of those who pray.

<h2 id='tocuniq366'>(Vers. 19.)</h2>

(Verse 19) If you have faith like a mustard seed, you will say to this mountain, 'Move from here to there,' and it will move. And nothing will be impossible for you. Some people think that faith compared to a mustard seed is small because the kingdom of heaven is compared to a mustard seed, but the apostle says, 'And if I have all faith, so that I could remove mountains' (I Cor. XV, 2). Therefore, great is the faith that is equal to a mustard seed. The movement of the mountain does not refer to the one we see with our physical eyes, but to the one who had been transported by the Lord from the lunatic." } For when he says, 'Say to this mountain, 'Move from here to there,' and it will move,' it is understood as referring to the devil. From this, those who argue that the apostles and all believers did not even have a small amount of faith are proven to be foolish, because none of them moved mountains. For the translation of a mountain from one place to another is not so profitable, nor is the seeking of empty signs, as the transfer of this mountain is necessary for the benefit of all, which is said by the prophet to corrupt the whole earth (Zach. IV).


<h2 id='tocuniq367'>(Vers. 20.)</h2>

(Verse 20) However, this kind is not cast out, except by prayer and fasting. While he teaches how the most wicked demon can be expelled, he instructs everyone to live.

<h2 id='tocuniq368'>(Vers. 21 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 21 and following) While they were conversing in Galilee, Jesus said to them: The Son of Man must be handed over to the hands of men, and they will kill him; and on the third day he will rise again. And they were greatly saddened. He always mixes sadness with prosperity, so that when they come suddenly, they will not terrify the apostles; but rather, let them be carried by premeditated souls: For if they are saddened by his impending death, they should be rejoiced by what is said about his resurrection on the third day. Furthermore, what causes them sadness, and causes them great sadness, does not come from unfaithfulness (otherwise they would have known that Peter was rebuked for not understanding the things of God, but the things of men), but rather because out of love for their teacher, they are willing to hear nothing negative or humiliating about him.

<h2 id='tocuniq369'>(Vers. 24.)</h2>

(Version 24.) And when they came to Capernaum, those who collected the didrachma went up to Peter and said, “Does your Teacher not pay the didrachma?” He said, “Yes.” After Augustus Caesar, Judea became subject to taxation, and all were registered. And so Joseph, with Mary his cousin, went up to Bethlehem to be registered. Again, since he was brought up in Nazareth (which is a town in Galilee near the city of Capernaum), they demand the taxes according to custom. And because of the greatness of the signs, those who collected them do not dare to ask Jesus himself, but they approach one of his disciples and maliciously ask whether he will pay the taxes or refuse to comply with Caesar's will, as we read in another place: Is it lawful to pay the tribute to Caesar or not? (Mark 12:14)" }


And when he entered the house, Jesus anticipated him, saying: What thinkest thou, Simon? Of whom do the kings of the earth take tribute or pollage? Of their own children or strangers?

<h2 id='tocuniq370'>(Vers. 25.)</h2>

(Verse 25.) What do you think, Simon? Do the kings of the earth receive tribute or taxes from their own sons or from strangers? And he said, from strangers. Then Jesus said to him: So, the sons are free. Our Lord, both according to the flesh and according to the spirit, was the son of a king, either being born from the lineage of David or the Word of the Almighty Father. Therefore, as a son of a king, he should not pay tribute like the other kings, but he who took on the lowliness of the flesh should fulfill all righteousness. And we, miserable as we are, who are called by the name of Christ, and do nothing worthy of such greatness: he suffered the cross for us, and paid the tribute, we do not pay the tribute for his honor, and we are immune as if we were children of a king.

<h2 id='tocuniq371'>(Vers. 26.)</h2>

(Verse 26) But lest we should scandalize them: go to the sea, and cast in a hook, and that fish which shall first come up, take: and when thou hast opened its mouth, thou shalt find a stater: take that, and give it to them for me and thee. What I should first admire in this place, I know not, whether his foreknowledge or the greatness of the Savior. Foreknowledge, because he knew that the fish would have a stater in its mouth, and that he himself would be the first to be caught. Greatness and power, if at his word the stater is immediately created in the mouth of the fish, and he by speaking has made what was to come to pass." } But it seems to me, according to mystical understanding, that this is the fish that was first caught, which was in the depths of the sea, and dwelt in salty and bitter depths, in order to be freed through the second Adam from the first Adam. And that which was found in its mouth, that is, in its confession, was rendered for Peter and the Lord. And indeed, the same thing is given a price, but it is divided, because the price was rendered for Peter as if for a sinner: but our Lord had not committed sin, nor was deceit found in his mouth (Isaiah 53). The word 'stater' is used, which means two didrachms, in order to show the likeness of the flesh, while both the servant and the Lord are redeemed for the same price. But it also builds understanding simply for the listener: that the Lord was of such great poverty that He did not have the means to pay taxes for Himself and the apostle. And if someone wants to object: how then did Judas carry money in his purse? We will respond that he considered it wrong to convert the funds of the poor for his own use, and he gave us the same example.


<h2 id='tocuniq372'>(Chap. XVIII.—Vers. 1.)</h2>

(Chapter XVIII.—Verse 1) At that time the disciples came to Jesus, saying: Who do you think is the greatest in the kingdom of heaven? As I have often mentioned, it is worth noting again. The reasons for investigating each of the Lord's words and actions are to be sought. After finding the coin, after paying the taxes, what does the sudden question of the apostles mean? At that time the disciples came to Jesus, saying: Who do you think is the greatest in the kingdom of heaven?" } Because they had seen the tribute given to Peter and the Lord, and because of the equality of price, they thought that Peter should be preeminent over all the apostles, who had been compared to the Lord in the giving of the tribute. Therefore, they ask who is greater in the kingdom of heaven? And Jesus, seeing their thoughts and understanding the reasons for their error, desires to heal the desire for glory through a competition of humility.

<h2 id='tocuniq373'>(Vers. 2.)</h2>

(Vers. 2.) And calling a little child, he set him in their midst, and said, Truly I say to you, unless you turn and become like children, you will never enter the kingdom of heaven. Whoever humbles himself like this child is the greatest in the kingdom of heaven.


<h2 id='tocuniq374'>(Vers. 3.)</h2>

(Verse 3.) Amen, I say to you, unless you are converted and become like little children, you will not enter the kingdom of heaven. The apostles are not commanded to have the age of children, but to have their innocence, and what they possess through the years, let these possess through diligence: so that they may be like little children in malice, not in wisdom.

<h2 id='tocuniq375'>(Vers. 4.)</h2>

(Verse 4.) Therefore, whoever humbles himself like this little child, he is the greatest in the kingdom of heaven. Like this little child, whose example I give to you, he does not persist in anger, does not hold a grudge, does not find delight in seeing a beautiful woman, does not think one thing and speak another; so unless you have such innocence and purity of heart, you cannot enter the kingdom of heaven. Or another way: Therefore, whoever humbles himself like this little child, he is the greatest in the kingdom of heaven. Whoever imitates me and humbles himself as I have humbled myself, taking on the form of a servant, will enter the kingdom of heaven (Philippians 2:8).

<h2 id='tocuniq376'>(Vers. 5.)</h2>

(Version 5.) And whoever welcomes such a little child in my name, welcomes me. Whoever is such, that he imitates the humility and innocence of Christ, in him Christ is welcomed. And wisely, lest when it is brought to the apostles, they think themselves honored, he added that they should be welcomed not because of their own merit, but because of the honor of the master.

<h2 id='tocuniq377'>(Vers. 6.)</h2>

(Verse 6.) But whoever causes one of these little ones who believe in me to stumble, it is better for him that a millstone be hung around his neck and he be thrown into the sea.

Let him be hanged with a millstone around his neck and thrown into the depths of the sea. Although this general opinion can be applied against all who scandalize someone, it can also be understood, based on the context of the discourse, as being directed against the apostles. They appeared to be competing with each other for dignity when they asked who would be greater in the kingdom of heaven. If they had persisted in this vice, they could have caused those whom they were calling to faith to stumble and perish through their scandal, while witnessing the apostles fighting among themselves for honor. But when he said, 'It is expedient for him that a millstone be hanged about his neck,' he speaks according to the custom of the province, by which those guilty of greater crimes among the ancient Jews were punished by being sunk in the depths with a bound stone. It is expedient for him, because it is much better to receive a brief punishment for guilt than to be preserved in eternal tortures. For the Lord will not judge (or punish) twice for the same thing (Nahum 1).

<h2 id='tocuniq378'>(Vers. 7.)</h2>

(Verse 7) Woe to the world because of scandals. For it is necessary that scandals come, but woe to that man through whom the scandal comes.

Not because it is necessary for stumbling blocks to come, otherwise those who cause stumbling would be without fault, but because it is necessary for stumbling blocks to occur in this world, each person is exposed to stumbling through their own fault. And at the same time, Judas is struck by a general consensus, as he had prepared his mind for betrayal.

<h2 id='tocuniq379'>(Vers. 8, 9.)</h2>

(Verse 8, 9) But if your hand or your foot causes you to stumble, cut it off and throw it away. It is better for you to enter life maimed or crippled than to have two hands or two feet and be thrown into the eternal fire. And if your eye causes you to stumble, gouge it out and throw it away. It is better for you to enter life with one eye than to have two eyes and be thrown into the fire of hell.  It is necessary for scandals to come, but woe to the man by whom the scandal comes. Therefore, every affection is cut off, and every relationship is severed, so that no one among the believers may be exposed to scandal through an opportunity for piety. If, he says, someone is so closely connected to you, like a hand, foot, eye, and is useful and attentive, and sharp in discernment, but causes you scandal and drags you into hell because of a disagreement in morals, it is better for you to be devoid of his closeness and carnal benefits, so that while you desire to profit your relatives and necessary acquaintances, you do not have a cause for ruin. So, neither brother, nor wife, nor sons, nor friends, nor any affection that can exclude us from the kingdom of heaven, should be preferred to the love of the Lord. Each believer knows what harms them or distracts their mind, and is often tempted. It is better to lead a solitary life than to lose eternal life for the sake of the necessities of this present life.

<h2 id='tocuniq380'>(Vers. 10, 11.)</h2>

(Verse 10, 11.) See that you do not despise one of these little ones. For I say to you that their angels in heaven always behold the face of my Father who is in heaven. For the Son of man has come to save that which was lost. He had said before that all close relationships and attachments that could cause scandal should be cut off by hand, foot, or eye: Therefore, he tempers the severity of the sentence with the given command, saying: See that you do not despise one of these little ones. Thus, he said, I command severity so that I may teach mercy to be mingled. However much there is in you, do not despise, but seek their well-being even for the sake of your own salvation. But if you see them persisting in sins and serving vices, it is better for you to be saved alone than to perish with many. For their angels in heaven always see the face of the Father. Great is the dignity of souls, that each one has an angel assigned to guard it from birth. Where we read in the Apocalypse of John: To the angel of the church in Ephesus, Thyatira, and to the angel of Philadelphia, and to the angels of the other four churches, write these things (Apoc. I, 2, 3). The Apostle also instructs women to cover their heads in the churches, because of the angels (I Cor. XI).

<h2 id='tocuniq381'>(Vers. 12, 13.)</h2>

(Verse 12, 13.) What do you think? If someone has a hundred sheep, and one of them goes astray, will he not leave the ninety-nine on the mountains and go in search of the one that went astray? And if he happens to find it, truly I tell you, he rejoices more over it than over the ninety-nine that did not go astray. Furthermore, he appeals to compassion, saying: See that you do not despise one of these little ones, and he adds the parable of the ninety-nine sheep left on the mountains and the one that went astray, which the good shepherd, because of its great weakness, could not walk and carried on his shoulders to the rest of the flock. Some think that he, being in the form of God, did not consider robbery to be equal with God; but he emptied himself, taking the form of a servant, becoming obedient to the Father unto death, even death on a cross (Philippians 2:6-8): and for this reason, he descended to the earthly realm to save the one lost sheep, that is, the human race. Others, however, think that the number ninety-nine refers to the righteous sheep; and in the one sheep, the sinner, as he said in another place: I have not come to call the righteous, but sinners: for it is not the healthy who need a doctor, but the sick (Luke 5:32). This parable is written in the Gospel according to Luke together with two other parables: the parable of the ten drachmas and the parable of the two sons (Luke 15).

<h2 id='tocuniq382'>(Vers. 14.)</h2>

(Verse 14.) Thus it is not the will of your Father who is in heaven that one of these little ones should perish. He refers to the previous proposition, of which he had said: Take heed that you do not despise one of these little ones; and he teaches therefore by means of a parable, that the little ones should not be despised. And in that which he says: It is not the will of your Father that one of these little ones should perish: whenever one of these little ones perishes, it is shown that it is not by the will of the Father.


<h2 id='tocuniq383'>(Vers. 15 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 15 and following) But if your brother sins against you, go and confront him alone, between you and him alone. If he listens to you, you have gained your brother. But if he does not listen, take one or two others with you, so that by the testimony of two or three witnesses every word may be confirmed. And if he refuses to listen to them, tell it to the church. And if he refuses to listen even to the church, let him be to you as a Gentile and a tax collector. If our brother sins against us and harms us in any way, we have the power, indeed the requirement, to forgive our debtors just as it is commanded.
