There were no Gentiles on the highways, but at the exits of the highways. However, it is questioned how some of the bad ones found among those who were outside, and there were some good ones. The Apostle to the Romans discusses this matter more fully (also adding) (Rom. II, 14): that the Gentiles, who naturally do the things that are of the law, condemn the Jews who have not made the written law. Among the Gentiles themselves, there is also infinite diversity; for we know that some are inclined to vices and rush towards evil, while others are devoted to the virtues of a noble character.

<h2 id='tocuniq459'>(Vers. 11, 12.)</h2>

(Verse 11, 12.) However, the king came in to see the guests, and he saw there a man who was not wearing a wedding garment, and he said to him: Friend, how did you come in here without a wedding garment? But he was silent. Those who had been invited to the wedding feast had filled it from hedges and corners and streets and various places. But afterwards, when the king came in to see the guests at his banquet (that is, those who were resting in his supposed faith, so that on the day of judgment he might visit the guests and judge the merits of each one), he found one who was not dressed in a wedding garment. This one, all those who are associated with wickedness are understood. But the wedding garment, the commands of the Lord, and the works that are accomplished according to the law and the Gospel, make up the clothing of the new man. Therefore, if anyone is found at the time of judgment not having the wedding garment, that is, the clothing of the heavenly man; but rather a polluted garment, that is, the remnants of the old man, he is immediately seized and it is said to him: Friend, how did you come in here? He calls a friend, because he was invited to a wedding: it accuses him of impudence, because he has soiled the wedding festivities with his dirty clothes. But he fell silent. For in that moment there will be no place for repentance, nor the opportunity to deny, since all the angels and the world itself are witnesses of sins.

<h2 id='tocuniq460'>(Vers. 13.)</h2>

(Verse 13) Then the king said to the servants: Bind his feet and hands, and send him into the outer darkness; there will be weeping and gnashing of teeth. The bound hands and feet, the weeping of the eyes, and the gnashing of teeth, signify the truth of resurrection. Or certainly, the hands and feet are bound in order to prevent doing evil and running to shed blood. In the weeping of the eyes and the gnashing of teeth, through the metaphor of bodily members, the severity of the torments is shown.


<h2 id='tocuniq461'>(Vers. 14.)</h2>

(Verse 14.) Many are called, but few are chosen. The short sentence 177 encompasses all the parables: that both in the work of the vineyard, and in the building of the house, and in the wedding banquet, the end is sought after, not the beginning.

<h2 id='tocuniq462'>(Vers. 15.)</h2>

(Verse 15.) Then the Pharisees went and plotted how they might trap him in his words. And they sent their disciples to him, along with the Herodians, saying, 'Teacher, we know that you are truthful and teach the way of God in accordance with the truth. You defer to no one, for you do not show partiality. Therefore, tell us what you think: Is it lawful to pay taxes to Caesar or not?' But Jesus, knowing their evil intent, said, 'You hypocrites, why are you testing me? Show me the coin used for tax payment.' So they brought him a denarius. And Jesus said to them, 'Whose image and inscription is this?' They said to him, 'Caesar's.' Then he said to them, 'Give to Caesar what is Caesar's, and to God what is God's.' When they heard this, they were amazed. So they left him and went away. Caesar Augustus had appointed Herod, the son of Antipater from Antipatris, as a foreigner and a proselyte, as the king of the Jews, who would be in charge of collecting taxes and would obey the Roman empire. Therefore, the Pharisees send their disciples with the Herodians, that is, with Herod's soldiers, or those whom the Pharisees called Herodians because they paid taxes to the Romans and were not devoted to divine worship. Some Latin speakers ridiculously believe that the Herodians were those who believed that Herod was the Messiah, which we never read anywhere at all.


<h2 id='tocuniq463'>(Vers. 16.)</h2>

(Verse 16.) Teacher, we know that you are truthful, and you teach the way of God in truth, and you are not concerned about anyone's opinion. For you do not show partiality to people. So tell us, what do you think: Is it lawful to pay taxes to Caesar or not? This is a cunning and deceitful question, aiming to trap the speaker into saying something that would make him fear God more than Caesar, and declare that taxes should not be paid, so that immediately the Herodians, who are listening, may accuse him of sedition against the Roman ruler.


<h2 id='tocuniq464'>(Vers. 18.)</h2>

(Ver. 18.) But Jesus, knowing their wickedness, said: Why do you test me, hypocrites? The first virtue of the one who responds is to understand the minds of those who ask, and to call not the disciples, but the tempters. Therefore, a hypocrite is called someone who is one thing and pretends to be another, that is, who acts differently in action and in speech.

<h2 id='tocuniq465'>(Vers. 19.)</h2>

(Verse 19.) Show me the coin of the census. And they presented him with a denarius. Wisdom always acts wisely, so that its opponents are refuted mainly by their own words. 'Show me,' he said, 'the denarius, that is, the type of coin that was counted as ten coins and had the image of Caesar.'

<h2 id='tocuniq466'>(Vers. 20.)</h2>

(Verse 20) 179 And Jesus said to them: Whose image and inscription is this? Those who think that Jesus' question shows ignorance, and not just a way of teaching, should learn from this passage that Jesus certainly could have known whose image was on the coin; but he asks in order to respond appropriately to their conversation.

<h2 id='tocuniq467'>(Vers. 21.)</h2>

(Verse 21) They said to him: Caesar's. Then he said to them: Render therefore what belongs to Caesar to Caesar; and what belongs to God to God. We cannot consider Augustus as Caesar, but Tiberius is understood to be his stepson, who succeeded him and under whom the Lord suffered. However, all the Roman emperors from the first Caesar, who seized power, have been called Caesars. Furthermore, what he said: Render what belongs to Caesar to Caesar, that is, the tribute money and the currency; and what belongs to God to God, let us offer tithes, first fruits, and sacrifices: just as he himself paid tribute for himself and Peter; and he rendered to God what belongs to God, doing the Father's will." }


<h2 id='tocuniq468'>(Vers. 22.)</h2>

(Verse 22.) And upon hearing, they marveled. Those who should have believed in such wisdom marveled that their cunning for plotting had found no place.

And leaving him, they went away, reporting the infidelity along with the miracle.

<h2 id='tocuniq469'>(Vers. 23.)</h2>

(Verse 23.) On that day, the Sadducees, who say there is no resurrection, approached him. There were two sects among the Jews: the Pharisees and the Sadducees. The Pharisees emphasized the importance of traditions and observances, which they call 'deuterosis,' over righteousness. Therefore, they were divided from the people. However, the Sadducees, who are called 'just,' claimed for themselves what they were not. While the Pharisees believed in the resurrection of both the body and the soul, and confessed angels and the spirit, the Sadducees denied all of these (according to the Acts of the Apostles)." } These are two houses, about which Isaiah clearly teaches that they are stumbling blocks (Isaiah 8).

<h2 id='tocuniq470'>(Vers. 24 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 24 and following) And they asked him, saying: Master, Moses said: If any man die, having a wife, and leave his wife without children, that his brother should take his wife, and raise up seed to his brother. Now there were with us seven brethren: and the first, when he had married a wife, died; and not having issue, left his wife to his brother. Likewise the second, and the third, unto the seventh. And last of all the woman also died. Those who did not believe in the resurrection of the body, and thought that the soul perished with the body, rightly invent such a fable, which proves their delusion, asserting the resurrection of the dead. However, it is possible that this may actually happen among their people at some point.

<h2 id='tocuniq471'>(Vers. 28.)</h2>

(Verse 28) Therefore, in the resurrection, whose wife will she be? For they all had her. They oppose the absurdity of the story, in order to deny the truth of the resurrection.

<h2 id='tocuniq472'>(Vers. 29.)</h2>

(Verse 29) But Jesus answered and said to them: You are mistaken, not knowing the Scriptures nor the power of God. Therefore, they are mistaken because they do not know the Scriptures, and because they are ignorant of the Scriptures, they consequently do not know the power of God, that is, Christ, who is the power of God and the wisdom of God (1 Corinthians 1).

<h2 id='tocuniq473'>(Vers. 30.)</h2>

(Verse 30.) For in the resurrection neither do they marry, nor are they given in marriage; but are as the angels of God in heaven. The Latin practice does not correspond to the Greek idiom. For to marry properly refers to women, and to take wives refers to men; but let us understand simply what is said, that to marry is written about men, and to be given in marriage about wives. If in the resurrection they do not marry, nor are given in marriage, then the bodies which can marry and be given in marriage will rise. For no one says about a stone and a tree, and about those things which do not have genital members, that they do not marry, or are not married; but about those things which can marry, nevertheless they do not marry in the same way. But what is brought forth: But they are like the angels of God in heaven. A spiritual conversation is promised." }

<h2 id='tocuniq474'>(Vers. 31 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 31 and following) But concerning the resurrection of the dead, have you not read what God said to you, saying: I am the God of Abraham, and the God of Isaac, and the God of Jacob: God is not the God of the dead, but of the living. And when the crowds heard this, they marveled at his teaching. In order to prove the truth of the resurrection, he could have used many other more obvious examples, one of which is: The dead will be raised, and those in the tombs will rise again (Isaiah 26:19). And in another place: Many who sleep in the dust of the earth will awaken: some to everlasting life, and others to shame and everlasting contempt (Dan. 12:2). Therefore, it is questioned what the Lord meant by preferring this testimony, which seems ambiguous or not sufficiently related to the truth of the resurrection: I am the God of Abraham, the God of Isaac, and the God of Jacob; and as if, by saying this, he proved what he wanted, immediately added: He is not the God of the dead, but of the living. Those who were also present at this tumult, knowing the mystery, were astonished at his teaching and answers. We have already said about the Sadducees, who denied the existence of angels, spirits, and the resurrection of the body, also proclaiming the destruction of souls. These people only accepted the five books of Moses, rejecting the prophecies of the prophets. Therefore, it was foolish to bring forth testimonies whose authority they did not follow. Moreover, he presents the example of Moses for proving the eternity of souls: 'I am the God of Abraham, and the God of Isaac, and the God of Jacob' (Exodus III, 6). And immediately he infers: 'God is not the God of the dead, but of the living;' so that when he has proven that souls continue after death (for it could not be that he would be their God, who no longer exist), the resurrection of the bodies, which have done good or evil with the souls, would consequently be introduced. Paul the apostle further explores this topic in more detail in the final part of the first Epistle to the Corinthians (I Cor. XV).

<h2 id='tocuniq475'>(Vers. 34 seqq.)</h2>

(Vers. 34 seqq.) 182 The Pharisees, however, when they heard that he had silenced the Sadducees, gathered together.  And one of them, a lawyer, asked him a question to test him. 'Teacher, which is the great commandment in the Law?' And he said to him, 'You shall love the Lord your God with all your heart and with all your soul and with all your mind. This is the great and first commandment. And a second is like it: You shall love your neighbor as yourself.' In his two statements, the whole law hangs and the prophets. What we read about Herod and Pontius Pilate, that they made an agreement in the death of the Lord, we also now see about the Pharisees and the Sadducees, who are opposed to each other, but consent with equal minds to test Jesus. Therefore, those who were previously confounded in the display of the coin, and had seen the faction of the opposing party undermined, should have been warned by example not to plot further ambushes: but malice and envy nourish impudence. One of the legal experts asked, not desiring to not know, but attempting, if the one being questioned knew what was being asked, what is the greater commandment: not asking about the commandments, but what is the first and greatest commandment; so that when all that God has commanded is great: whatever he responds, he has the opportunity to accuse, asserting that something else is great among many. Therefore, whoever knows and asks not with the desire to learn, but with the desire to understand, if the one who is going to respond knows, approaches in the likeness of the Pharisees, not as a disciple, but as a tempter.


<h2 id='tocuniq476'>Fourth Book</h2>

Fourth Book

<h2 id='tocuniq477'>(Vers. 41 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 41 onwards) 183 Now while the Pharisees were gathered together, Jesus questioned them, saying: What do you think about the Christ, whose son is he? They said to him: David. He said to them: How then does David in the Spirit call him Lord, saying: The Lord said to my Lord, Sit at my right hand, until I make your enemies your footstool? If therefore David calls him Lord, how is he his son? Those who were gathered to test Jesus, attempting to catch him in deceitful questioning, provided an opportunity for their own confutation. And they ask (or, And He is asked) about Christ, whose son He is. The questioning of Jesus is beneficial to us even until today against the Jews. And those who confess that Christ is to come assert that He is a simple man and a holy man from the lineage of David. Let us therefore, being taught by the Lord, question them: if He is a simple man, and only the son of David, how does David call Him his Lord? Not by uncertain error, nor by his own will, but in the Holy Spirit (or, But in the Holy Spirit He is silent). However, the testimony that he has set forth is taken from the 109th Psalm. Therefore, the Lord is called David, not according to what he was born, but according to what he always was born from the Father, surpassing the Father of his own flesh. The Jews fabricate many frivolous things to deceive the truth of the question, asserting that Abraham's native language was Damascus, of which Eliezer was his son. And from the person of Abraham himself, the psalm is written, that after the killing of five kings, the Lord God said to his Lord Abraham, 'Sit at my right hand, until I make your enemies the footstool of your feet.' (Gen. XIV) Whom shall we ask? How did God say to Abraham the following: With you is the beginning on the day of your power, in the brightness of the saints, I have begotten you from the womb before the morning star; and: The Lord has sworn and will not repent; you are a priest forever, according to the order of Melchizedek? And let us try to answer how Abraham was born before the morning star, and how he was a priest according to the order of Melchizedek: for whom Melchizedek offered bread and wine, and from whom he received tithes of the spoils.


<h2 id='tocuniq478'>(Vers. 46.)</h2>

(Verse 46.) And no one was able to answer him a word, nor did anyone dare from that day on to ask him any more questions. The Pharisees and Sadducees, seeking an opportunity for slander, and hoping to find some word by which they could trap him, since they had been refuted in their arguments, no longer asked him questions, but handed him over directly to Roman authority. From this we understand that the poison of envy can indeed be overcome, but it is difficult to find peace.


<h2 id='tocuniq479'>(Chap. XXIII.—Vers. 1 seqq.)</h2>

(Chapter 23, Verses 1 onwards) Then Jesus spoke to the crowds and to his disciples, saying: The scribes and Pharisees have seated themselves on Moses' chair; therefore, whatever they tell you, do and observe, but do not do according to their deeds; for they say things and do not do them. How gentle and kind is the Lord? He is tempted by the Pharisees, their traps are broken, and according to the Psalmist: The arrows of the little ones have become their wounds (Psalm 63:8). Nevertheless, due to the dignity of the priesthood and their position, he urges the people to submit to them, considering not their actions but their teachings. But when he says, 'The scribes and Pharisees sit on the chair of Moses', he points out the teaching of the Law by means of the chair. Therefore, we must understand the teaching also in what is said in the Psalm, 'He did not sit on the seat of pestilence' (Ps. 1:1). And: 'He overturned the chairs of those selling doves' (Mt. 21; Mk. 11).

<h2 id='tocuniq480'>(Vers. 4.)</h2>

(Verse 4.) However, they bind heavy and burdensome loads and impose them on people's shoulders; but they themselves are unwilling to move them with their finger. This applies generally to all teachers who command heavy things but do not do the smaller things. However, it should be noted that both shoulders, finger, loads, and chains by which the loads are bound should be understood spiritually.

<h2 id='tocuniq481'>(Vers. 5.)</h2>

(Verse 5.) They do all their deeds to be seen by others. So whenever you do whatever you do, do it to be seen by others, you are a scribe and a Pharisee.

<h2 id='tocuniq482'>(Vers. 6.)</h2>

(Verse 6) For they enlarge their phylacteries and make their fringes long. They love the place of honor at feasts and the best seats in the synagogues and greetings in the marketplaces and to be called Rabbi by others. Woe to you, scribes and Pharisees, hypocrites! For you travel across sea and land to make a single proselyte, and when he becomes a proselyte, you make him twice as much a child of hell as yourselves. When the Lord gave the commandments of the Law through Moses, He finally added: Bind them on your hand, and they shall be immovable before your eyes (Deuteronomy 6:8). And the meaning is: Let my commandments be in your hand, so that they may be fulfilled in action; let them be before your eyes, so that you may meditate on them day and night. The Pharisees, misinterpreting this, wrote the Ten Commandments of Moses on parchment, complicating them, and tying them on their foreheads, making it like a crown on their heads, so that they would always be in front of their eyes: which the Indians, Persians, and Babylonians still do today: and anyone who has this is considered religious among the peoples. Moses had also commanded (Num. 15) that fringes of hyacinth color should be made on the four corners of their garments, to distinguish the people of Israel, so that just as circumcision gave a sign of the Jewish people on their bodies, their clothing would also have some difference. Superstitious teachers, seeking public attention and pursuing profits from women, made large tassels and bound very sharp thorns in them, so that, walking and sitting, they would sometimes be pricked, and as if by this reminder, they would be drawn back to the works of the Lord and the duties of His service. Therefore, because the Lord had said, 'They do all their works to be seen by men,' which He accused in general terms, now He divides it into specific parts. Those little pictures of the Ten Commandments were called phylacteries, because whoever had them would have them as a kind of protection and reminder of themselves. The Pharisees did not understand that these things should be carried in the heart, not on the body. Otherwise, even cabinets and chests have books and knowledge of God. Among us, these superstitious women still do these things today, in little Gospels, and on the wood of the cross, and in similar things (which indeed have zeal for God, but not according to knowledge) (Rom. X), straining out a gnat and swallowing a camel (below, in the same book). Such was the fringe, small and short, commanded by the Law, which the woman who was flowing with blood touched in the cloak of the Lord (Luke 8:44): but she is not pierced by the superstitious thorns of the Pharisees; rather, she is healed by his touch. And while they unnecessarily enlarge their phylacteries, and make large fringes, seeking glory from men, they are accused in the rest of why they seek the first places at dinners, and the first seats in synagogues; and in public they follow their appetite and glory: and they are called Rabbi by men, which in the Latin language means teacher. Denique sequitur:

<h2 id='tocuniq483'>(Vers. 8 seq.)</h2>

(Verse 8 onwards) But you are not to be called Rabbi, for One is your Teacher, and you are all brothers. And do not call anyone on earth your father, for One is your Father, who is in heaven. Nor are you to be called teachers, for One is your Teacher, the Christ. The greatest among you shall be your servant. And whoever exalts himself will be humbled, and whoever humbles himself will be exalted. And do not call anyone on earth your father, for One is your Father, who is in heaven, and there is no other teacher, except God the Father and our Lord Jesus Christ. Father, because all things are from Him. Teacher, because all things are through Him: or because through the dispensation of His flesh, we are all reconciled to God. It is asked why the Apostle, teacher of the gentiles, declared himself to be against this precept (2 Corinthians 5; Colossians 1); or how, with the common language, especially in the monasteries of Palestine and Egypt, they call each other Fathers. This is resolved as follows: Being a father or a teacher by nature is different from being one through indulgence. If we call someone a father, we show honor to their age, not reveal the source of our life. Likewise, a teacher is called from the company of a true teacher. And without going into endless repetition, just as one God by nature and one Son do not prejudice the others from being called gods (or gods) by adoption, and sons, so one both father and teacher do not prejudice others, so that they are called fathers and teachers in an abusive manner.

<h2 id='tocuniq484'>(Vers. 13, 14.)</h2>

(Verse 13, 14) But woe to you, scribes and Pharisees, hypocrites! For you shut up the kingdom of heaven against men; for you neither go in yourselves, nor do you allow those who are entering to go in. Woe to you, scribes and Pharisees, hypocrites! For you devour widows' houses, and for a pretense make long prayers. Therefore you will receive greater condemnation. The scribes and Pharisees have knowledge of the Law and the Prophets, and they know that Christ is the Son of God. They are not ignorant of his birth from a virgin. But while they desire to prey upon the subject people, they themselves do not enter the kingdom of heaven, nor do they allow those who are able to enter. This is what the prophet Hosea accuses: The priests have hidden the way, they have killed Sicimam (Hosea 6:9). And again: The priests have not said, where is the Lord? (Hosea 4). Or certainly every teacher who scandalizes his disciples with evil deeds, shuts the kingdom of heaven before them.

<h2 id='tocuniq485'>(Vers. 15.)</h2>

(Verse 15.) Woe to you, scribes and Pharisees, hypocrites! for you compass sea and land to make one proselyte, and when he is made, you make him twofold more the child of hell than yourselves. We do not serve with the same intent with which we seek. Scribes and Pharisees, while traversing the whole world for the sake of business or different gains, were eager to make a proselyte from the Gentiles, that is, a stranger and uncircumcised person, to mix with the people of God. But he who before, while he was a pagan, simply wandered, and was once a son of hell, seeing the vices of the magistrates, and understanding to destroy them by his work, which they taught with words, returns to his vomit: and becoming a pagan, as a transgressor, he will be worthy of greater punishment. But the son is called hell, just as the son of perdition, and the son of this age. For each one is called the son of whomever's works he does.


<h2 id='tocuniq486'>(Vers. 16 seq.)</h2>

(Verse 16 and following) Woe to you, blind leaders, who say, 'Whoever swears by the temple, it is nothing; but whoever swears by the gold of the temple, he is obligated.' Fools and blind! For which is greater, the gold or the temple that sanctifies the gold? And whoever swears by the altar, it is nothing; but whoever swears by the gift that is on it, he is obligated. Blind! For which is greater, the gift or the altar that sanctifies the gift? Therefore, whoever swears on the altar, swears on it and on all things that are above it. And whoever swears in the temple, swears in it and in the one who dwells in it. And whoever swears in heaven, swears on the throne of God and on the one who sits upon it. Above, as it seemed to us, we have explained what the tradition of the Pharisees signified, saying: Whatever gift is from me, will benefit you: now the double tradition, drawing towards one opportunity for greed, is condemned, so that they may be accused of doing everything for profit and not for fear of God. For just as in the phylacteries and in the fringes the desire for holiness sought glory, and sought gains through an opportunity for glory, so another invention of tradition accuses the teachers of impiety. If anyone, in a dispute or in some argument, or in a doubtful cause, swore an oath in the temple, and afterwards was convicted of falsehood, he was not considered guilty of the crime. But if he swore on gold and money, which was offered to the priests in the temple, immediately he was compelled to fulfill what he had sworn. Again: If anyone were to swear on the altar, no one held him guilty of perjury; but if he were to perjure himself in a gift, or in oblations, that is, in sacrifices, and in meal offerings, and other things that are offered to God upon the altar, these were most eagerly sought after. Therefore, the Lord accused them both of folly and deceit, because the temple is much greater than the gold which is sanctified by the temple, and the altar is greater than the sacrifices, which are sanctified by the altar. However, they did it not out of fear of God, but out of greed for wealth.

<h2 id='tocuniq487'>(Vers. 23.)</h2>

(Verse 23.) Woe to you, Scribes and Pharisees, hypocrites! for you tithe mint and dill and cumin, but have neglected the weightier matters of the law, such as justice, mercy, and faith. It was necessary to do these things and not neglect the others. Many precepts are given in the Law that foreshadow future events. But others are clear, as the Psalmist says: The commandment of the Lord is clear, enlightening the eyes (Psalm 19:9), which they immediately desire to follow. For example: You shall not commit adultery; you shall not steal; you shall not bear false witness, etc. But the Pharisees, because the Lord had commanded (let us leave aside mystical interpretations for now) that tithes of all things be offered in the temple for the support of the priests and Levites, of whom the Lord was a part, their only concern was to comply with the commanded observances; they disregarded other matters which were more important, whether they should be done or not. And from this chapter, it accuses them of greed because they eagerly demand tithes even on inexpensive vegetables, and they neglect justice in the resolution of business disputes, and compassion for the poor, the orphans, and widows, and faith in God, which are great.

<h2 id='tocuniq488'>(Vers. 24.)</h2>

(Verse 24) Blind leaders, straining out a gnat but swallowing a camel. I think the camel, according to the meaning of this passage, represents the magnitude of the commandments, judgement, and mercy, and faith. The gnat, on the other hand, represents tithing mint, dill, cumin, and other cheap herbs. We devour and neglect these things that are against God's commandments, which are great, and we show diligence in matters of religion that bring profit but are small.


<h2 id='tocuniq489'>(Vers. 25, 26.)</h2>

(Verse 25, 26.) Woe to you, scribes and Pharisees, hypocrites! For you clean the outside of the cup and the plate, but inside they are full of greed and self-indulgence. Blind Pharisee! First clean the inside of the cup and the plate, that the outside also may be clean. In different words but with the same meaning as above, he accuses the Pharisees of hypocrisy and deceit because they present one thing to people outwardly and do another thing at home. Not because their superstition resided in the cup and the dish; but because they displayed outwardly sanctity to men, in their dress, in their speech, in their phylacteries, in the fringes, in the length of their prayers, and such like; while inwardly they were full of the filthiness of vices.

<h2 id='tocuniq490'>(Vers. 27, 28.)</h2>

(Verse 27, 28.) Woe to you, scribes and Pharisees, hypocrites! Because you are like whitewashed tombs, which appear beautiful on the outside, but inside are full of dead men's bones and all uncleanness. Even so you also outwardly appear righteous to men, but inside you are full of hypocrisy and lawlessness. What he had demonstrated with the cup and platter, that they were clean on the outside, but filthy inside, he now repeats by the example of the tombs: how outside the tombs were adorned with lime, and decorated with marble and gold and various colors, but inside were full of dead men's bones. Similarly, the perverse teachers, who teach one thing and do another, demonstrate cleanliness through the appearance of their clothing and humility of their words, but inside they are full of all uncleanness and desire." } Finally, this expresses more clearly the same thing, saying: Thus you appear righteous to outward people, but inside you are full of hypocrisy and iniquity.

<h2 id='tocuniq491'>(Vers. 29 seqq.)</h2>

(V. 29 seqq.) Woe to you, scribes and Pharisees, hypocrites! Because you build the tombs of the prophets and decorate the monuments of the righteous, and you say, 'If we had lived in the days of our fathers, we would not have been partners with them in shedding the blood of the prophets.' Therefore, you testify against yourselves that you are sons of those who murdered the prophets. By a very wise syllogism, they are convicted of being the offspring of murderers, while they, by their opinion of goodness and glory to the people, build tombs for the prophets whom their ancestors killed, and they say, 'If we had lived in that time, we would not have done what our fathers did.' However, even if they do not say it in words, they speak through their actions, in that they ambitiously and magnificently build memorials for the slain, whom they do not deny were murdered by their ancestors.

And you fill up the measure of your fathers. As he had approved of the former words, that they were the sons of murderers, and of those who had killed the prophets, now he concludes what he had intended, and he sets forth, as it were, the last part of the syllogism. And you fill up the measure of your fathers. What was lacking to them, you supply. They killed the servants: you crucify the Lord. They killed the prophets: you kill him who was foretold by the prophets.

<h2 id='tocuniq492'>(Vers. 33.)</h2>

(Verse 33.) Serpents, (It is added also) offspring of vipers, how will you escape the judgment of Gehenna? This very thing John the Baptist had said (Luke III). As therefore from vipers vipers are born: so from murderer fathers, you, he says, are born murderers.

<h2 id='tocuniq493'>(Vers. 34.)</h2>

(Verse 34.) Therefore, behold, I send to you prophets and wise men and scribes. And some of them you will kill and crucify, and some of them you will flog in your synagogues and persecute from town to town. So that upon you may come all the righteous blood shed on earth, from the blood of righteous Abel to the blood of Zechariah the son of Barachiah, whom you murdered between the sanctuary and the altar. Truly, I say to you, all these things will come upon this generation. At the same time, observe the Apostle writing to the Corinthians (I Cor. VII), that there are various gifts of the disciples of Christ: some are prophets, who preach future events; some are wise, who know when they should speak; some are scribes, most learned in the Law, among whom Stephen was stoned, Paul killed, Peter crucified, and the disciples in the Acts of the Apostles were beaten; and they were persecuted from city to city, expelled from Judea, so that they would migrate to the people of the Gentiles.


<h2 id='tocuniq494'>(Vers. 35, 36.)</h2>

(Verse 35, 36) So that upon you may come all the righteous blood shed on earth, from the blood of righteous Abel to the blood of Zechariah son of Barachiah, whom you murdered between the sanctuary and the altar. Amen I say to you, all these things will come upon this generation. There is no doubt about Abel, that he is the one whom his brother Cain killed. But the righteousness of Abel is not only confirmed by the present judgment of the Lord, but also by the testimony of Genesis (Gen. 4), where the gifts offered by him to God are narrated. We seek to know who this Zacharias, son of Barachiah, is, because we have read about many Zachariases. And so that the opportunity for error is not given to us, it is added: whom you have killed between the temple and the altar. Different things are read in different sources, and I must present the opinions of each individual. Some say that Zacharias, son of Barachiah, is the one who is the eleventh among the twelve prophets, and his father's name agrees with him; but the Scripture does not speak about where he was killed between the temple and the altar, especially since at the time of his death there were hardly any ruins of the temple. Some believe that Zacharias, the father of John, is understood from certain apocryphal dreams, approving that he was killed because he proclaimed the advent of the Savior. Because this does not have authority from the Scriptures, it is easily dismissed as it is proven. Others believe that this Zacharias is the one who was killed by King Joas of Judah between the temple and the altar, as the history of the Kings narrates. But it should be noted that this Zacharias is not the son of Barachias, but the son of Joiada the priest. And the Scripture also records: ‘He did not remember the kindness that Joash’s father Jehoiada had done to him’ (2 Chronicles 24:22). So if we accept the identification of Zechariah and the place of his killing, we ask why he is called the son of Barachiah and not Jehoiada. In our language, Barachiah means ‘blessed by the Lord,’ and Jehoiada is shown to mean ‘the righteousness of the priest’ in Hebrew. In the Gospel used by the Nazarenes, we find it written that he is the son of Jehoiada, not Barachiah (191). The simpler brothers, among the ruins of the temple and altar, or at the exits of the gates that lead to Siloam, pointing to the red stones, think they are polluted with the blood of Zechariah. We do not condemn the error, which arises from hatred of the Jews and devotion to faith. Let us briefly explain why the blood of the just Abel is sought, up to Zechariah son of Barachiah from that generation, when neither of them killed him. The rule of the Scriptures is to present two generations, of the good or the evil, that is, one for each individual. Let us take examples from good things: Who shall ascend into the mountain of the Lord? or who shall stand in His holy place? (Psalm 24:3) And when he had described several people of different ages who were going to ascend to the mountain of the Lord, he then adds: This is the generation of those who seek Him, who seek the face of the God of Jacob. And in another place concerning all the saints: The generation of the righteous shall be blessed. (Psalm 112:2) But concerning the wicked, as in the present passage: The generation of vipers. And all things shall be required of this generation. And in Ezekiel, when he had described the sins of the land, the prophetic word added: If Noah and Job and Daniel were there, I will not let go of the sins of that land (Ezek. XIV, 14): all the righteous who would be similar in virtues to them are understood to be represented by Noah and Job and Daniel. Therefore, those who have acted similarly to Cain and Joas against the apostles are referred to as being from the same generation.


<h2 id='tocuniq495'>(Vers. 37.)</h2>

(Verse 37.) Jerusalem, Jerusalem, you who kill the prophets and stone those who are sent to you: how often I have longed to gather your children together, as a hen gathers her chicks under her wings, but you were unwilling! Jerusalem, it is not the stones and buildings of the city that he calls, but the inhabitants, whom he mourns with a father's affection, as we read in another place that he wept when he saw her (Luke 19). And in saying, 'how often I have longed to gather your children together,' he testifies that all the prophets sent by him were rejected. We also read in the song of Deuteronomy the likeness of a hen gathering her chicks under her wings: As an eagle protects its nest, and desires its young, spreading out its wings, receiving them, and carrying them on its feathers (Deut. XXXII, 11).

<h2 id='tocuniq496'>192 (Vers. 38.)</h2>

192 (Version 38.) Behold, your house shall be left desolate. This very thing Jeremiah had already said in the person of Jeremiah: I have forsaken my house, I have left my inheritance: my inheritance is become unto me as a lion's den (Jer. XII, 7, 8). We see with our own eyes the desolate house of the Jews, that temple which shone more brightly: for it lost its inhabitant Christ, and desiring to seize his inheritance, killed the heir.


<h2 id='tocuniq497'>(Vers. 39.)</h2>

(Verse 39.) For I say unto you: you shall not see me henceforth, until you say: Blessed is he who comes in the name of the Lord. He speaks to Jerusalem, and to the people of Judaea. But this verse, in which even infants and sucklings used at the entrance of the Lord's Savior in Jerusalem, when they said: Blessed is he who comes in the name of the Lord, hosanna in the highest, is taken from the 117th psalm, which is clearly written about the coming of the Lord. And what He says, He wants to be understood as this: Unless you do penance (Luke XIII), and confess that I am the one about whom the Prophets have sung, the Son of the Almighty Father, you will not see my face. The Jews have been given a time for penance: let them confess the blessed one who comes in the name of the Lord, and let them gaze upon the face of Christ.

<h2 id='tocuniq498'>(Chap. XXIV.—Vers. 1, 2.)</h2>

Chapter XXIV - Verses 1, 2: And Jesus went out from the temple and was going away. And His disciples came up to point out the buildings of the temple to Him. But He answered and said to them, 'Do you not see all these things? Truly I say to you, not one stone here will be left upon another, which will not be torn down.' According to the story, the meaning is clear. As the Lord left the temple, all the buildings of the law and the composition of the commandments were destroyed in such a way that nothing can be fulfilled by the Jews. And with the head removed, all the members fight among themselves.


<h2 id='tocuniq499'>(Vers. 3, 4.)</h2>

(vv. 3, 4.) But while he was sitting on the Mount of Olives, the disciples came to him privately, saying: “Tell us, when will these things happen, and what will be the sign of your coming and of the end of the age?” And Jesus answered them, saying: “See that no one deceives you.” He sits on the Mount of Olives, where the true light of knowledge was being born, and the disciples secretly approach him, who desired to know the mysteries and revelations of the future, and they ask three things: At what time will Jerusalem be destroyed? When will Christ come? When will the end of the age come?


<h2 id='tocuniq500'>(Vers. 5.)</h2>

(Version 5.) For many will come in my name, saying, 'I am the Christ,' and they will deceive many. One of whom is Simon the Samaritan, whom we read about in the Acts of the Apostles, who claimed to be a great power of God (Acts 8). He also left behind these writings among others in his own volumes, saying: 'I am the word of God, I am beautiful, I am the paraclete, I am omnipotent, I am all things of God.' But even John the Apostle speaks in his epistle: 'You have heard that the Antichrist is coming, now many antichrists have come' (1 John 2:18). I think all heresiarchs are Antichrists and teach under the name of Christ things that are contrary to Christ. It is not surprising if we see some being deceived by them, since the Lord said: And many will be led astray.

<h2 id='tocuniq501'>(Vers. 6.)</h2>

(Ver. 6.) For you are about to hear of battles and opinions about battles; see that you are not troubled. For these things must happen, but the end is not yet. So when we see these things happening, let us not think that the day of judgment is at hand, but that it is reserved for that time, the sign of which is clearly set forth in what follows.

<h2 id='tocuniq502'>(Vers. 7, 8.)</h2>

(Ver. 7, 8.) For nation will rise against nation, and kingdom against kingdom, and there will be pestilences and famines, and earthquakes in various places. But all these things are the beginning of sorrows. I do not doubt that these things, indeed, will happen according to the literal meaning of what has been written: but it seems to me that the kingdom against kingdom, and their pestilence, whose speech spreads like cancer (II Tim. II), and the famine of hearing the word of God, and the shaking of the whole earth, and the separation from true faith, are more intelligibly understood among heretics, who, fighting against each other, make victory for the Church." } But what he said: These however are all beginnings of sorrow, is better translated as beginnings of birth pains: so that as if some kind of conception the coming of Antichrist, not birth, may be understood.

<h2 id='tocuniq503'>(Vers. 9.)</h2>

(Verse 9.) Then they will deliver you up to tribulation and kill you, and you will be hated by all nations for my name's sake. The term 'apostle' refers to anyone who believes, not to the specific individuals who were apostles during that time.

<h2 id='tocuniq504'>(Vers. 12, 13.)</h2>

(Verse 12, 13.) And since iniquity will abound, the love of many will grow cold. But he who perseveres to the end, he will be saved. He did not deny the faith of all, but of many. For many are called, but few are chosen. For in the apostles and their successors, charity will remain, of which it is written: 'Many waters cannot quench love' (Song of Songs 8:7). And even Paul himself: Who shall separate us from the love of Christ? tribulation, or distress, or famine (Rom. 8:35)? and the rest.

<h2 id='tocuniq505'>(Vers. 14.)</h2>

(Verse 14.) And this Gospel of the kingdom will be preached in the whole world, as a testimony to all nations; and then the end will come. The sign of the Lord's coming is the preaching of the Gospel throughout the whole world, so that no one is without excuse; which has either already been fulfilled, or will be fulfilled very soon. For I do not think that any nation remains which does not know the name of Christ. And although they may not have had preachers, they cannot ignore the reputation of the faith from neighboring nations.


<h2 id='tocuniq506'>(Vers. 15.)</h2>

(Verse 15.) So when you see the abomination of desolation, spoken of by the prophet Daniel, standing in the holy place (let the reader understand), then let those who are in Judea flee to the mountains. Whoever is on the housetop must not come down to take what is in his house. And whoever is in the field must not turn back to get his cloak. But woe to those who are pregnant and to those who are nursing babies in those days! Pray that your flight may not be in winter or on a Sabbath. For then there will be great tribulation, such as has not been from the beginning of the world until now, nor ever will be. And if those days had not been shortened, no flesh would be saved; but because of the elect, those days will be shortened. Of this also the apostle speaks (II Thess. II): that the man of sin and the adversary is to be exalted against everything that is called God and is worshipped, so that he dares to stand in the temple of God and show himself as God, whose coming according to the work of Satan destroys them and reduces them to the solitude of God, those who have received him. It can be understood either simply of the Antichrist or of the image of Caesar, which Pilate placed in the temple, or of the equestrian statue of Hadrian, which stood in the very place of the holy of holies until the present day. Abomination, according to the ancient Scripture, is also called an idol; and for this reason, it is added, of desolation; because it is placed in a desolate and destroyed temple.

<h2 id='tocuniq507'>(Vers. 16 seq.)</h2>

(Verse 16 onwards) Then those who are in Judea should flee to the mountains; and those who are on the housetop should not go down to take anything from their house; and those who are in the field should not turn back to get their cloak. The abomination of desolation can be understood as any perverse teaching; when we see it standing in the holy place, that is, in the Church, and proclaiming itself to be God, we must flee from Judea to the mountains, that is, leaving behind worldly desires and Jewish wickedness, and drawing closer to the eternal mountains, from which God wonderfully enlightens us (Psalm 75); and be on the rooftop and in the chamber, where the fiery darts of the devil cannot reach us; not descending to take anything from our former way of life; not looking backwards, but instead sowing in the field of spiritual Scriptures, so that we may reap fruits from it. Neither is it allowed to wear another tunic, which the apostles are prohibited from having. Regarding this place, that is, the abomination of desolation, which was spoken of by the prophet Daniel, Porphyry blasphemed against us in his thirteenth volume of his work, while standing in a holy place, to whom Eusebius of Caesarea, the bishop, responded in three volumes: the eighteenth, nineteenth, and twentieth. Apollinaris (also known as Apollinarius) also wrote extensively on this matter, and attempted, unnecessarily, to discuss it in one chapter, which has been debated over with numerous lines of verse.


<h2 id='tocuniq508'>(Vers. 19.)</h2>

(Verse 19.) But woe to those who are pregnant and nursing in those days. Woe to those souls who have not led their offspring to a perfect man, but have the beginnings of faith, so that they need the nourishment of teachers. This can also be said, that during the persecution of Antichrist, or the Roman captivity, pregnant and nursing women, burdened by the weight of their wombs and children, were unable to make a hasty escape.

<h2 id='tocuniq509'>(Vers. 20.)</h2>

(Verse 20.) But pray that your flight may not be in winter or on the Sabbath. If we desire to escape the captivity of Jerusalem, when it was captured by Titus and Vespasian, they must pray that their flight may not be in winter or on the Sabbath; because in winter the severity of the cold prevents them from going into the wilderness and hiding in the mountains and deserts; in the Sabbath, it is either a violation of the Law if they want to flee, or impending death if they remain. But if the end of the world is understood, it commands this, that our faith not grow cold and our love for Christ not diminish, and that we not become lazy in the work of God on the Sabbath of virtues.

<h2 id='tocuniq510'>(Vers. 22.)</h2>

(Verse 22.) And unless those days were shortened, no flesh would be saved; but for the sake of the elect, those days will be shortened. The shortened days, not according to the foolishness of some (who believe that the moments of time can be changed and do not remember that scripture: According to your ordinance, the days remain (Psalm 118:91)), but according to the quality of time we should understand, that is, the days are shortened not in measurement but in number; just as it is said in the blessing: I will fill him with length of days (Psalm 90); so now the shortened days should be understood: so that the faith of the believers is not shaken by the delay of time.


<h2 id='tocuniq511'>(Vers. 23.)</h2>

(Verse 23) Then if anyone says to you: behold, here is the Christ, or there; do not believe. Many leaders arose during the time of the Jewish captivity who claimed to be the Christ, to the extent that, during the Roman siege, there were three factions inside. But a better understanding of the end of the world is understood.

<h2 id='tocuniq512'>(Vers. 24.)</h2>

(Verse 24.) For false Christs and false prophets will arise and perform great signs and wonders, so as to lead astray, if possible, even the elect. See, I have told you beforehand. There are three ways, as I have already said, in which this place should be interpreted; either concerning the time of the Roman siege, or concerning the end of the world, or concerning the battle of the heretics against the Church, and such antichrists who, under the guise of false knowledge, fight against Christ.


<h2 id='tocuniq513'>(Vers. 25, 26.)</h2>

(Verses 25, 26.) Therefore, if they say to you, ‘Look, he is in the wilderness,’ do not go out; ‘Look, he is in the inner rooms,’ do not believe it. If someone promises you that Christ is dwelling in the wilderness of the Gentiles and philosophers, or in the inner rooms of heretics who promise the secrets of God, do not go out, do not believe it; or (because in times of persecution and distress false prophets always find an opportunity to deceive) if someone wants to boast under the name of Christ, do not immediately give your faith.


<h2 id='tocuniq514'>(Vers. 27.)</h2>

(Verse 27.) For as the lightning comes from the east and shines as far as the west, so will be the coming of the Son of Man. Do not go out, do not believe that the Son of Man is in the desert of the Gentiles or in the secret places of heretics, but that his faith shines from east to west in the Catholic Church. It should also be said that the second coming of the Savior will not be in humility as before, but in glory to be shown. It is foolish therefore to seek him in a small or hidden place, who is the light of the whole world.

<h2 id='tocuniq515'>(Vers. 28.)</h2>

(Verse 28) Wherever the body is, there the eagles will be gathered together. From the natural example that we witness daily, we are instructed by the sacrament of Christ. Eagles and vultures are also said to sense corpses across the seas and gather for food of this kind. Therefore, if irrational birds, separated by such large stretches of land and the waves of the sea, sense a small corpse wherever it may lie by natural instinct, how much more should we and the entire multitude of believers hasten to Him, whose lightning comes from the East and shines to the West! But we can understand the body, that is, the πτῶμα, which is more significantly called cadaver in Latin, as the passion of Christ, by which we are provoked; so that wherever it is read in the Scriptures, we may gather together, and through it, we may come to the Word of God, as it is written: They have pierced my hands and my feet (Ps. 22:16) . And in Isaiah: Like a sheep led to the slaughter (Isa. 53:7) ; and similar things to these. But the saints are called eagles, because the youth is renewed like the eagles; and those who are feathered according to Isaiah, and they take up their wings, so that they may come to Christ's passion (Isaiah 46).

<h2 id='tocuniq516'>(Vers. 29.)</h2>

(Verse 29.) But immediately after the tribulation of those days, the sun will be darkened, and the moon will not give its light, and the stars will fall from heaven, and the powers of the heavens will be shaken. The sun and moon will be darkened, and will not give their light; and the other stars will fall from heaven, and the powers of the heavens will be shaken, not by a diminution of light (otherwise we read that the sun will have sevenfold light), but because in comparison to true light, all things will be dark to the sight. So, if that sun, which now shines throughout the whole world, and the moon, which is the second luminary, and the stars, which are lit as a solace of the night, and all the powers (which we understand to be the multitudes of angels), will be accounted as darkness in the coming of Christ: let the brows of those who, considering themselves holy, do not fear the presence of judgments, be shaken.

<h2 id='tocuniq517'>(Vers. 30.)</h2>

(Verse 30.) And then the sign of the Son of Man will appear in heaven. By this sign, we may understand either the Cross, as the Jews saw (according to Zechariah 12 and John 19) the one they fashioned; or the banner of triumphant victory.

And then all the tribes of the earth will mourn, and they will see the Son of man coming in the clouds of heaven with great power and majesty. Those who have not believed in heaven will mourn, but they are written in the earth.

<h2 id='tocuniq518'>(Vers. 31.)</h2>

(Verse 31.) And He will send His angels with a trumpet and a loud voice; and they will gather His elect from the four winds, from the highest heavens to their ends. The Apostle speaks of this trumpet (I Cor. XV; I Thess. IV): and in the Apocalypse of John we read (Apoc. VIII): and in the Old Testament (Num. X), it is commanded that trumpets be made of flexible gold, silver, and bronze, so that they may sound forth the lofty mysteries of doctrine.


<h2 id='tocuniq519'>(Vers. 32, 33.)</h2>

(Verse 32, 33.) But learn a lesson from the fig tree: When its branch has already become tender and puts forth leaves, you know that summer is near. In the same way, when you see all these things, know that it is near, right at the doorstep. Under the example of the tree, he taught about the coming of the end. He said, "Just as when the branches of the fig tree become tender and it puts forth buds and leaves, you understand that summer is coming and the entrance of the west wind and spring: in the same way, when you see all these things that are written, do not think that the end of the world is already here, but rather that certain prologues and forerunners are coming to show that it is near and right at the doorstep.


<h2 id='tocuniq520'>(Vers. 34.)</h2>

(Verse 34) Amen, I say to you, this generation will not pass away until all these things happen. Above, we spoke of the generations of the good, and on the contrary, of the evil as being separate. Therefore, it either signifies all kinds of people, or specifically the Jews.

<h2 id='tocuniq521'>(Vers. 35.)</h2>

(Verse 35.) Heaven and earth will pass away, but my words will not pass away. Heaven and earth will pass away by transformation, not by their destruction: otherwise, how will the sun be darkened, and the moon not give its light, and the stars fall, if the heaven in which these things exist, and the earth, do not exist?

<h2 id='tocuniq522'>(Vers. 36.)</h2>

(Verse 36.) But no one knows about that day or hour, not even the angels in heaven, nor the Son, but only the Father. In some Latin manuscripts, it is added that not even the Son knows, while in the Greek manuscripts, especially in the copies of Adamantius and Pierius, this is not found written. But because it is read in some manuscripts, it seems worth discussing. Arius and Eunomius rejoice, as if the ignorance of the teacher is the glory of the disciples, and they say: He who knows and he who is ignorant cannot be equal. Against whom these things are to be briefly said: When Jesus has made all times, that is, the Word of God: For all things are made by him, and without him nothing is made (John 1:3), in all times, even the day of judgment: with what consequence can he ignore a part whose whole he knows? This also must be said: What is greater, the knowledge of the Father, or of judgment? If he knows the greater, how does he not know the lesser? We have read the Scripture. All things that belong to the Father have been handed over to me (Luke 10:22). If all things belong to the Father and the Son, how is it that the Son reserved for Himself the knowledge of one day and did not want to share it with the Son? But it must also be inferred: If He does not know the last day of times, He also does not know the nearly last day, and backwards all of them. For it is not possible for one who first does not know to know what comes second. Therefore, since we have proven that the Son does not ignore the day of judgment (God is added by some), a reason must be given why He is said to not know. The apostle writes about the Savior: In whom are hidden all the treasures of wisdom and knowledge (Colossians 2:3). Therefore, all the treasures of wisdom and knowledge are in Christ, but they are hidden. Why are they hidden? After the resurrection, when questioned by the apostles, he answered more clearly about the day: It is not for you to know the times or seasons that the Father has set by his own authority (Acts 1:7). When he says, 'It is not for you to know,' he shows that he himself knows, but it is not expedient for the apostles to know, so that they may always live uncertain about the coming of the judge, as if every day were the 200th day of judgment." } Finally, the subsequent discourse of the Gospel compels us to understand the same, saying that only the Father knows: in the Father, He includes the Son. For every Father, the name of the Son is.

<h2 id='tocuniq523'>(Vers. 37 seq.)</h2>

(Verse 37 and following) Just as in the days of Noah, so it will be at the coming of the Son of Man. For as they were in the days before the flood, eating and drinking, marrying and giving in marriage, until the day that Noah entered the ark, and they did not know until the flood came and took them all away; so will the coming of the Son of Man be. It is asked how it is written above: For nation will rise against nation, and kingdom against kingdom, and there will be famines, and plagues, and earthquakes; and now they should remember those things that are signs of peace. But it is to be considered, according to the Apostle, that after wars, and dissensions, and pestilences, and famines, and earthquakes, and other things by which the human race is devastated, peace will quickly follow, which promises quietness for all, so that the faith of the believers may be confirmed, whether after the evils have occurred, they hope for the judgment to come. For this is what we read in Paul: when they say, peace and security, then sudden destruction will come upon them, like the pain of a woman in labor, and they will not escape (I Thess. V, 3).


<h2 id='tocuniq524'>(Vers. 40, 41.)</h2>

(Verse 40, 41) Then there will be two in the field: one will be taken and one will be left. Two women will be grinding at the mill: one will be taken and one will be left. Then, he said, there will be two in the field, when, at the time of the consummation and judgment, two will be found in the field having the same labor and almost the same sowing, but not receiving the fruits of labor equally. Two women will also be grinding together: one will be taken and one will be left." } In the two who dwell in the field, and in the two who grind together, understand either the Synagogue, and (or) the Church, which seem to grind together in the Law, and to grind the flour of the commandments of God from the same Scriptures: or the other heresies, which seem to grind the flour of their teachings from both the Old and New Testaments, or from one of them: and although they have the same Christian name and purpose, they will not receive the same reward: some being chosen and others left behind.


<h2 id='tocuniq525'>(Vers. 42, 43.)</h2>

(Verses 42, 43) Watch therefore, for you do not know at what hour your Lord is coming. But know this, that if the master of the house had known in what watch the thief would come, he would have watched and would not have allowed his house to be broken into. Clearly He shows why He said above: But of that day and hour no one knows, not even the angels of heaven, but the Father alone: which it is not expedient for the apostles to know, so that they may always believe Him to be coming in uncertain expectation, whom they do not know when He is coming. And he did not say, 'We do not know at what hour the Lord will come,' but you do not know. And with the example of the father of the family being sent forth, why he keeps silent about the day of the consummation, he teaches more clearly, saying:

Therefore, you also must be ready, for you do not know the hour when the Son of Man is coming. Who then is the faithful and wise servant, whom his master has set over his household, to give them food at the proper time? Blessed is that servant whom his master will find so doing when he comes. Truly, I say to you, he will set him over all his possessions. He further emphasizes and repeats why he did not predict the day and hour of the consummation, neither the angels nor himself, but only the Father, because it is not expedient for the apostles to know; and he inserts an example of the head of a household, that is, his own and the faithful servants, that is, the apostles, to encourage the anxious mind, so that they may provide nourishment of teachings to their fellow servants at the proper time.


<h2 id='tocuniq526'>(Vers. 48, 49.)</h2>

(Vers. 48, 49.) But if that evil servant shall say in his heart, My lord delayeth his coming; and shall begin to beat his fellow servants, and to eat and drink with the drunken; the servant who is anxious and always waiting for the master's coming, gives food to the servants in due time, and afterwards is set over all the goods of the householder: so, on the contrary, he who said according to Ezekiel: This will happen in long times (Ezek. XII, 22), and does not think that the Lord will come quickly; becoming more secure, indulges in feasts and luxury: and he will perceive not a lenient householder, but a most stern judge.


<h2 id='tocuniq527'>(Vers. 50, 51.)</h2>

(Verse 50, 51) The lord will come to his servants on a day they do not expect and at an hour they do not know. And he will divide them and place a portion with the hypocrites. There will be weeping and gnashing of teeth. This teaches them that when the master is not expected, then he will come, and it admonishes the stewards of vigilance and solicitude. Furthermore, when it says he will divide them, it does not mean he will cut them with a sword, but that he will separate them from the company of the saints and place a portion with the hypocrites, namely with those who were in the field and grinding, and yet were abandoned. We often said that a hypocrite is one thing, and to show something else: just as it seemed to do the same thing in the field and in the mill, which a religious man did, but the outcome of their intentions was different.

<h2 id='tocuniq528'>(Chap. XXV.—Vers. 1 seq.)</h2>

(Chapter 25, verses 1 onwards) Then the kingdom of heaven will be like ten virgins, who took their lamps and went out to meet the bridegroom and the bride. Five of them were foolish, and five were wise. The foolish ones, when they took their lamps, did not take oil with them. But the wise ones took oil in their vessels along with their lamps. Some people simply interpret this parable, that is, the likeness of the ten virgins, in a straightforward manner: some, according to the Apostle, are virgins both in body and mind; others only preserving the virginity of their bodies, either not performing works similar to their aim, or being reserved for the care of their parents, nevertheless being married in mind (1 Corinthians 7). But it seems to me that a different meaning is being referred to in what is said, and that it pertains not to virginal bodies, but to the whole human race. For just as two women in the field and two women grinding at the mill signify two peoples, Christians and Jews, or saints and sinners, who are seemingly themselves plowing and grinding in the Church, yet they do everything in hypocrisy: so now all ten virgins embrace all people, who seem to believe in God and praise themselves in the Holy Scriptures, whether they be from the church, Jews, or heretics. Therefore, all virgins are called, because they boast in the knowledge of one God, and their minds are not defiled by the crowd of idolatry. Virgins have oil, who are adorned by faith and works. Those who appear to confess the Lord with similar faith do not have oil, but they neglect the works of virtue. We can interpret the five virgins, wise and foolish, as the five senses: some hasten to heavenly things and desire things above; others, gaping at earthly dregs, do not have the remedies of truth to illuminate their hearts. It is spiritually said by sight, hearing, and touch: What we have seen, what we have heard, what we have looked upon with our eyes, and what our hands have touched (1 John 1:1). By taste: Taste and see that the Lord is sweet (Psalm 34:9). By smell: We run after the fragrance of your ointments (Song of Songs 1:3). And: We are the sweet fragrance of Christ (2 Corinthians 2:15).

<h2 id='tocuniq529'>(Vers. 5.)</h2>

(Verse 5) But while the bridegroom delayed, they all slumbered and slept. For not a little time passes between the first and second coming of the Lord. They all slumbered, that is, they died: for the death of the saints is called sleep. Afterwards it is said, they slept: because they will be awakened later.

<h2 id='tocuniq530'>(Vers. 6.)</h2>

(Verse 6.) But in the middle of the night, a cry was made, behold the bridegroom is coming, go out to meet him. Suddenly, like in the darkest night, and when everyone is fast asleep, through the cry of angels and the trumpets of preceding powers, the coming of Christ will resound. Let us say something that may be useful to the reader. The tradition of the Jews is that Christ will come in the middle of the night in a similar way to the time of the Egyptians, when the Passover was celebrated, and the destroyer came, and the Lord passed over the dwellings, and the doorposts of our homes were consecrated with the blood of the lamb (Exodus 12). Hence, I believe that the apostolic tradition has persevered, so that on the eve of Easter, it is not allowed to dismiss the people until half of the night, waiting for the coming of Christ. And after that time has passed, with presumed security, everyone celebrates the feast day. From this, the psalmist said: At midnight, I arose to give thanks to you for your righteous judgments (Psalm 119:62).

<h2 id='tocuniq531'>(Vers. 7.)</h2>

(Verse 7.) Then all those maidens arose, and adorned their lamps. All 204 maidens arose, and each adorned their lamps, that is, the senses, in which they received the oil of knowledge, so that they would have the works of virtue, which would shine before the true judge.

<h2 id='tocuniq532'>(Vers. 8.)</h2>

(Verse 8.) But the foolish said to the wise: 'Give us some of your oil, for our lamps are going out.' They who complain that their lamps are going out, show that they shine only in part; and yet they do not have an unfailing light, nor perpetual works. Therefore, if anyone has a virgin soul, and is a lover of purity, they should not be content with mediocre things that quickly fade away and wither when the heat rises; but they should strive for perfect virtues, so that they may have everlasting light.


<h2 id='tocuniq533'>(Vers. 9.)</h2>

(Verse 9) The wise responded, saying: Lest perhaps it may not be enough for us and for you. They respond to this, not out of greed, but out of fear. For each person will receive a reward according to their works, and the virtues of some cannot lift up the vices of others on the day of judgment. And just as during the Babylonian captivity, Jeremiah could not help the sinners, and it is said to him: Do not pray for this people (Jeremiah 7:16): so fearful will be that day, when each person will be anxious for themselves alone.


Go instead to the sellers and buy for yourselves. This oil is sold, and it is bought at a high price, and it is obtained with difficult labor, which we understand in almsgivings and in all virtues and counsels of the magistrates.

<h2 id='tocuniq534'>(Vers. 10.)</h2>

(Verse 10.) But while they were going to buy, the bridegroom came. They indeed give a wise counsel, that they should not meet the bridegroom without oil for their lamps: but because the time for buying had already passed, and with the coming of the day of judgment, there was no place for repentance, as the Psalmist says: In hell, who shall confess to you? (Psalm 6:6) They are compelled not to commit new works, but to settle the account of past deeds.

And those who were invited entered with him to the wedding feast, and the door was shut. After the day of judgment, the opportunity for good works and justice will not be left.

<h2 id='tocuniq535'>(Vers. 11.)</h2>

(Verse 11.) But at last the other virgins also came, saying: Lord, Lord, open to us. The excellent confession indeed in calling upon the Lord, and the same repetition, is an indication of faith. But what profit is there in invoking with words, when you deny him with your actions?

<h2 id='tocuniq536'>(Vers. 12.)</h2>

(Verse 12.) But he answered and said: Amen I say to you, I do not know you. The Lord knows those who are his, and whoever does not know, will not be known (2 Timothy 2:19). The Lord does not know the workers of iniquity: and although they may be virgins, and may boast in both the purity of their bodies and the confession of true faith (1 Corinthians 14:38); yet because they do not have the oil of knowledge, it is enough punishment for them to be unknown by the bridegroom.


<h2 id='tocuniq537'>(Vers. 13.)</h2>

(Verse 13.) Therefore, watch, for you do not know the day nor the hour. I always advise the prudent reader not to acquiesce in superstitious interpretations, and not to consider things that are said by the will of those who invent them, but to consider what is said before, in the middle, and afterwards, and to connect everything that has been written. Therefore, from this it follows: Watch, for you do not know the day nor the hour. This includes everything that was said, that is, about the two people in the field, and the two grinding at the mill, and the master of the house who entrusts his possessions to his servant, and the ten virgins. Therefore, these parables were presented so that, because we all are ignorant of the day of judgment, we may diligently prepare the light of good works, so that, while we are ignorant, the judge may come.


<h2 id='tocuniq538'>(Vers. 14, 15.)</h2>

(Verse 14, 15.) For as a man going into a far country, called his servants, and delivered to them his goods. And to one he gave five talents, and to another two, and to another one, to every one according to his proper ability: and immediately he took his journey. This man, without doubt, is Christ, who after his resurrection, ascending as a conqueror to the Father, called his apostles and delivered to them the doctrine of the Gospel, not giving more to one and less to another based on generosity or stinginess, but according to the abilities of the recipients: just as the Apostle says that he fed those who could not take solid food with milk (1 Cor. 4). Finally, he who had made ten talents from five, and he who had made four from two, received the same joy; not considering the magnitude of profit, but the willingness of effort. In five, two, and one talent, let us understand different gifts that have been given to each person. Or in the first, all senses examined: In the second, intelligence and works: In the third, reason, by which we are separated from animals.


<h2 id='tocuniq539'>(Vers. 16.)</h2>

(Verse 16) But the one who had received the five talents went and worked with them, and he gained another five talents. Having received earthly senses, he doubled his knowledge of heavenly things: understanding the Creator through His creation, the incorporeal through the corporeal, the invisible through the visible, the temporary through the eternal.

<h2 id='tocuniq540'>(Vers. 17.)</h2>

(Verse 17) Likewise, the one who had received two also gained two more. And this person, according to his abilities, doubled whatever he had learned in the Law in the Gospel: whether he understood knowledge and good deeds of present life, or the patterns of future blessedness.

<h2 id='tocuniq541'>(Vers. 18.)</h2>

(Verse 18.) But he who had received one went and dug in the ground and hid his master's money. The wicked servant, occupied with earthly works and worldly pleasures, neglected and defiled the commandments of God. Although it is written elsewhere by another evangelist that he bound it in a cloth (Luke 19), that is, he weakened the doctrine of the master of the house by living softly and delicately.

<h2 id='tocuniq542'>(Vers. 19, 20.)</h2>

(Verse 19, 20.) After a long time, the master of those servants came and settled accounts with them. And he who had received the five talents came forward, bringing five talents more, saying, 'Master, you delivered to me five talents; here, I have made five talents more.' It is a great time between the Ascension of the Savior and his second coming. But if the apostles are to give an account and be resurrected in fear of the judge, what ought we to do?


<h2 id='tocuniq543'>(Vers. 21-23.)</h2>

(Verse 21-23.) His master said to him: Well done, good and faithful servant! You have been faithful over a little; I will set you over much. Enter into the joy of your master. And he also who had the two talents came forward, saying, 'Master, you delivered to me two talents; here, I have made two talents more.' His master said to him: Well done, good and faithful servant! You have been faithful over a little; I will set you over much. Enter into the joy of your master. I keep on telling both, as I said before, and he who had made ten talents out of five, and he who had made four out of two, the same speech flatters the same master of the house. And it should be noted that all the things we have at present, however great and numerous they may seem, are small and few compared to future things. 'Enter,' he says, 'into the joy of your master, and receive what no eye has seen, nor ear heard, nor has entered into the heart of man' (I Cor. II). But what can be given greater to a faithful servant than to be with the Lord, and to see the joy of his Lord?

<h2 id='tocuniq544'>(Vers. 24, 25.)</h2>

(Verse 24, 25) But he who had received one talent also approached and said: Lord, I know that you are a hard man; you reap where you did not sow, and gather where you did not scatter. And fearing, I went and hid your talent in the ground. Here you have what is yours. Truly, what is written has been fulfilled: 'To excuse excuses in sins' (Psalm 140:4). It happened even to this servant, that to laziness and negligence, the crime of pride also joined. For whoever should straightforwardly confess his inaction and beg the head of the household, on the contrary he accuses falsely and says that he acted wisely, in order that while he seeks the gains of money, he may not even risk his own fate.

<h2 id='tocuniq545'>(Vers. 26-28.)</h2>

(Vers. 26-28.) But his lord answering, said to him: Wicked and slothful servant, thou knewest that I reap where I sow not, and gather where I have not strewed. Thou oughtest therefore to have committed my money to the bankers, and at my coming I should have received my own with usury. Take ye away therefore the talent from him, and give it to him that hath ten talents. For to everyone that hath shall be given, and he shall abound: but from him that hath not, that also which he seemeth to have shall be taken away. The lazy person, because he did not want to double the talent, is condemned in the one case for pride, in the other for negligence. 'If,' he says, 'you knew me to be harsh and cruel, and that I pursue other people's things, and there reap where I have not sown, why did not such a thought of fear impress you, so that you would know that I would seek my own more diligently, and give my money, or silver, to the money-changers? For both words mean 'silver' in Greek. 'The words of the Lord are pure words, like silver tested by fire, proved on earth, purified seven times' (Ps. 11:7). Therefore, money and silver is the proclamation of the Gospel, and a divine discourse, which should have been given to money-changers and bankers, that is, to other teachers (which the apostles did, ordaining elders and bishops in each province), or to all believers, who can double the money and return it with interest, so that they may fulfill in practice whatever they have learned in words. However, the talent is taken away and given to the one who made ten talents, so that we may understand that, although in both labors there is an equal joy of the master, that is, of the one who doubled five into ten and of the one who doubled two into four, a greater reward is owed to the one who worked more with the master's money. Where the Apostle says: Honour the presbyters, who are truly presbyters, especially those who labour in the word of God (I Tim. 5:17) . From the fact that the wicked servant dared to say: I reap where I did not sow, and gather where I did not scatter, we understand that even the good life of the Gentiles and philosophers is acceptable to the Lord, and that those who act justly are different from those who act unjustly, and that those who neglect the written law are condemned in comparison to those who serve the natural law.


<h2 id='tocuniq546'>(Vers. 29.)</h2>

(Verse 29.) For to everyone who has, more will be given, and he will have an abundance. But from the one who does not have, even what he has will be taken away. Many, even though they may naturally be wise and have sharp intellect, if they are negligent and laziness corrupts the goodness of their nature, compared to someone who may be a little slower but has compensated for what they lacked through hard work and diligence, they lose the goodness of their nature and the reward that had been promised to them is seen passing on to others. It can also be understood this way: to him who truly believes and has good will in the Lord, even if he may lack something in his works as a human, it will be given by the good judge. But he who does not have faith, even the other virtues which he seemingly naturally possessed, will be lost. And elegantly even, it is said, that which he seems to have will be taken away from him.
