For whatever is without the faith of Christ should not be attributed to him who has wrongly misused it, but to him who has also assigned good to even the servant of nature.


<h2 id='tocuniq547'>(Vers. 30)</h2>

(Verse 30) And throw out the unprofitable servant into the outer darkness: there will be weeping and gnashing of teeth. The Lord is light; whoever is sent out from Him is truly without light. But as for the weeping and gnashing of teeth, we have already explained it above.

<h2 id='tocuniq548'>(Vers. 31 seq.)</h2>

(Vers. 31 seq.) But when the Son of Man comes in his glory, and all the angels with him, then he will sit on the throne of his glory. And all the nations will be gathered before him, and he will separate them one from another, as a shepherd separates the sheep from the goats. And he will place the sheep on his right hand, but the goats on the left. Then the king will say to those on his right hand, 'After two days I will celebrate the Passover and be handed over to be crucified and mocked by men; and I will be given vinegar and gall to drink; and in this way, he rightly precedes the glory of the triumphant, so that, following scandals, he may compensate with the reward of his promise.' And it is to be noted that the one who is to be seen in majesty is the Son of Man. And what follows: He shall set the sheep indeed on his right hand, but the goats on the left, understand according to that which you read elsewhere: The heart of the wise is in his right hand, and the heart of the fool is in his left (Eccl. X, 2). And above in this same Gospel: Let not your left hand know what your right hand doeth (Matt. VI, 3). The sheep are commanded to stand on the right hand, that is, the righteous, but the goats, that is, the sinners, on the left, who are always offered for sin in the Law (Exod. XII). And he did not mention the goats, which can have offspring, and when they are shorn they come out of the bath, all with twin offspring, and no sterile one among them (Can. IV); but he mentioned the kids, an amorous and playful animal, always eager for mating.

<h2 id='tocuniq549'>(Vers. 34 seq.)</h2>

(Verse 34 onwards) Come, you blessed of my Father, inherit the kingdom prepared for you from the foundation of the world. For I was hungry and you gave me food to eat. I was thirsty and you gave me something to drink. I was a stranger and you welcomed me. I was naked and you clothed me. I was sick and you visited me. I was in prison and you came to me. Then the righteous will answer him, saying: Lord, when did we see you hungry and feed you, or thirsty and give you something to drink? But when did we see you as a guest and welcome you, or naked and clothe you? When did we see you sick or in prison and visit you?' And the king will answer them, 'Truly, I say to you, as you did it to one of the least of these my brothers, you did it to me.'

<h2 id='tocuniq550'>(Vers. 40, 41.)</h2>

(Verse 40, 41.) Amen I say to you, as long as you did it to one of these least brothers of mine, you did it to me. Then He will say to those on His left, 'Depart from me, you cursed, into the eternal fire prepared for the devil and his angels. For I was hungry and you gave me no food, I was thirsty and you gave me no drink, a stranger and you did not welcome me, naked and you did not clothe me, sick and in prison and you did not visit me.' Then they will answer him, saying: Lord, when did we see you hungry, or thirsty, or a stranger, or naked, or sick, or in prison, and did not minister to you? Then he will answer them, saying: Amen I say to you, as long as you did not do it to one of these least ones, neither did you do it to me. It was a liberating insight for us that Christ, hungry, would be fed in every poor person, thirsty would be given drink, a stranger would be brought into shelter, naked would be clothed, the sick would be visited, and the imprisoned would find solace in speaking with him. But from this that follows: Whatever you did to one of these my least brethren, you did it to me, it does not seem to me that he was speaking generally about the poor, but about those who are poor in spirit, to whom he is reaching out a hand, he had said: These are my brothers and my mother, who do the will of my Father (Mark 3:34-35; Luke 8:21).

<h2 id='tocuniq551'>(Vers. 46.)</h2>

(Verse 46.) And these will go into eternal punishment, but the righteous into eternal life. Wise reader, take note that both eternal punishments and perpetual life have no fear of ruin thereafter.

<h2 id='tocuniq552'>(Chap. XXVI.—Vers. 1 seq.)</h2>

(Chapter XXVI.—Verses 1ff) And it came to pass, when Jesus had finished all these words, he said to his disciples: You know that after two days the Passover will be here, and the Son of Man will be betrayed and crucified. Let those who think that the Savior feared death be ashamed, for out of fear of suffering he said: Father, if it is possible, let this cup pass from me (Luke 22:42). He knew that he would be betrayed and crucified after two days, yet he does not avoid danger, nor does he flee in fear. He is so courageous that even when others refuse to go, he goes resolutely, as Thomas says: Let us also go, that we may die with him (John 11:16). And desiring to put an end to the carnal festivities, and to restore the truth of Easter by passing over to the shadow, he said: With desire have I desired to eat this pasch with you, before I suffer (Luke 22:15). For even Christ our pasch is sacrificed (1 Corinthians 5:7), if we eat it not in the unleavened bread of sincerity and truth. Moreover, when he says: After two days shall be the pasch (Mark 14:1), let us seek after that which is sacred, leaving aside any simple understanding. After two days of bright light, the true Passover for the world is celebrated, which is called in Hebrew Phase, not from the passion as most believe, but from the crossing over: because the exterminator, seeing the blood, passed through the doors of the Israelites and did not strike them. Or rather, the Lord Himself, providing assistance, walked above His people. Read the book of Exodus (Ch. XI, XII), about which we will discuss more fully if life permits. But our crossing, that is, the Passover, is celebrated in this way: if leaving behind earthly things and Egypt, we hasten towards heavenly things.

<h2 id='tocuniq553'>(Vers. 3 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 3 and following) Then the chief priests and the elders of the people gathered in the courtyard of the high priest, who was called Caiaphas, and they plotted to arrest Jesus by deceit and kill him. But they said, 'Not during the festival, or there may be a riot among the people.' Those who were supposed to prepare the victims for the upcoming Passover, polish the walls of the temple, sweep the floors, clean the vessels, and purify themselves according to the law in order to be worthy of eating the lamb, are gathered together to devise a plan to kill the Lord, not fearing rebellion, as the simple speech shows; but fearing that the people might take matters into their own hands to help him.


<h2 id='tocuniq554'>(Vers. 6)</h2>

(Verse 6) But when Jesus was in Bethany, in the house of Simon the leper, about to suffer for the whole world and redeem all nations with his blood, he stayed in Bethany, the house of obedience, which was formerly the house of Simon the leper. Not that Simon was still a leper at that time, but he who was formerly a leper had been cleansed by the Savior, with his original name remaining, so that the power of the healer may be evident. For in the catalog of the apostles, with his previous vice and profession, Matthew is called a tax collector, who had certainly ceased to be a tax collector."  } A certain leprous person represents the 212th part of the people, which believed in the Lord and was cured by Him. Simon himself is also said to be obedient, who can be interpreted in another sense as the world, in whose house the Church is cured.

<h2 id='tocuniq555'>(Vers. 7.)</h2>

(V. 7.) A woman came to him with an alabaster jar of expensive perfume and poured it on his head as he reclined. No one should think that she is the same woman who poured the perfume on his head and on his feet. For she washes with tears, wipes with her hair, and is clearly called a prostitute. But nothing like this is written about her. For the prostitute could not immediately become worthy of the Lord's head. Another evangelist placed the alabaster jar of expensive perfume (which is a type of marble) and placed pure and sincere nard (John 12), in order to demonstrate the faith of the Church and the Gentiles.


<h2 id='tocuniq556'>(Vers. 8, 9.)</h2>

(Verse 8, 9.) But when the disciples saw this, they were indignant and said, 'Why this waste? This could have been sold at a high price and the money given to the poor.' I know that some criticize this passage, questioning why only Judas is mentioned as being upset, when it is clear that all the apostles were ignorant of the symbolic meaning known as 'synecdoche,' where one is used to represent many or many are used to represent one. For even Paul in his Epistle which is written to the Hebrews (although many Latin writers doubt it), when he described the sufferings and merits of the saints, he added: They were stoned, they were tempted, they were sawn asunder, they were slain with the sword (Heb. 11:37), as if the Jews think that only Isaiah the Prophet was sawn asunder. We can also say that the apostles were truly indignant on account of the poor: but Judas on account of his gains. And his muttering is also condemned, for he did not care for the poor, but rather wanted to cater to his own thievery.

<h2 id='tocuniq557'>(Vers. 10, 11.)</h2>

(Ver. 10, 11.) But Jesus, knowing this, said to them: Why do you trouble this woman? For she has done a good work for me. For you will always have the poor with you, but you will not always have me. Another question arises, why did the Lord say to the disciples after the resurrection: Behold, I am with you always, even to the end of the age; and now he speaks, but you will not always have me. But it seems to me in this place he is speaking of his physical presence, which will not be with them in the same way after the resurrection, as it is now in every gathering and familiarity. The Apostle, mindful of this thing, says: 'So from now on we regard no one from a worldly point of view. Though we once regarded Christ in this way, we do so no longer.' (2 Corinthians 5:16)

<h2 id='tocuniq558'>(Vers. 12.)</h2>

(Verse 12) For she has poured this ointment on my body, to prepare me for burial. What you think is a waste of ointment is actually a burial custom. It is not surprising that she has given me the pleasant smell of her faith, since I am going to shed my blood for her.

<h2 id='tocuniq559'>(Vers. 12-14.)</h2>

(Verses 12-14.) Amen I say to you, wherever this Gospel is preached throughout the whole world, what this woman has done will also be told in memory of her. Then one of the twelve, who was called Judas Iscariot, went to the chief priests. In the whole world, not so much this woman as the Church is proclaimed, for having buried the Savior and anointed His head. And take note of future events, that He will suffer and die after two days, and that His Gospel will be celebrated throughout the whole world.


<h2 id='tocuniq560'>(Vers. 15.)</h2>

(Verse 15.) And he said to them, 'What are you willing to give me, and I will hand him over to you?' Unfortunate Judas, he thought he could compensate for the loss he had made by the shedding of the ointment with the price of the teacher. Yet he does not demand a specific amount, so that at least the betrayal might seem profitable, but he put in the power of the buyers the amount they wanted to give, as if it were a cheap slave.

<h2 id='tocuniq561'>214 (Vers. 16.)</h2>

214 (Verse 16.) But they agreed to give him thirty silver coins. And from then on he sought an opportunity to betray him. Joseph, contrary to what many think according to the Septuagint interpreters, was sold for twenty gold coins, but according to the Hebrew Truth, for twenty silver coins; for a servant could not be more valuable than the Lord.

<h2 id='tocuniq562'>(Vers. 17.)</h2>

(Verse 17) Now on the first day of the Feast of Unleavened Bread, the disciples came to Jesus, saying, 'Where do you want us to prepare for you to eat the Passover?' The first day of Unleavened Bread is on the fourteenth day of the first month, when the Passover lamb is sacrificed. It is also the day when the moon is full and the leaven is removed. Among the disciples who came to Jesus, they were asking, 'Where do you want us to prepare for you to eat the Passover?' And I suspect that Judas was the betrayer.

<h2 id='tocuniq563'>(Vers. 18.)</h2>

(Verse 18.) And Jesus said: Go into the city to a certain man, and say to him: The Teacher says, My time is near; I will keep the Passover at your house with my disciples. The new Scripture preserves the custom of the old Testament. We often read: He said to him, and in that place and that place; which in Hebrew is called Pheloni Elmoni (), and yet the names of persons and places are not given. And you will find there a man carrying a jar of water. For this reason, these words have been omitted, so that an opportunity for free celebration would be given to all who are going to celebrate Easter.

<h2 id='tocuniq564'>(Vers. 19.)</h2>

(Verse 19.) And the disciples did as Jesus had appointed them, and prepared the Passover. In another Gospel it is written (Luke 22) that they found a large upper room furnished and prepared there. But it seems to me that the upper room signifies the spiritual law, which, going out from the constraints of the letter, receives the Savior in a lofty place, as Paul himself says (Philippians 3), that he has considered the things that he once regarded as gain as garbage and filth, in order to prepare a worthy dwelling for the Lord.


<h2 id='tocuniq565'>(Vers. 20.)</h2>

(Verse 20.) And when evening came, he reclined at table with the twelve disciples. Judas acts in such a way that suspicion of being a betrayer is removed.

<h2 id='tocuniq566'>(Vers. 21.)</h2>

(Verse 21) And as they were eating, he said: Amen I say to you, that one of you is about to betray me. He who had predicted the Passion also predicts the betrayer, giving an opportunity for repentance, so that when he understood his thoughts and secret plans were known, he would repent of his deed. And yet he does not specifically point him out, so that he would not be openly accused and become more shameless. He casts the accusation in the plural, so that the guilty one may feel remorse.


<h2 id='tocuniq567'>(Vers. 22.)</h2>

(Verse 22) And they were greatly saddened, and one by one they began to say: Is it I, Lord? And certainly the eleven apostles knew that they had not thought anything of the sort against the Lord: but they believed more in the teacher than in themselves, fearing their own weakness, they sadly asked about the sin of which they were not aware of.

<h2 id='tocuniq568'>(Vers. 23.)</h2>

(Verse 23.) But He answered and said, He that dippeth his hand with me in the dish, the same shall betray me. Oh, the wonderful patience of the Lord! First He had said: one of you shall betray me. The traitor persists in evil, he reveals himself more clearly, yet he does not explicitly name himself. With the others saddened and pulling back their hands, and denying food to his own mouth, Judas, with audacity and impudence, by which he was to betray, even puts his hand with the Master into the dish, so as to deceitfully pretend to have a good conscience.


<h2 id='tocuniq569'>(Vers. 24.)</h2>

(Verse 24.) Woe, however, to that man by whom the Son of man will be betrayed. Neither at first, nor at second, does he retract his steps from the act of betrayal, but by the patience of the Lord he nourishes his impudence, and he stores up for himself wrath on the day of wrath (Rom. II). Punishment is foretold, so that the announced punishments may correct the one whom shame did not conquer. But what follows:

It would have been good for him if that man had not been born: Not because he is considered to have existed before he was born, because no one can be well off unless he has existed: but it is simply said, it is much better not to exist, than to exist in a bad way.

<h2 id='tocuniq570'>(Vers. 25.)</h2>

(Ver. 25.) But Judas, who betrayed him, answered and said: Is it I, Lord? Lest he should seem to betray himself by keeping silent, he also asks, being pricked by his conscience, who it was that had confidently sent his hand into the dish.

Am I, Rabbi? He said to him: You said it. And he unites a gesture of flattery, or a sign of disbelief. For the others who were not going to betray, they say: Am I, Lord? This one who was going to betray, does not call him Lord, but teacher, as if he had an excuse, if he denied the Lord, at least he would betray the teacher. And he said to him: You said it. The betrayer is refuted with the same response, with which Pilate will answer later.


<h2 id='tocuniq571'>(Vers. 26 seqq.)</h2>

(Vers. 26 seqq.) And as they were eating, Jesus took bread, and blessed it, and broke it, and gave it to the disciples, and said, Take, eat; this is my body. And he took the cup, and gave thanks, and gave it to them, saying, Drink ye all of it; For this is my blood of the new testament, which is shed for many for the remission of sins. After the paschal lamb had been fulfilled in its prefiguration, and he had eaten the flesh of the lamb with his apostles, he takes bread, which strengthens the heart of man, and passes on to the true sacrament of the Passover, so that just as Melchizedek, the high priest of the Most High God, had offered bread and wine in his prefiguration (Gen. XIV), he himself would also represent in truth his own body and blood. In Luke we read about two cups that Jesus offered to the disciples (Luke 22). One in the first month, and the other in the second, so that whoever could not eat the lamb among the holy ones in the first month, let him eat the goat among the penitents in the second month.

<h2 id='tocuniq572'>(Vers. 29.)</h2>

(Verse 29.) But I say to you, I will not drink from this fruit of the vine from now on until that day when I drink it new with you in my Father's kingdom. He transitions from worldly things to spiritual things, as the vineyard was transplanted from Egypt to the people of Israel, of whom the Lord speaks through Jeremiah: 'I have planted you as a true vine, but you have turned into a bitter fruit of a foreign vine.' (Jeremiah 2:21) And the prophet Isaiah sings in a song about his beloved, and the entire Scripture testifies in various places. He says, therefore, that he will not drink of this vine, except in the kingdom of his Father. The kingdom of the Father, I think, is the faith of the believers, confirmed also by the Apostle himself: The kingdom of God is among you (Luke 17:21). Therefore, when the Jews receive the kingdom of the Father (pay attention to what he says, the Father, not God), every Father is the name of the Son. When, I say, they believe in God the Father, and the Father brings them to the Son, then the Lord will drink of their wine, and, like Joseph reigning in Egypt, he will be intoxicated with his brothers.


<h2 id='tocuniq573'>(Vers. 30.)</h2>

(Verse 30.) And having sung a hymn, they went out to the Mount of Olives. This is what we read in a certain psalm: All the fat of the earth have eaten and have worshipped (Ps. XXI, 30). According to this example, whoever has been satisfied with the Savior's bread and intoxicated with the cup, can praise the Lord and ascend to the Mount of Olives, where there is refreshment from labors, solace from sorrow, and knowledge of true light.

<h2 id='tocuniq574'>(Vers. 31.)</h2>

(Verse 31.) Then Jesus said to them: All of you will be scandalized in me this night. He predicts that they will suffer, so that, when they have suffered, they will not despair of salvation, but by repenting, they will be freed. And he specifically added, in this night you will be scandalized; for just as those who are drunk are drunk at night: so too, those who suffer scandal endure in the night and in darkness (I Thess. 5). But we declare: The night is passed, and the day has drawn near (Rom. 13:12).


<h2 id='tocuniq575'>(Vers. 32.)</h2>

(Verse 32.) For it is written: I will strike the shepherd, and the sheep of the flock will be scattered. But after I have been raised up, I will go ahead of you into Galilee. This is also written in different words in the book of the prophet Zechariah; and (if I am not mistaken) it is said from the perspective of the prophet to God: Strike the shepherd, and the sheep of the flock will be scattered (Zech. 13:7). It is also fitting to this meaning in the sixty-eighth psalm, which is entirely sung by the Lord: For those whom you have struck, they have pursued. However, the good shepherd is struck so that he may lay down his life for his sheep, and out of many flocks of errors, one flock is made, and one shepherd (John 10). This testimony is more fully explained in the book, which we have written on the Best Method of Interpretation.

<h2 id='tocuniq576'>(Vers. 33.)</h2>

(V.33) But Peter answering, said to him: Although all shall be scandalized in thee, I will never be scandalized. It is not rashness, nor deceit; but the faith of the Apostle Peter, and his burning love for the Lord and Savior, of whom we have spoken above.

<h2 id='tocuniq577'>(Vers. 34.)</h2>

(Verse 34.) Jesus said to him: Truly I say to you, that in this night, before the rooster crows, you will deny me three times. And Peter, with a fervor of faith, promised, and the Savior, as if God, knew the future. And take note that Peter will deny in the night, and deny a third time. But after the rooster crowed, and as the darkness diminished, the approaching light was announced, Peter turned and wept bitterly, washing away the stains of denial with tears of repentance.

<h2 id='tocuniq578'>(Vers. 36.)</h2>

(Verse 36.) Then Jesus came with them to a village called Gethsemane and said to His disciples, 'Sit here while I go over there and pray.' Gethsemane means 'very fertile valley' in which He commanded the disciples to sit for a while and wait for Him to return while the Lord prayed for everyone alone.

<h2 id='tocuniq579'>(Vers. 37.)</h2>

(Verse 37) And taking Peter and the two sons of Zebedee, he began to be sorrowful and troubled. What we have said above about passion and pre-passion is also shown in this chapter, that the Lord, in order to prove the truth of assuming human nature, did indeed become sorrowful, but in order to prevent passion from dominating his soul, he began to be sorrowful in advance. For it is one thing to be sorrowful, and another to begin to be sorrowful. However, he was saddened not by the fear of suffering, since he had come for this purpose, to suffer, and he had accused Peter of cowardice. But it was because of the most unfortunate Judas, and the scandal of all the apostles, and the rejection of the Jewish people, and the destruction of miserable Jerusalem. Hence, Jonah was also saddened by the withering of the gourd or the ivy, not wanting his temporary dwelling to perish. But if they interpret the sadness of the soul as not the Savior's compassion for those who will perish, but as the passion of a heretic, let them respond: how do they explain that which is said in the person of God through Ezekiel: And in all these things you saddened me?


<h2 id='tocuniq580'>(Vers. 38.)</h2>

(Verse 38) Then he said to them, 'My soul is sorrowful even to death. Stay here and keep watch with me.' The soul is saddened, not for death itself, but saddened until it is freed from suffering by the apostles' own passion. And when he commanded them to stay here and keep watch with him, he was not prohibiting sleep, the time of which was not approaching danger, but rather prohibiting the sleep of unbelief and the torpor of the mind. Therefore let those who suspect that Jesus took on an irrational soul, say how He could be saddened and know the time of sadness. For although even brute animals mourn, they nevertheless do not know neither the causes nor the time until which they should be saddened.

<h2 id='tocuniq581'>(Vers. 39.)</h2>

(Verse 39) And going on a little, he fell on his face, praying and saying: My Father, if it be possible, let this cup pass from me. Nevertheless, not as I will, but as you will. Having given the apostles the command to endure and keep watch with the Lord, he went a little further and fell on his face, showing the humility of his mind in the form of flesh, and he speaks with endearment: My Father, and he requests that, if possible, the cup of suffering pass from him, of which we have spoken before. But he requests not to suffer out of fear, but out of the mercy for the former people, lest he drink the cup offered by them. Wherefore, he expressly did not say, let this cup pass from me, but let this cup, that is, the cup of the Jewish people, which cannot have the excuse of ignorance, if they kill me, having the Law and the prophets, who prophesy about me daily. However, turning towards himself, what he had scrupulously refused from the perspective of a man, he confirms from the perspective of God and the Son. However, not as I want, but as you. No, he says, let it not be done according to the human affection that I speak; but because of which I descended to your lands by your will.

<h2 id='tocuniq582'>(Vers. 40.)</h2>

(Verse 40) And he came to his disciples and found them sleeping, and he said to Peter: So you could not watch with me one hour? He who had said before: Even if all are scandalized in you, I will never be scandalized, now cannot overcome sleep due to the magnitude of sadness.

<h2 id='tocuniq583'>(Vers. 41.)</h2>

(Verse 41.) Watch and pray, so that you may not enter into temptation. It is impossible for the human soul not to be tempted. Therefore, in the Lord's Prayer, we say: Lead us not into temptation, which we cannot bear. (Matthew 6:13; Luke 11:4). We are not completely rejecting temptation, but rather, praying for the strength to withstand it. Therefore, at present, it does not say: Watch and pray, lest you be tempted; but rather, so that you do not enter into temptation, meaning, so that temptation does not overcome and conquer you, and hold you within its snares." } For example: A martyr, who sheds his blood for the confession of the Lord, is indeed tempted; but he is not bound by the snares of temptations. However, whoever denies, falls into the wounds of temptation.

The spirit indeed is willing, but the flesh is weak. This is against the reckless, who think that they can achieve whatever they believe. Therefore, as much as we trust in the ardor of the mind, so much do we fear the fragility of the flesh. But nevertheless, according to the Apostle, the works of the flesh are mortified in the spirit (1 Peter 3).

<h2 id='tocuniq584'>(Vers. 42.)</h2>

(Verse 42) Again, for the second time, he went away and prayed, saying: My Father, if this chalice cannot pass away, unless I drink it, may your will be done. He prays a second time, that if Nineveh cannot be saved in any other way, unless the gourd withers, may the will of the Father be done, which is not contrary to the will of the Son, as he himself says through the prophet: To do your will, O God, I desired (Ps. 39:9).

<h2 id='tocuniq585'>(Vers. 43, 44.)</h2>

(Verse 43, 44.) And he came again and found them sleeping. For their eyes were heavy. And leaving them, he went away again and prayed for the third time, saying the same words. He alone prays for all, just as he alone suffers for everyone. But the eyes of the apostles grew weak and burdened with imminent denial.

<h2 id='tocuniq586'>(Vers. 45.)</h2>

(Verse 45) Then He came to His disciples and said to them, 'Sleep now, and rest: behold, the hour is at hand, and the Son of Man will be delivered into the hands of sinners' (Matthew 26:45 and 2 Corinthians 13). After He had prayed a third time, asking that every word be confirmed by the testimony of two or three witnesses, and having obtained through subsequent repentance that the fear of the apostles would be corrected, He goes confidently towards His persecutors and willingly offers Himself to be killed. And He said to His disciples:

<h2 id='tocuniq587'>(Vers. 46, 47.)</h2>

(Verse 46, 47.) Arise, let us go, behold, the one who will betray me is approaching. While he was still speaking, behold, Judas, one of the twelve, came, and with him a great crowd with swords and clubs, sent by the chief priests and elders of the people. Let us not be found like those who fear and retreat, let us willingly go towards death, so that they may see our confidence and joy in suffering.

<h2 id='tocuniq588'>(Vers. 48.)</h2>

(Verse 48.) But he who betrayed him, gave them a sign, saying: Whomsoever I shall kiss, that same is he, hold him fast. Miserable Judas, and yet not pitiable, with the same unfaithfulness with which he betrayed his master and Lord, he believed that the signs, which he saw the Savior performing, were not done by divine power, but by magic arts. And because he had perhaps heard of him being transfigured on the mountain, he feared that he might escape from the hands of the ministers in a similar transformation. Therefore, give a sign, so that they may know that it is him whom you would show with a kiss.

<h2 id='tocuniq589'>(Vers. 49.)</h2>

(Verse 49.) And immediately approaching Jesus, he said: Hail, Rabbi. And he kissed him. Indeed, with shameless and wicked confidence, calling the teacher and kissing him, whom he was betraying. Yet the disciple still has some sense of shame, as he does not hand him over to his persecutors openly, but through the sign of a kiss. This is the sign that God placed on Cain, so that whoever found him would kill him (Genesis IV).

<h2 id='tocuniq590'>(Vers. 50.)</h2>

(Verse 50) And Jesus said to him: Friend, why have you come? Then they came and laid hands on Jesus, and arrested Him. The word, Friend, is to be understood either as a response, or certainly according to what we read above: Friend, how did you come in here without a wedding garment (Matt. XXII, 12)?

<h2 id='tocuniq591'>(Vers. 51.)</h2>

(Verse 51) And behold, one of those who were with Jesus, extending his hand, drew out his sword and struck the servant of the high priest, cutting off his ear. In another gospel it is written that Peter did this, with the same fervor of mind as with everything else. The servant of the high priest is also called Malchus: the ear that was cut off is the right one. It must be briefly said that Malchus, that is, formerly the king of the Jewish people, became a servant of impiety and the greed of the priests. And he has lost his right ear so that he hears all the cheapness of the letter in his left: but the Lord has given the right ear back to those who wanted to believe from the Jews, and has made them a royal and priestly race.

<h2 id='tocuniq592'>(Vers. 52.)</h2>

(Verse 52.) Then Jesus said to him: Put your sword back in its place. For all who draw the sword will die by the sword. And if one does not carry the sword in vain, who is appointed as the avenger of the Lord's wrath against those who do evil: yet whoever takes up the sword will die by the sword. Which sword? The one that is turned into a fiery one before paradise (Genesis 3): and the sword of the spirit, which is described as the armor of God (Ephesians 6).


<h2 id='tocuniq593'>(Vers. 53, 54.)</h2>

(Verse 53, 54.) Do you think that I cannot ask my Father, and he will at once send me more than twelve legions of angels? But how then would the Scriptures be fulfilled, that it must happen this way? I do not need the help of twelve apostles, even if they all defended me. I can have twelve legions of angelic armies. One legion among the ancient people was composed of six thousand men. For the sake of brevity, we will not explain the number of troops at this time, but it is enough to say that seventy-two thousand angels, divided into as many nations as there are human languages, would make up twelve legions. The following sentence shows a ready mind to suffer, that the prophets would have sung in vain unless the Lord had truly affirmed their words by his suffering.

<h2 id='tocuniq594'>(Vers. 55.)</h2>

(Verse 55.) In that hour Jesus said to the crowds: Are you coming out with swords and clubs to capture me, as if I were a robber? Every day I sat in the temple teaching, and you did not seize me. It is foolish, he said, to seek with swords and clubs the one who willingly surrenders himself into your hands, and to search for him as if he were hiding in the darkness and avoiding your eyes, when he teaches daily in the temple. But you gather against me in the darkness because your power is in the darkness.

<h2 id='tocuniq595'>(Vers. 56.)</h2>

(Verse 56) But all this has happened so that the scriptures of the prophets might be fulfilled. Then all the disciples, leaving him, fled. What are the scriptures of the prophets? They have pierced my hands and my feet (Ps. 22:17); and elsewhere: He was led like a sheep to the slaughter (Isaiah 53:7). And in another place: He was led to death because of the iniquities of my people (Ibid., sec. 70).

<h2 id='tocuniq596'>(Vers. 57.)</h2>

(Verse 57.) And they that held Jesus led him away to Caiaphas, the high priest, where the scribes and the elders were assembled. Moses, at God's command, had decreed that the priesthood should descend from father to son, and that the succession of priests should be maintained in the generations (Exodus 29). Josephus reports that Caiaphas bought the high priest's office from Herod for a year only. Therefore, it is not surprising that this wicked high priest judges unjustly.


<h2 id='tocuniq597'>(Vers. 58.)</h2>

(Verse 58.) But Peter followed him from afar to the courtyard of the high priest. He followed from afar, who was going to deny the Lord.

<h2 id='tocuniq598'>(Vers. 59, 60.)</h2>

(Verse 59, 60.) And going inside, he sat with the officers, to see the end. But the chief priests and the whole council were seeking false testimony against Jesus, that they might put him to death. And they did not find any, though many false witnesses came forward. Either out of love for the disciples, or out of human curiosity, the high priest wanted to know what judgment he should render concerning the Lord: whether he should condemn him to death or release him after flogging. And in this matter there was a difference among the ten apostles and Peter. Those people flee, that one, although far away, still follows the Savior.

<h2 id='tocuniq599'>(Vers. 61.)</h2>

(Verse 61) However, two false witnesses came forward and said, 'He said, 'I can destroy the temple of God and rebuild it in three days.'' How are they false witnesses if they are saying what we read the Lord said? But a false witness is one who does not understand the words in the same sense as they are spoken. For the Lord had spoken about the temple of his body. But even in their own words, they are slandering and by adding or changing a few, they make an unjust accusation. The Savior said, 'Destroy this temple, and in three days I will raise it up.' They responded, 'It took forty-six years to build this temple, and will You raise it up in three days?' But He was speaking of the temple of His body. Therefore, when He was raised from the dead, His disciples remembered that He had said this; and they believed the Scripture and the word which Jesus had spoken.


<h2 id='tocuniq600'>(Vers. 62.)</h2>

(Verse 62.) And the high priest, standing up, said to him: Do you not answer anything to what these witness against you? But Jesus kept silent. The high priest, with a sudden outburst of anger and impatience, not finding a place for calumny, shook the pontiff from his throne, in order to show the madness of his mind through the motion of his body. The more Jesus remained silent in response to unworthy men, false witnesses, and impious priests, the more the pontiff, overcome with rage, challenged him to respond, so that he could find an opportunity to accuse him from any occasion of conversation. Nevertheless, Jesus remained silent. For he knew, as if God, that whatever he responded would be twisted into an accusation.

<h2 id='tocuniq601'>(Vers. 63.)</h2>

(Verse 63) And the high priest said to him: I adjure you by the living God, that you tell us if you are the Christ, the Son of God? Why do you adjure, most impious high priest, to accuse or to believe? If to accuse, others argue: condemn the silent one. If to believe, why did you not want to believe the one confessing?

<h2 id='tocuniq602'>(Vers. 64.)</h2>

(Verse 64) Jesus said to him: You have said it. Nevertheless, I say to you: from now on you will see the Son of man sitting at the right hand of the power of God and coming in the clouds of heaven. And a similar response against Pilate and against Caiaphas, so that they may condemn themselves by their own verdict.

<h2 id='tocuniq603'>(Vers. 65, 66.)</h2>

(Vers. 65, 66.) Then the high priest tore his garments, saying: He has blasphemed. What more need do we have for witnesses? Look, now you have heard the blasphemy. What do you think? And they answered, saying: He is worthy of death. The same fury that had driven him from the priestly throne now incites him to tear his garments. He tore his garments in order to show that the Jews had lost the glory of the priesthood and that the pontiffs held an empty seat. But it is also a Jewish custom, when they hear something blasphemous and seemingly against God, to tear their garments. We read that Paul and Barnabas did this when they were honored with divine worship in Lycaonia. However, Herod, because he did not give honor to God but acquiesced to the excessive favor of the people, was immediately struck by an angel.

<h2 id='tocuniq604'>(Vers. 67.)</h2>

(Verse 67.) Then they spat in his face, and struck him with their fists. Thus was fulfilled what was spoken: I gave my cheeks to those who struck me, and my face I did not hide from disgrace and spitting (Lamentations 3:30).

<h2 id='tocuniq605'>(Vers. 68.)</h2>

(Verse 68) But others struck Him on the face, saying: Prophesy to us, Christ, who is it that struck you? It would have been foolish to respond to those who were beating Him and to prophesy the one who was about to strike Him, when it clearly appeared to be the act of a madman. But just as He did not prophesy this to you, He very clearly predicted that Jerusalem would be surrounded by an army and not one stone would be left upon another in the temple.

<h2 id='tocuniq606'>(Vers. 69.)</h2>

(Verse 69.) But Peter was sitting outside in the courtyard. He was sitting outside so that he could see the outcome of the matter. And he did not approach Jesus, so that no suspicion would arise among the officials.

<h2 id='tocuniq607'>(Vers. 72.)</h2>

(Verse 72) And again he denied with an oath, 'I do not know the man.' And after a little while those who stood by came up and said to Peter, 'Surely you are one of them, for your accent betrays you.' Then he began to invoke a curse on himself and to swear, 'I do not know the man.' And immediately the rooster crowed. And Peter remembered the saying of Jesus, 'Before the rooster crows, you will deny me three times.' And he went out and wept bitterly. For if he did not deny, then the Lord has lied, who said: Truly I say to you, that tonight, before the rooster crows, you will deny me three times. See what he says, you will deny me, not a man.

<h2 id='tocuniq608'>(Vers. 73.)</h2>

(Verse 73.) Truly, you are also one of them: for even your speech betrays you. Not that Peter had a different language or was from a foreign nation. For all were Hebrews, both those who accused and those who were accused. But each province and region has its own peculiarities, and it cannot avoid the sound of the native language. Therefore, the people of Ephraim in the Book of Judges (chapter 12) cannot pronounce the word σύνθημα.


<h2 id='tocuniq609'>(Vers. 74, 75.)</h2>

(Verses 74, 75.) Then he began to curse and swear, saying that he did not know the man. And immediately the rooster crowed. And Peter remembered the word of Jesus, that he had said: Before the rooster crows, you will deny me three times. In another Gospel we read: that after Peter's denial and the rooster's crowing, the Savior looked at Peter and, with his gaze, provoked him to bitter tears. It was not possible for him to remain in the darkness of denial, whom the light of the world had looked upon.


And going out, he wept bitterly. Sitting in the courtyard of Caiaphas, he could not repent. He goes out from the assembly of the wicked, to wash the defiled denials with bitter tears of remorse.

<h2 id='tocuniq610'>(Chap. XXVII.—Vers. 1 seqq.)</h2>

(Chapter 27 - Verses 1 and following) When morning came, all the chief priests and elders of the people took counsel against Jesus to put him to death. And they bound him and led him away and delivered him over to Pilate the governor. Not only to Pilate, but also to Herod he was brought, so that both of them could mock the Lord. And see the eagerness of the priests for evil. They stayed awake all night to commit murder. And they handed him over to Pilate, bound. For they had this custom, that whoever they had sentenced to death, they would hand over bound to the judge.

Then Judas, who betrayed him, seeing that he was condemned, deeply remorseful, returned the thirty silver coins to the chief priests and elders, saying: 'I have sinned by betraying innocent blood.' He cast out the weight of his avarice, the magnitude of his impiety. Seeing the Lord condemned to death, Judas returned the price to the priests, as if he had the power to change the sentence of his persecutors. Therefore, although he changed his will, he did not change the outcome of his initial intention. But if he who delivered up the just blood sinned, how much more did the Jews sin, who bought the just blood, and, by offering a price, provoked the disciple to betray his master? Let those who attempt to introduce different natures, and claim that Judas, as a traitor, was of a bad nature and could not have been saved by choice and apostleship, respond as to how a bad nature could have repented.

<h2 id='tocuniq611'>(Vers. 5.)</h2>

(Vers. 5.) But they said: What is that to us? You see. And throwing the silver coins into the temple, he departed: and going away, he hanged himself. It was useless to have repented, by which he could not correct his crime. If a brother sins against a brother in such a way that he is able to correct what he has sinned, it can be forgiven. But if the works persist, repentance is assumed in vain. This is what is said in the psalm about the same most unfortunate Judas: And let his prayer be turned to sin (Psalm 108:7); so that not only could he not correct the crime of betrayal, but he also added to his previous crime the guilt of his own murder." } And this is what the Apostle says in his second letter to the Corinthians: 'So that on the contrary you should rather forgive and comfort him, lest perhaps such a one be swallowed up with too much sorrow.' (2 Corinthians 2:7)

<h2 id='tocuniq612'>(Vers. 6.)</h2>

(Verse 6.) But the chief priests, taking the silver, said: It is not lawful to put them into the corbona (another spelling: corbona), because it is the price of blood. Truly, straining out a gnat and swallowing a camel. For if they do not put money into the corbona, that is, into the treasury and the gifts of God, because it is the price of blood, why is blood itself being shed?

<h2 id='tocuniq613'>(Vers. 7, 8.)</h2>

(Verses 7, 8.) But after consulting, they bought a field from the potter, for the burial of strangers; therefore that field has been called the Field of Blood until this day. They indeed acted with a different intention, so that they would leave a lasting monument to their impiety from the purchase of the field. However, we, who were strangers to the Law and the prophets, have embraced their wicked pursuits for salvation; and we find rest in the price of his blood. But the field is called 'figulus' because our potter is Christ.

<h2 id='tocuniq614'>(Vers. 9, 10.)</h2>

(Vers. 9, 10.) Then was fulfilled what was spoken by Jeremiah the prophet, saying, 'And they took the thirty silver coins, the price of Him who was priced, whom they of the children of Israel priced, and gave them for the potter's field, as the Lord directed me.' This quotation is not found in Jeremiah. However, in Zechariah, who is almost the last of the twelve prophets, a similar passage is quoted (Zech. XI): and although the meaning does not differ much, yet the order and the wording are different. I recently read in a certain Hebrew volume, which a Hebrew from the Nazarene sect offered to me, an apocryphal book of Jeremiah, in which I found the following written word for word. However, it seems to me more like a reference to Zechariah: in the manner commonly used by the Evangelists and Apostles, who, without adhering to the exact order of words, present only the meaning from the Old Testament as an example.

<h2 id='tocuniq615'>(Vers. 11.)</h2>

(Verse 11) But Jesus stood before the governor, and the governor asked Him, saying: Are You the King of the Jews? When Pilate asked nothing else of Him, except whether He is the King of the Jews, the Jews are accused of impiety, because they were not even able to falsely find something to accuse the Savior of.

Jesus said to him: You say so. Thus he answered in order to speak the truth and not reveal the accusation. And note that although Pilate, who was unwilling to pronounce judgment, answered in part: He did not want to respond to the priests and leaders, deeming them unworthy of his words.

<h2 id='tocuniq616'>(Vers. 13 seqq.)</h2>

(Ver. 13 seqq.) Then Pilate said to him: Do you not hear how many testimonies they bring against you? And he did not respond to him with a word, so that the governor marveled greatly. Now at the feast, the governor was accustomed to releasing one prisoner to the crowd, whomever they desired. It is a Gentile who accuses Jesus, but he refers the matter to the Jewish people. Do you not hear how many testimonies they bring against you? But Jesus, on the other hand, did not want to respond at all, so that the accusation would not be cleared by the governor and the benefit of the cross would be delayed.

<h2 id='tocuniq617'>(Vers. 16 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 16 onwards) At that time, they had a notable prisoner named Barrabbas. So when they were gathered together, Pilate said to them: Whom do you want me to release to you, Barrabbas or Jesus who is called Christ? For he knew that they had handed Him over because of envy. Now in the Gospel that is written according to the Hebrews, the son of their teacher is interpreted, who had been condemned for sedition and murder. But Pilate offered them the option to release whomever they wanted, either a robber or Jesus; not hesitating, he chose Jesus, knowing that He had been handed over because of envy. Therefore, the clear cause of the cross is envy.

<h2 id='tocuniq618'>(Vers. 19 seqq.)</h2>

(v. 19 and following) But while he was sitting on the judgment seat, his wife sent to him, saying: Have thou nothing to do with that just man; for I have suffered many things this day in a dream because of him. And the chief priests and ancients persuaded the people that they should ask Barabbas and destroy Jesus. But the governor answering, said to them: Whether will you of the two to be released unto you? But they said: Barabbas. Note that often to the Gentiles dreams are revealed by God; and that the testimony of the people regarding Pilate and his wife confessing the just Lord is noteworthy." }


<h2 id='tocuniq619'>(Vers. 22, 23.)</h2>

(Verse 22, 23.) Pilate said to them: What then shall I do with Jesus who is called Christ? They all said: Crucify him. The governor said to them: For what evil has he done? But they shouted even more, saying: Crucify him. Pilate gave many opportunities to release the Savior. First, he compared him to a just thief. Then he asked: What then shall I do with Jesus who is called Christ? That is, your king. And when they answered, Crucify him, he did not immediately agree; but according to the suggestion of his wife, who had said: Have thou nothing to do with that just man, he also answered: For what evil has he done? By saying this, Pilate acquitted Jesus. But they shouted even more, saying: Crucify him. So that what was said in the twenty-first psalm would be fulfilled: Many dogs have surrounded me, and a band of evildoers has encircled me (Psalm 22:12). And also what Jeremiah said: My inheritance has become to me like a lion in the forest; they have raised their voice against me (Jeremiah 12:8). And likewise Isaiah in this fitting statement: I waited for them to bring justice, but they did evil instead of righteousness, and made an outcry (Isaiah 5:7).


<h2 id='tocuniq620'>(Vers. 24.)</h2>

(Verse 24) But seeing that Pilate was accomplishing nothing, but rather that a riot was occurring, he took some water and washed his hands in front of the crowd, saying: I am innocent of the blood of this just person: you shall see. Pilate took water, according to that prophecy: I will wash my hands amongst the innocent (Ps. 25:6); so that by the washing of his hands the works of the Gentiles would be cleansed, and he would make us strangers to the impiety of the Jews, who shouted, crucify him, in a way testifying to this and saying: Indeed, I wanted to set the innocent free; but since sedition arises and a charge of treason against Caesar is brought against me: I am innocent of the blood of this just person. The judge who is forced to pass sentence against Christ does not condemn the accused; but he reproaches those who offer him, pronouncing that he who is to be crucified is just. 'You,' he says, 'will see. I am the servant of the law: your voice spills blood.'

<h2 id='tocuniq621'>(Vers. 25.)</h2>

(Verse 25.) And all the people answered, saying: His blood be upon us and upon our children. This curse persists against the Jews even to this day, and the blood of the Lord is not removed from them. Hence, through Isaiah it is spoken: If you stretch out your hands to me, I will not hear you. For your hands are full of blood (Isaiah 1:15). The Jews leave the best inheritance to their children, saying: His blood be upon us and upon our children.


<h2 id='tocuniq622'>(Vers. 26.)</h2>

(Verse 26) Then he released Barabbas to them, but he had Jesus flogged and handed him over to be crucified. Barabbas, a robber who incited riots in the crowds and was a murderer, was released to the Jewish people, that is, the devil, who still reigns in them today, and therefore they cannot have peace. Jesus, on the other hand, being handed over by the Jews, is acquitted by Pilate's wife, and is called just by the governor himself. And the centurion confesses that he truly is the Son of God. Inquire, learned reader, how it was fitting for Pilate to wash his hands and say: I am innocent of the blood of this just person, and afterwards to deliver Jesus to be crucified, having been scourged? But it is to be known that he served the Roman laws by which it was sanctioned that one who is to be crucified should first be beaten with scourges. Therefore, Jesus was handed over to be beaten by the soldiers, and they cut those most sacred limbs, the chest capable of containing God, with scourges. But this was done so that, because it was written: 'Many are the scourges of sinners' (Psalm 31:10), by that scourging, we might be freed from scourges, with Scripture saying to the just man: 'The scourge will not come near your dwelling' (Psalm 90:10).

<h2 id='tocuniq623'>(Vers. 27 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 27 onwards) Then the soldiers of the governor took Jesus into the praetorium and gathered the whole cohort around Him. They stripped Him and put a scarlet robe on Him. And they twisted together a crown of thorns and put it on His head, and put a reed in His right hand. And they knelt down before Him and mocked Him, saying, 'Hail, King of the Jews!' The soldiers, because He had been called the King of the Jews, and the scribes and the priests accused Him of claiming to be the ruler of Israel, mocked Him in this way, to degrade Him from His former garments and dress Him in a scarlet robe as a mock royal garment, which ancient kings used. And they placed a crown of thorns on His head instead of a crown, and gave Him a reed as a scepter, and mocked Him as if He were a king. But we understand all these things mystically. For just as Caiaphas said: It is necessary for one man to die for the sake of all (John 11:50), not knowing what he was saying, so also, whatever they did, even though they may have had other intentions, they nevertheless bestowed sacraments upon us who believe. In the scarlet cloak, he sustains the bloody works of the nations; in the crown of thorns, he unravels the ancient curse; in the pen, he kills venomous creatures. Whether he held a pen in his hand to write sacrilege against the Jews.


<h2 id='tocuniq624'>(Vers. 30.)</h2>

(Verse 30) And spitting on him, they took a reed and struck his head. At that moment it was fulfilled; I did not turn my face away from the shame of spitting (Isaiah 50:6), and yet even when they strike his head with a reed, he patiently endures all, in order to fulfill the true prophecy of Isaiah, which says: He will not break a bruised reed (Isaiah 42:3).

<h2 id='tocuniq625'>(Vers. 31.)</h2>

(Verse 31) And after they had mocked him, they took off the cloak from him, and put his own clothes on him, and led him away to crucify him. When Jesus is whipped, spat upon, and mocked, he does not have his own clothes, but those which he had taken on for our sins. But when he is crucified, and the show of illusion and mockery has passed, then he receives back his original clothes and puts on his own attire; and immediately the elements are disturbed, and the creature gives witness to the Creator.


<h2 id='tocuniq626'>(Vers. 32.)</h2>

(Verse 32.) But as they were going out, they found a man from Cyrene, named Simon, and they forced him to carry his cross. Lest anyone think that this account is contrary to that of John the Evangelist. For he said that the Lord, as he went out of the praetorium, carried his own cross; but Matthew reports that they found a man from Cyrene, named Simon, whom they compelled to carry Jesus' cross. But this is to be understood that Jesus, as he went out of the praetorium, himself carried his own cross: afterwards they encountered Simon, whom they imposed the task of carrying the cross. But according to anagogical interpretation, the nations embrace the cross of Jesus, and the obedient stranger bears the ignominy of the Savior.

<h2 id='tocuniq627'>(Vers. 33.)</h2>

(Verse 33.) And they came to a place called Golgotha, which is the place of Calvary. I have heard someone explain that Calvary is the place where Adam was buried, and it is thus named because the head of the ancient man is buried there, and this is what the Apostle says: Arise, you who sleep, and arise from the dead, and Christ will enlighten you. A favorable interpretation that soothes the ears of the people, but not true. For outside the city and beyond the gate, there are places where the heads of the condemned are cut off, and Calvary, that is, the beheaded ones, have taken their name. Therefore, the Lord was crucified there, so that where there had been a site of condemnation, there the standards of martyrdom might be raised. And just as he was made a curse for us, and was whipped, and was crucified, so that he might be crucified as guilty among the guilty for the salvation of all. But if someone should wish to argue, why was the Lord crucified there, so that his blood might drip upon Adam's tomb, let us question him, why were other criminals also crucified in the same place? From which it is evident that Calvary does not signify the tomb of the first man, but rather the place of beheading, as where sin abounded, grace superabounded (Rom 5). But we read that Adam was buried near Hebron and Arba, in the volume of Jesus son of Nun (Josh 14).

<h2 id='tocuniq628'>(Vers. 34.)</h2>

(Verse 34) And they gave him vinegar to drink with gall mixed in, and when he had tasted it, he did not want to drink. God speaks to Jerusalem: I planted you as a true vine, how then have you become bitter as a foreign vine? (Jeremiah II, 21) The bitter vine makes bitter wine, which the Lord Jesus drank, so that what is written may be fulfilled: They gave me gall for my food, and in my thirst they gave me vinegar to drink (Psalm LXVIII, 22). But when it is said, 'And when he had tasted, he would not drink,' this indicates that he did indeed taste the bitterness of death for us, but on the third day he rose again.

<h2 id='tocuniq629'>(Vers. 35.)</h2>

(Verse 35) After they crucified him, they divided his garments, casting lots, so that what was spoken by the prophet might be fulfilled, saying: They divided my garments among them, and for my clothing they cast lots. And this was prophesied in the same psalm: They divided my garments among them, and for my clothing they cast lots (Psalm 22:18).

<h2 id='tocuniq630'>(Vers. 36.)</h2>

(Verse 36.) And they were sitting and watching over him. The diligence of the soldiers and priests benefits us, so that the greater and more evident power of his resurrection may appear.

<h2 id='tocuniq631'>(Vers. 37.)</h2>

(Verse 37.) And they placed upon his head his accusation written, This is Jesus, the king of the Jews. I cannot sufficiently admire, considering the greatness of the matter, that they, in order to deceive the redeemed by a false price and to incite an unfortunate people to sedition and clamor, found no other cause for his execution than that he was the king of the Jews. And perhaps they did this mockingly and laughing. However, Pilate also responded to those who did not want it: What I have written, I have written. Whether you want it or not, the Jews, the entire multitude of the nations, answer to you: Jesus is the king of the Jews, that is, the ruler of believers and confessors.

<h2 id='tocuniq632'>(Vers. 38.)</h2>

(Verse 38.) Then they crucified two thieves with him, one on the right and one on the left. If Golgotha is the burial place of Adam, and not a place of the condemned, and therefore the Lord is crucified there to raise up Adam, why are the two thieves crucified in the same place?

<h2 id='tocuniq633'>(Vers. 39 seqq.)</h2>

(v. 39 onwards) And those passing by blasphemed him, shaking their heads and saying, 'Ah! You who destroy the temple of God and rebuild it in three days, save yourself! If you are the Son of God, come down from the cross.' Similarly, the chief priests, along with the scribes and elders, mocked him, saying, 'He blasphemes, because he goes off the path and refuses to walk in the true way of the Scriptures. They shook their heads because they had already moved their feet before, and they did not stand on solid ground. But he, mocking, says that the foolish people believed false witnesses.

<h2 id='tocuniq634'>(Vers. 42.)</h2>

(Verse 42.) He saved others, but he cannot save himself. Even unwillingly, the scribes and Pharisees confess that he saved others. Therefore, your own verdict condemns you. For the one who saved others, surely if he wanted to, he could save himself.

<h2 id='tocuniq635'>(Vers. 43.)</h2>

(Verse 43.) If he is the king of Israel, let him come down from the cross, and we will believe in him. He trusts in God; let God deliver him now if he desires him. For he said, 'I am the Son of God.'" A fraudulent promise. What is more difficult, to descend from the cross while still alive, or to rise from the tomb while dead? He has risen, and you did not believe. Therefore, even if he were to descend from the cross, you would not believe. But it seems to me that the demons are instigating this. For as soon as the Lord was crucified, they sensed the power of the cross, and they understood that their powers were broken. And this is what they are doing, that he may descend from the cross. But the Lord, knowing the snares of his adversaries, remains on the scaffold in order to destroy the devil.


<h2 id='tocuniq636'>(Vers. 44.)</h2>

(Verse 44) And the thieves also, who were crucified with him, reproached him. Here, by way of a figure of speech called synecdoche, both thieves are portrayed as blaspheming. But Luke asserts that while one was blaspheming, the other confessed, and he rebuked the blasphemer. It is not that the Gospels disagree, but rather that both initially blasphemed, and then, as the sun set, the earth shook, rocks were split, and darkness fell, one of them believed in Jesus and corrected his previous denial with a subsequent confession. Among the two robbers, both the Gentiles and the Jews blasphemed the Lord at first. Later, one of them, terrified by the greatness of the signs, repented and continues to rebuke the Jews today for blasphemy.

<h2 id='tocuniq637'>(Vers. 45.)</h2>

(Verse 45) And at the sixth hour, darkness came over the whole land until the ninth hour. Those who wrote against the Gospels suspect a solar eclipse, which usually happens at fixed and regular times, as the disciples of Christ were mistakenly interpreted on the resurrection of the Lord: since a solar eclipse only occurs when the moon rises. However, there is no doubt that the moon was full at the time of Passover. And so, lest it should appear that the shadow of the earth, or a lunar eclipse, had caused a brief and rust-colored darkness to occur, it is stated to have lasted for a period of three hours, so that every opportunity for natural causes could be eliminated. And I believe this was done to fulfill the prophecy, which says: The sun shall go down at noon, and the earth shall be darkened in the day of light (Amos, VIII, 9); and in another place: The sun has gone down while it was still day (Jerem. XV, 9). And it seems to me that the brightest light of the world, that is, the greater luminary, withdrew its rays, so that it would not see the hanging Lord, or so that the wicked blasphemers would not enjoy its light.

<h2 id='tocuniq638'>(Vers. 46.)</h2>

(Verse 46.) And about the ninth hour, Jesus cried out with a loud voice, saying: Eli, Eli, lammasabacthani, which means, My God, My God, why have you forsaken me? He made use of the beginning of the twenty-first psalm, and that which is read in the middle of the verse: Look upon me, it is superfluous. For it is read in Hebrew: My God, My God, why have you forsaken me? Therefore, they are impious who believe that this psalm was spoken by David, or Esther, or Mordecai, since even the testimonies of the evangelists understand it to refer to the Savior, as when it says: They divided my garments among them, and upon my clothing they cast lots. And another thing: They pierced my hands and my feet. Do not be surprised by the lowly words and complaints of the abandoned, when you see the form of a servant, the scandal of the cross.

<h2 id='tocuniq639'>(Vers. 47.)</h2>

(Verse 47.) But some of those standing there, when they heard it, said: This man is calling for Elijah. Not everyone, but some, whom I believe to have been Roman soldiers, not understanding the propriety of the Hebrew language, thought that he was invoking Elijah because of what he said: Eli, Eli. However, if we want to understand those Jews who said this, they do so in their usual way, to defame the Lord of weakness, who is invoking Elijah's help.


<h2 id='tocuniq640'>(Vers. 48.)</h2>

(Verse 48.) And immediately one of them ran and took a sponge, soaked it in vinegar, put it on a reed, and gave it to Him to drink. And these things were done so that the prophecy would be fulfilled: 'In my thirst they gave me vinegar to drink' (Psalm 69:21). Even to this day, the Jews and all unbelievers drink vinegar and gall to Jesus in remembrance of His Resurrection; and they give Him wine mixed with myrrh to make Him sleep, so that He does not see their evil.

<h2 id='tocuniq641'>(Vers. 50.)</h2>

(Verse 50.) But Jesus, crying out again with a loud voice, yielded up his spirit. It is a testimony of divine power to freely release one's spirit, as He Himself had said: No one can take my life from me, but I lay it down of my own accord. I have the authority to lay it down, and I have the authority to take it up again (John 10:18).

<h2 id='tocuniq642'>(Vers. 51.)</h2>

(Verse 51.) And behold, the veil of the Temple was torn in two parts from top to bottom. The veil of the temple was torn, and all the sacred mysteries of the Law that were previously concealed were revealed and passed on to the Gentile people. In the Gospel, which we often mention, we read that the threshold of the temple, of infinite size, was broken and divided. Josephus also reports that the angelic virtues, former guardians of the temple, likewise cried out: Let us depart from these seats.


<h2 id='tocuniq643'>(Vers. 52.)</h2>

(Verse 52.) And the earth shook, and the rocks were split, and the tombs were opened. There is no doubt that ((Al. quid)) signifies literally the magnitude of the signs, such as the crucified Lord himself, and the heaven, and the earth, and all things. But it seems to me that the earthquake and the rest represent a type of the believers, who, having left behind their former errors and the hardness of their hearts, were first like the tombs of the dead, and later acknowledged the Creator.


<h2 id='tocuniq644'>(Vers. 53.)</h2>

(Verse 53.) And many bodies of the saints who had fallen asleep were raised. And coming out of the tombs after his resurrection, they went into the holy city, and appeared to many. Just as Lazarus, who was dead, was raised, so too many bodies of the saints were raised to show the Lord rising from the dead (John 11). And yet, although the tombs were opened, they did not rise until the Lord had risen, so that he would be the firstborn of the resurrection from the dead. But let us understand the holy city, in which they were seen to rise again, either as the heavenly Jerusalem, or this earthly one, which was formerly holy. Just as Matthew is called a tax collector, not because he remains a tax collector as an apostle, but because he retains the former title. The city of Jerusalem was called holy because of the temple and the holy of holies, and as a distinction from other cities where idols were worshiped. When it is said 'truly', it appears to many that the resurrection was not general, so that it would appear to everyone, but rather special to many, so that those who deserved could see.

<h2 id='tocuniq645'>(Vers. 54.)</h2>

(Verse 54.) But the centurion and those with him, guarding Jesus, seeing the earthquake and the things that were happening, were greatly afraid, saying, Truly this man was the Son of God. In another Gospel, after the earthquake, a clearer reason for the miracle of the centurion is explained: when he saw him release his spirit, he said, Truly this man was the Son of God. For no one has the power to release the spirit except the one who is the creator of souls. But let us understand spirit in this place as referring to the soul, either as making up a spiritual and vital body, or as the substance of the soul itself being spirit, according to what is written: 'You take away their breath, and they die' (Psalm 104:29). And it should be considered that the centurion, before the cross, truly confesses the Son of God in the very scandal of the Passion, while Arius preaches a creature in the Church.

<h2 id='tocuniq646'>(Vers. 55, 56.)</h2>

(Verse 55, 56) Now there were many women there from afar who had followed Jesus from Galilee, ministering to him: among whom were Mary Magdalene, and Mary the mother of James and Joseph, and the mother of the sons of Zebedee. It was the Jewish custom, and it was not considered a fault according to the ancient customs of the Gentiles, for women to provide food and clothing to their teachers from their own resources. Paul mentions that he rejected this because it could cause scandal among the nations. For he himself says: Do we not have the power to lead about sisters, women, as also the other apostles do? (I Cor. IX, 5) ? But the Lord provided for them from his substance, so that he might sow their carnal life, from whom they sowed spiritual things. Not because the Lord needed the food of creatures, but to show a pattern to teachers that they should be content with food and clothing provided by disciples. But let us see what companions he had: Mary Magdalene, from whom he had cast out seven demons, and Mary of James, and Joseph's mother, his aunt, sister of Mary, the mother of the Lord, and the mother of the sons of Zebedee, who had shortly before asked for the kingdom for her children, and others whom we read about in the other Gospels (Luke VIII).


<h2 id='tocuniq647'>(Vers. 57, 58.)</h2>

(Vers. 57, 58.) But when evening had come, a certain rich man from Arimathea named Joseph, who was also a disciple of Jesus, came. He approached Pilate and requested the body of Jesus. Then Pilate ordered the body to be given. The mention of the man being rich is not meant as a boast of the author, but to show the reason why he was able to obtain Jesus' body from Pilate. For it was not fitting for a poor and unknown person to approach the Roman governor and obtain the body of one who had been crucified. In another Gospel (Luke 23), this Joseph is called βουλευτὴς, which means counselor, and some think that the first psalm was composed about him: Blessed is the man who does not walk in the counsel of the wicked, and so on.

<h2 id='tocuniq648'>(Vers. 59.)</h2>

(Verse 59.) And Joseph, having received the body, wrapped it in a clean linen cloth. By this simple burial of the Lord, the ambition of the rich is condemned, who cannot even part with their wealth in tombs. We can also understand this spiritually, that the body of the Lord should be wrapped not in gold, gems, and silk, but in pure linen, even though this also signifies that Joseph wrapped Jesus in a clean linen cloth, who had received Him with a pure mind.


<h2 id='tocuniq649'>(Vers. 60.)</h2>

(Verse 60.) And he put it in his new tomb, which had been hewn out of the rock, and he rolled a great stone to the entrance of the tomb and went away. The new tomb is placed, so that after the resurrection, it would not be claimed that someone else had risen while the other bodies remained. However, it can also symbolize the new tomb of the Virgin Mary's womb: the stone placed at the entrance and the large stone showing that the tomb could not be opened without the help of many.


<h2 id='tocuniq650'>(Vers. 61 seqq.)</h2>

(Vers. 61 seqq.) Now there was there Mary Magdalene and another Mary, sitting opposite the tomb. And the next day that followed the day of preparation, the chief priests and Pharisees came together unto Pilate, saying, Sir, we remember that that deceiver said, while he was yet alive: After three days I will rise again. And while the others left the Lord, the women remained faithful, waiting for what Jesus had promised; and therefore they deserved to be the first to see Him risen, for whoever perseveres until the end will be saved (Matthew X, 22; XXIV, 13).


<h2 id='tocuniq651'>(Vers. 64 seqq.)</h2>

(Verse 64 onwards) Therefore, command that the tomb be guarded until the third day, lest his disciples come and steal him away and tell the people, 'He has risen from the dead,' and the last deception will be worse than the first.' Pilate said to them, 'You have a guard of soldiers. Go, make it as secure as you can.' So they went and made the tomb secure by sealing the stone and setting a guard. It was not enough for the chief priests and the Pharisees to crucify the Lord Savior, unless they also guard the tomb, receive a cohort, seal the stone, and put their hand against the one rising, so that their diligence might confirm our faith: for the more it is kept hidden, the more the power of the resurrection is shown. And he was buried in a new tomb, which had been hewn out of a rock, so that if it had been constructed from many stones, the foundations of the mound being dug up, it would be excavated by theft. But the testimony of the prophets is that he should be placed in a tomb, saying: He will dwell in a hewn cliff of a very strong rock (Isaiah 33:16). And immediately after two verses follows: you will see the king with glory (Ibid., 17).


<h2 id='tocuniq652'>(Chap. XXVIII.—Vers. 1.)</h2>

(Chapter XXVIII, Verse 1.) But on the evening of the Sabbath, when the first light of the Sabbath dawned, Mary Magdalene and the other Mary came to see the tomb. The fact that these women are described at different times in the Gospels is not a sign of falsehood, as the wicked claim, but rather a diligent act of visitation, as they frequently come and go, and do not allow the tomb of the Lord to be empty or far away for long.

<h2 id='tocuniq653'>(Vers. 2, 3.)</h2>

(Va. 2, 3.) And behold, there was a great earthquake. For the angel of the Lord descended from heaven, and coming, rolled back the stone, and sat upon it. And his appearance was like lightning, and his garment like snow. Our Lord, one and the same Son of God and Son of Man, according to both natures, divine and human, now demonstrates signs of his greatness, now of his humility. And even in the present place, although he is a man who was crucified, who was buried, who is enclosed in a tomb, whom a stone restrains, nevertheless the things that happen outside reveal the Son of God, the fleeing sun, the approaching darkness, the trembling earth, the torn veil, the split rocks, the raised dead, the ministry of angels, which from the beginning of his birth attest that he is God. Gabriel came to Mary, the angel spoke to Joseph; the same message was announced to the shepherds, afterwards a chorus of angels was heard saying: Glory to God in the highest, and on earth peace to people of good will (Luke 2)."  } He is tempted in solitude, and after the victory, immediately the angels serve Him. Now also the Angel comes, the guardian of the Lord's tomb, and in a white garment, He manifests the glory of the triumphant one. Moreover, as the Lord ascends to heaven, two angels are seen on the Mount of Olives, promising to the apostles according to the Savior's coming (Acts 1).

<h2 id='tocuniq654'>(Vers. 4, 5.)</h2>

(Vers. 4, 5.) But because of his fear, the guards were terrified and became like dead men. But the angel, answering, said to the women: Do not fear. For I know that you seek Jesus, who was crucified. He is not here, for he has risen as he said. The guards, terrified with fear, lie astounded like dead men, and yet the angel comforts not them, but the women. Do not fear, he says to them. Let them fear, he says, let the terror continue in those who continue in disbelief. Furthermore, because you seek Jesus crucified, hear that he has risen and fulfilled his promises.

<h2 id='tocuniq655'>(Vers. 6, 7.)</h2>

(Verse 6, 7.) Come and see the place where the Lord was placed. And quickly going, tell his disciples. So if you do not believe my words, believe in the empty tomb, and go quickly and tell his disciples.

Because he has risen, and behold, he goes before you into Galilee: there you shall see him: behold, I have told you. This is at the turning point of the nations, where there was previously error and a slippery path, and he did not leave a firm and stable footprint.

<h2 id='tocuniq656'>(Vers. 8.)</h2>

(Verse 8) And they quickly went out of the tomb with fear and great joy, running to announce to his disciples. The hearts of the women were filled with two emotions, fear and joy: one because of the magnitude of the miracle, the other out of the desire for his resurrection; and yet both stirred up their feminine courage. They went to the apostles, so that through them the seed of faith might be spread.

<h2 id='tocuniq657'>(Vers. 9.)</h2>

(V. 9.) And behold, Jesus met them, saying: Hail. Those who were seeking, those who were running thus, deserved to have the risen Lord meet them first and to hear, Hail, so that the curse of the woman Eve might be overturned in women.

But they came close and held his feet, and worshiped him. These women approached and held his feet because they worshiped him. However, she who was seeking the living among the dead and did not yet know that the Son of God had risen, rightly heard: Do not touch me, for I have not yet ascended to my Father (John 20:17).

<h2 id='tocuniq658'>(Vers. 10.)</h2>

(Verse 10.) Then Jesus said to them: Do not be afraid. And in the Old and New Testament, this must always be observed: that when a more splendid (or narrower) vision appears, fear is first driven away, so that, with the mind calmed, what is said can be heard.

Go, tell my brothers to go to Galilee, there they will see me. And when they had gone, behold, some of the guards came into the city and reported to the chief priests all that had happened. These are the brothers of whom he said elsewhere: I will declare your name to my brothers (Psalm 22:23): who do not see the Savior in Judea, but in the multitude of the nations.

<h2 id='tocuniq659'>(Vers. 12 seqq.)</h2>

(Vers. 12 seqq.) And gathering with the elders, having taken counsel, they gave a large sum of money to the soldiers, saying: Say that his disciples came by night and stole him away while we were sleeping. And if this comes to the governor's ears, we will persuade him and make you free from worry. So they took the money and did as they were instructed. And this story has been spread among the Jews to this day. The guards report the miracle: they return to the city excitedly and report to the chief priests what they have seen, what has happened. Those who were supposed to convert to repentance and seek the risen Jesus persist in wickedness and turn the money that had been given for the use of the temple into the redemption of falsehood, just as they had previously given thirty pieces of silver to the traitor Judas. Therefore, all those who misuse the offerings of the temple and the funds dedicated to the Church for their own desires are similar to the scribes and priests who bought falsehood and the blood of the Savior.


<h2 id='tocuniq660'>(Vers. 16, 17.)</h2>

(Verse 16, 17.) However, the eleven disciples went to Galilee, to the mountain where Jesus had appointed them. And when they saw him, they worshipped; but some doubted. After Jesus' resurrection, he is seen on the mountain in Galilee and is worshipped there; although some doubt, and their doubt increases our faith. Then he reveals himself more clearly to Thomas, showing him the wounded side with a spear, and the hands with nails.

<h2 id='tocuniq661'>(Vers. 18.)</h2>

(Verse 18.) And Jesus approached them, saying: All power is given to me in heaven and on earth. Power is given to those who were recently crucified, buried in a tomb, lay dead, and later resurrected. In heaven and on earth, power is given so that the one who previously reigned in heaven may now reign on earth through the faith of believers.

<h2 id='tocuniq662'>(Vers. 19.)</h2>

(Verse 19) Therefore, go and teach all nations, baptizing them in the name of the Father, and of the Son, and of the Holy Spirit. First, they teach all nations, then they immerse them in water. For it cannot happen that the body receives the sacrament of baptism unless the soul has first accepted the truth of faith. And they are baptized in the name of the Father, and of the Son, and of the Holy Spirit, so that there may be one divinity of those who give, one bestowal: and the name of the Trinity is one God.


<h2 id='tocuniq663'>(Vers. 20.)</h2>

(Verse 20) Teaching them to observe all things whatsoever I have commanded you. The principal order: He commanded the apostles that first they should teach all nations, then dip them in the sacrament of faith, and after faith and baptism, they should command what should be observed. And lest we think that what is commanded is light and few, he added: All things whatsoever I have commanded you. That whoever believes, who is baptized in the Trinity, should do all the things that are commanded.


And behold, I am with you all days, even to the consummation of the world. He who promises to be with his disciples until the consummation of the world, and shows that they will always be victorious, and that he will never depart from the believers. But he who promises his presence until the consummation of the world does not ignore the day on which he knows he will be with the apostles.
